关于作者

规划极限编程

Planning Extreme Programming

肯特·贝克
Kent Beck
马丁福勒
Martin Fowler
出版商：艾迪生卫斯理
Publisher: Addison Wesley
第一版 2000 年 10 月 12 日

ISBN：0-201-71091-9，160 页



购买印刷版



Buy Print Version

“XP 是当今我们领域中最重要的运动。我预测它将对当代人至关重要，就像 SEI 及其能力成熟度模型对上一代人一样重要。”

"XP is the most important movement in our field today. I predict that it will be as essential to the present generation as the S.E.I. and its Capability Maturity Model were to the last."

——摘自 Tom DeMarco 的前言

--From the foreword by Tom DeMarco

极限编程的标志——持续的集成和自动化测试、结合持续的客户反馈的频繁的小版本发布，以及团队合作的方法——使其成为一种异常灵活和有效的软件开发方法。曾经被认为是激进的极限编程 (XP) 正迅速被公认为一种特别适合面临模糊或快速变化需求的小型团队的方法——即当今快节奏软件开发世界中的大多数项目。

The hallmarks of Extreme Programming--constant integration and automated testing, frequent small releases that incorporate continual customer feedback, and a teamwork approach--make it an exceptionally flexible and effective approach to software development. Once considered radical, Extreme Programming (XP) is rapidly becoming recognized as an approach particularly well-suited to small teams facing vague or rapidly changing requirements--that is, the majority of projects in todays fast-paced software development world.

在这种灵活性和快速变化的背景下，规划至关重要；没有它，软件项目很快就会分崩离析。由公认的 XP 权威 Kent Beck 和 Martin Fowler 撰写，Planning Extreme Programming 介绍了规划和跟踪成功的极限编程项目所需的方法、方法和建议。关键 XP 哲学：规划不是一次性事件，而是贯穿项目生命周期的不断重新评估和过程修正的过程。

Within this context of flexibility and rapid-fire changes, planning is critical; without it, software projects can quickly fall apart. Written by acknowledged XP authorities Kent Beck and Martin Fowler, Planning Extreme Programming presents the approaches, methods, and advice you need to plan and track a successful Extreme Programming project. The key XP philosophy: Planning is not a one-time event, but a constant process of reevaluation and course-correction throughout the lifecycle of the project.

您将了解规划对于控制工作量、减轻程序员压力、提高生产力和保持项目正常进行的重要性。规划极限编程还侧重于估算每个用户故事（需求）的成本和时间、确定其优先级并相应地规划软件发布的重要性。

You will learn how planning is essential to controlling workload, reducing programmer stress, increasing productivity, and keeping projects on track. Planning Extreme Programming also focuses on the importance of estimating the cost and time for each user story (requirement), determining its priority, and planning software releases accordingly.

具体主题包括：

Specific topics include:

  • 计划和四个关键变量：成本、质量、时间和范围

  • Planning and the four key variables: cost, quality, time, and scope

  • 决定将多少特性合并到一个版本中

  • Deciding how many features to incorporate into a release

  • 估算用户故事的范围、时间和工作量

  • Estimating scope, time, and effort for user stories

  • 优先考虑用户故事

  • Prioritizing user stories

  • 平衡用户故事的商业价值和技术风险

  • Balancing the business value and technical risk of user stories

  • 根据客户和程序员的输入重建发布计划

  • Rebuilding the release plan based on customer and programmer input

  • 选择迭代长度

  • Choosing the iteration length

  • 跟踪迭代

  • Tracking an iteration

  • 当你不打算约会时该怎么办

  • What to do when youre not going to make the date

  • 处理错误

  • Dealing with bugs

  • 对团队进行更改

  • Making changes to the team

  • 外包

  • Outsourcing

  • 处理商业合同

  • Working with business contracts

此外，本书还会提醒您注意预示严重问题的危险信号：不会做出决定的客户、不断增长的缺陷报告、每日构建失败等等。整整一章都专门讲述战壕中的战争故事，这些故事说明了许多程序员在现实世界中遇到的问题以及他们设计的解决方案。

In addition, this book alerts you to the red flags that signal serious problems: customers who will not make decisions, growing defect reports, failing daily builds, and more. An entire chapter is devoted to war stories from the trenches that illustrate the real-world problems many programmers encounter and the solutions theyve devised.

To our Cindies...

前言

Foreword

在On War中，Carl von Clausewitz 告诉我们，军事史就像一个钟摆，在装甲和机动性的相对优势之间来回摆动。身穿闪亮盔甲的骑士能够统治没有它们的骑士，但他们无法与成吉思汗和他的蒙古人横扫平原的敏捷、几乎赤身裸体的小马战士相提并论。一旦有了坦克，轻骑兵本身就注定要失败，而坦克也敌不过拥有萨格导弹的快脚巴勒斯坦少年。有了马奇诺防线，法国人赌钟摆会再次转向装甲，但事实并非如此，德国人只是绕开了它。

In On War, Carl von Clausewitz tells us that military history is a pendulum swinging back and forth between the relative advantages of armor and of mobility. The knights in shining armor were able to dominate any knight without, but they were no match for the quick, nearly naked pony warriors that swept across the plains with Genghis Kahn and his Mongols. Light cavalry itself was doomed as soon as there were tanks, and tanks were no match for fleet-footed Palestinian teenagers with Sagger missiles. With the Maginot Line, the French were gambling that the pendulum had swung again toward armor, but it hadn't, and the Germans simply went around it.

在 IT 领域，我们刚刚走出装甲（流程）为王的时代。现在我们正在进入一个只有移动性才重要的时代。以正确的方式构建产品听起来仍然是一个值得称赞的目标，但让我们面对现实吧，如今真正重要的是快速构建产品。因为我们在我们的领域中痴迷于过程，所以我们倾向于像我们对 1980 年代和 90 年代强加给我们的命令做出反应一样对这一新命令做出反应。我们问过，“我们应该在我们的流程中添加什么来应对这种新情况？” 这个问题的答案不会是正确的，因为这个问题本身就是错误的。

In the field of IT, we are just emerging from a time in which armor (process) has been king. And now we are moving into a time when only mobility matters. Building a product the right way still sounds like a laudable goal, butlet's face itwhat really matters today is building it fast. Because we are process-obsessed in our field, we have tended to react to this new imperative as we reacted to the imperatives thrust upon us in the 1980s and 1990s. We have asked, "What shall we add to our process to deal with this new situation?" No answer to that question is going to be right because the question itself is wrong.

新的机动性要求是我们从过程中减去：我们需要得到光。

What the new mobility imperative requires is that we subtract from process: We need to get light.

“轻装上阵”不仅仅意味着放弃繁重的流程和随之而来的堆积如山的文档。这意味着对人员进行投资，这样他们就可以在没有正式流程且不会产生大量纸张的情况下快速有效地工作。没有人比 Kent Beck 和 Martin Fowler 更清楚如何做到这一点。

"Getting light" means more than just abandoning heavy process and its attendant mountain of documentation. It means investing in people so they can work quickly and effectively without formal process and without generating a ton of paper. No one has a better vision of how this is done than Kent Beck and Martin Fowler.

他们发起的 XP 运动是一种使 IT 项目变得轻便快捷的方法。XP 的原则不仅仅是另一种方法论、另一种过程。它们是过程的对立面。它们是使过程无关紧要的手段。

The XP movement they have founded is a way to make IT projects light and quick. The principles of XP are not just another methodology, another process. They are the antithesis of process. They are means to make process irrelevant.

由于 XP 项目完全不同，按理说管理它们也不同。Planning Extreme Programming侧重于如何以最佳方式领导 XP 开发人员组成的团队。Beck 和 Fowler 的药方常常是苦涩的，有时是明智的，而且几乎总能击中目标。

Because XP projects are completely different, it stands to reason that managing them is different too. Planning Extreme Programming focuses on how a team of XP-empowered developers is optimally led. Beck and Fowler's prescriptions are often wry, sometimes wise, and almost always bang on target.

XP 是当今我们领域中最重要的运动。我预测它对当代人的重要性就像 SEI 及其能力成熟度模型对上一代人的重要性一样。

XP is the most important movement in our field today. I predict that it will be as essential to the present generation as the SEI and its Capability Maturity Model were to the last.

汤姆·德马科

Tom DeMarco

缅因州卡姆登

Camden, Maine

前言

Preface

这是一本关于规划软件项目的书。我们主要是为项目经理编写它——那些必须计划和跟踪计划与现实的对应关系的人。我们还为程序员和客户编写它，他们在规划和开发软件方面发挥着至关重要的作用。

This is a book about planning software projects. We are writing it mostly for project managersthose who have to plan and track the correspondence of the planning with reality. We also are writing it for programmers and customers, who have a vital role to play in planning and developing software.

规划不是预测未来。当您制定开发软件的计划时，开发不会像那样进行。永远不会。如果这样做，您的客户甚至不会高兴，因为当软件到达那里时，客户不想要计划的东西；他们想要不同的东西。

Planning is not about predicting the future. When you make a plan for developing a piece of software, development is not going to go like that. Not ever. Your customers wouldn't even be happy if it did, because by the time the software gets there, the customers don't want what was planned; they want something different.

像许多人一样，我们喜欢艾森豪威尔的名言：“在准备战斗时，我总是发现计划是无用的，但计划是必不可少的。” [1] 这就是为什么这不是一本关于计划的书；这是关于计划。规划是如此宝贵和重要，如此重要，只要发展持续，它就值得每天进行一点。

Like so many, we enjoy Eisenhower's quotation: "In preparing for battle I have always found that plans are useless, but planning is indispensable."[1] That's why this isn't a book about plans; it's about planning. And planning is so valuable and important, so vital, that it deserves to go on a little every day, as long as development lasts.

[1] 理查德尼克松，六次危机（纽约：试金石出版社，1990 年）。

[1] Richard Nixon, Six Crises (New York: Touchstone Press, 1990).

如果你遵循本书中的建议，你每天都会有一个新问题需要解决——计划——但我们不会为此道歉，因为没有计划，软件开发不可避免地会偏离轨道。

If you follow the advice in this book, you are going to have a new problem to solve every dayplanningbut we won't apologize for that, because without planning, software development inevitably goes off the rails.

本书的范围有意缩小。它涵盖了如何规划和跟踪 XP 项目的软件开发。它基于我们作为顾问和教练的经验，以及越来越多使用 XP 的早期采用者的经验。

The scope of this book is deliberately narrow. It covers how to plan and track software development for XP projects. It's based on our experience as consultants and coaches, together with the experience of the growing band of early adopters who are using XP.

因此，这不是一本关于整个项目管理的书。我们不涵盖典型的项目经理工作，例如人员评估、招聘和预算编制。我们不会解决有成群的开发人员的大型项目的问题，我们也不会谈论在其他软件过程的上下文中进行规划，或规划其他活动。我们认为这里有每个人都可以使用的原则和技术，但我们一直坚持我们所知道的流程部分——让团队中的每个人都指向一个方向，发现何时不再如此，并恢复和谐。

As a result this isn't a book about the whole of project management. We don't cover typical project manager jobs such as personnel evaluation, recruiting, and budgeting. We don't address the issues of large projects with hordes of developers, nor do we say anything about planning in the context of other software processes, or of planning other activities. We think there are principles and techniques here that everyone can use, but we have stuck to the parts of the process we knowgetting everybody on the team pointed in one direction, discovering when this is no longer true, and restoring harmony.

XP（极限编程）是一个实践系统（如果你愿意，你可以使用m词；我们宁愿不用，谢谢）软件开发人员社区正在发展以解决快速交付高质量软件的问题，然后对其进行改进以满足不断变化的业务需求。

XP (Extreme Programming) is a system of practices (you can use the m-word if you want to; we'd rather not, thank you) that a community of software developers is evolving to address the problems of quickly delivering quality software, and then evolving it to meet changing business needs.

XP 不仅仅是计划。它涵盖了小型团队软件开发的所有方面——设计、测试、实施、部署和维护。然而，规划是 XP 难题的关键部分。（有关 XP 的概述，请阅读Extreme Programming Explained: Embrace Change。阅读时，也可以购买我们所有其他书籍的副本。）

XP isn't just about planning. It covers all aspects of small team software developmentdesign, testing, implementation, deployment, and maintenance. However, planning is a key piece of the XP puzzle. (For an overview of XP, read Extreme Programming Explained: Embrace Change. While you're at it, buy copies of all of the rest of our books, too.)

XP 通过将长期项目分解为一系列独立的、为期一到三周的小型项目来处理它们。在每次迭代期间

XP addresses long projects by breaking them into a sequence of self-contained, one- to three-week mini-projects. During each iteration

  • 客户选择要添加的功能。

  • Customers pick the features to be added.

  • 程序员添加功能，以便它们完全准备好部署。

  • Programmers add the features so they are completely ready to be deployed.

  • 程序员和客户编写和维护自动化测试以证明这些功能的存在。

  • Programmers and customers write and maintain automated tests to demonstrate the presence of these features.

  • 程序员改进系统的设计以优雅地支持系统中的所有功能。

  • Programmers evolve the design of the system to gracefully support all the features in the system.

如果没有周密的计划，这个过程就会分崩离析。

Without careful planning, the process falls apart.

  • 团队必须选择最好的功能来实现。

  • The team must choose the best possible features to implement.

  • 团队必须尽可能积极地应对不可避免的挫折。

  • The team must react as positively as possible to the inevitable setbacks.

  • 团队成员不能过度投入，否则他们会放慢速度。

  • Team members must not overcommit, or they will slow down.

  • 团队不能承诺不足，否则客户不会物有所值。

  • The team must not undercommit, or customers won't get value for their money.

  • 团队成员必须弄清楚自己的位置并准确报告，以便每个人都可以相应地调整计划

  • Team members must figure out clearly where they are and report this accurately, so that everyone can adjust their plans accordingly

每日计划者的工作是帮助团队在所有这些领域保持正轨。

The job of the daily planner is to help keep the team on track in all these areas.

我们根据需要提出项目规划想法。作为顾问，我们通常是在项目大多已​​死时才被介绍给他们的。这些项目通常不做任何计划，或者他们淹没在错误类型的过多计划中。

We come by our project planning ideas by necessity. As consultants, we are usually introduced to projects when they are mostly dead. The projects typically aren't doing any planning, or they are drowning in too much planning of the wrong sort.

由此产生的想法是我们能想到的可能可行的最简单的规划想法。但最重要的是，记住世界上所有的规划技术，包括这些，如果您忘记了软件是由人类构建的，就无法拯救您。最后，让人们保持专注、快乐和积极，他们就会实现目标。

The resulting ideas are the simplest planning ideas we could think of that could possibly work. But above all, remember all the planning techniques in the world, including these, can't save you if you forget that software is built by human beings. In the end keep the human beings focused, happy, and motiviated and they will deliver.

肯特贝克，梅林，俄勒冈

Kent Beck, Merlin, Oregon

Martin Fowler，马萨诸塞州梅尔罗斯http://www.martinfowler.com

Martin Fowler, Melrose, Massachusetts http://www.martinfowler.com

2000 年 7 月

July 2000

>我有一个狡猾的计划。

——鲍德里克，黑爵士

>I have a cunning plan.

Baldrick, Blackadder

第 1 章 为什么要计划？

Chapter 1. Why Plan?

老鼠和人的最佳计划

帮派欢呼。

——罗伯特·伯恩斯，《致老鼠》

The best-laid schemes o' mice an' men

Gang aft a gley.

Robert Burns, "To a Mouse"

我们计划确保我们始终在做最重要的事情，与其他人有效协调，并对突发事件做出快速反应。

We plan to ensure that we are always doing the most important thing left to do, to coordinate effectively with other people, and to respond quickly to unexpected events.

肯特大约十岁时，他第一次在爱达荷州狭长地带飞蝇钓。在追捕溪鳟鱼一事无成、汗流浃背的一天之后，他和他的朋友们回家了。在茂密的树林中跌跌撞撞地走了半个小时后，他们意识到自己迷路了。肯特开始恐慌——呼吸急促、视野狭窄、发冷。然后有人提出了一个计划——他们会步行上坡，直到他们找到一条他们知道在上面的伐木路。瞬间，恐慌消失了。

When Kent was about ten, he went fly-fishing for the first time in the Idaho panhandle. After a fruitless, sweaty day in pursuit of brook trout, he and his friends headed for home. After half an hour of stumbling through dense trees, they realized they were lost. Kent started to panicfast breathing, tunnel vision, chills. Then someone suggested a planthey would walk uphill until they hit a logging road they knew was up there. Instantly, the panic disappeared.

肯特当时对制定计划的重要性感到震惊。没有计划，他会做一些愚蠢的事情，或者只是变得紧张。有了计划，他又平静了下来。

Kent was struck at the time by the importance of having a plan. Without the plan, he was going to do something stupid, or just go catatonic. With the plan he was calm again.

软件开发计划的工作方式相同。如果你知道你有一个紧迫的截止日期，但你制定了一个计划并且计划说你可以在截止日期前完成，那么你将带着紧迫感开始你的第一个任务，但仍然尽可能地工作。毕竟，你有足够的时间。这正是最有可能导致计划实现的行为。恐慌会导致疲劳、缺陷和沟通中断。

Plans in software development work the same way. If you know you have a tight deadline, but you make a plan and the plan says you can make the deadline, then you'll start on your first task with a sense of urgency but still working as well as possible. After all, you have enough time. This is exactly the behavior that is most likely to cause the plan to come true. Panic leads to fatigue, defects, and communication breakdowns.

但我们也看到计划导致麻烦。它们可能会浪费大量时间，拖延那些宁愿做一些有成效的事情的人的日子。计划可以作为打人的棍子，最糟糕的是，它们可以隐藏问题，直到为时已晚。

But we've also seen plans lead to trouble. They can be a huge time sink, dragging days out of people who'd rather be doing something productive. Plans can be used as a stick to beat people with, and worst of all, they can conceal trouble until it's too late to deal with it.

为什么我们应该计划

Why We Should Plan

我们不计划，所以我们可以预测未来。业务和软件变化太快，无法进行预测。即使可以预测三年后我们需要什么，也不一定有帮助，因为从现在到那时我们需要很多不同的东西。

We don't plan so we can predict the future. Business and software are changing too rapidly for prediction to be possible. Even if it were possible to predict what we needed in three years, it wouldn't necessarily help because between now and then we need so many different things.

你应该做某事越明显，问为什么就越重要。在处理一个严肃的软件开发项目时，您必须做一些计划。因此，在开始计划项目之前，您必须了解为什么需要执行该项目。如果不了解您为什么需要该项目，您将如何判断您是否成功了？

The more obvious it is that you should do something, the more important it is to ask why. You must do some planning when tackling a serious software development project. Therefore, before you start planning a project, you have to understand why you need to carry out the project. Without understanding why you need the project, how will you be able to tell if you have succeeded?

我们计划因为

We plan because

  • 我们需要确保我们始终致力于我们需要做的最重要的事情。

  • We need to ensure that we are always working on the most important thing we need to do.

  • 我们需要与其他人协调。

  • We need to coordinate with other people.

  • 当意外事件发生时，我们需要了解前两个事件的后果。

  • When unexpected events occur we need to understand the consequences for the first two.

首先是计划的明显原因。没有什么比在系统的一部分上努力工作却发现它并不重要并且在系统的下一个版本中被废弃更令人沮丧的了。花在做一件事上的时间就是没有花在做其他事情上的时间，如果其他事情很重要，那么我们可能会失败。

The first is the obvious reason for planning. There's nothing more frustrating than working hard on a part of the system only to find that it doesn't really matter and gets scrapped in the next release of the system. Time spent doing one thing is time not spent doing something else, and if that something else is important then we may fail.

假设现在是两点，我们在波士顿。我们想开车去阿卡迪亚，但我们也想去理发，去弗里波特买露营装备。上次我们开车去阿卡迪亚花了五个小时，没有停下来。所以我们看到了一些选择。如果我们直奔阿卡迪亚，我们可以在七点前到达那里。如果我们想在途中停下来吃晚饭，比如一个小时，我们将在八点前到达。要理发，我们还需要一个小时，那就是九点。访问自由港将增加一个小时。我们看看什么对我们最重要。如果我们想要吃饱，装备好，还不算太晚，而且我们可以不那么在意自己的外表，我们可能会决定放弃理发。计划可以帮助我们看到我们的选择。

Say it's two o'clock and we're in Boston. We want to drive up to Acadia, but we'd also like to get haircuts and hit Freeport for camping gear. Last time we drove up to Acadia it took us five hours with no stops. So we see some options. If we shoot straight up to Acadia we can be there by seven o'clock. If we want to stop for dinner on the way, say an hour, we will be there by eight. To get haircuts we'd need another hour, so that would be nine. Visiting Freeport would add another hour. We look at what's most important to us. If we want to be fed, equipped, not too late, and we could care less about our appearance, we might decide to drop the haircut. A plan helps us see our options.

协调是其他人都希望我们计划的原因。我们接到妻子的电话，约我们在巴尔港共进晚餐。因为现在是两点钟，我们知道如果我们直接开车，在自由港停留，八点左右到达那里，我们就可以见到他们。软件充满了这样的协调：营销公告、财务周期或管理承诺。计划让我们了解什么是合理的。

Coordination is why everyone else wants us to plan. We get a call from our wives to meet for dinner in Bar Harbor. Since it's two o'clock we know we can meet them if we drive right up, stop in Freeport, and be there around eight. Software is full of such coordination: marketing announcements, financial periods, or management promises. Planning allows us to get an idea of what is reasonable.

但计划的好坏取决于计划所依据的估计，而估计总是排在实际之后。如果我们遇到可怕的交通堵塞，世界上所有的计划都无法帮助我们完成那个晚餐约会。正如伯恩斯先生在本章开头引述的那样，现实世界有破坏计划的可怕习惯。

But planning is only as good as the estimates that the plans are based on, and estimates always come second to actuals. If we hit a horrible traffic jam, all the planning in the world can't help us make that dinner date. The real world has this horrible habit of destroying plans, as Mr. Burns noted in this chapter's opening quote.

当现实世界闯入时，计划仍然有帮助，因为它使我们能够考虑意外事件的影响。我们两点钟出发，遇到交通不便，直到五点钟才到达波特兰。我们知道我们通常在一个半小时后到达那里，所以我们的经验（和计划）告诉我们打电话给我们的朋友把晚餐时间推迟到八点半，然后放弃对自由港的访问。计划让我们既可以调整我们所做的事情，也可以与他人协调。关键是一旦知道了事件的影响，就要及时调整计划。我们的妻子宁愿知道我们在五点钟而不是八点钟知道我们的延迟，而且在自由港度过时间真的很烦人，后来才意识到我们真的搞砸了与我们的 Cindies 的晚餐。（我们甚至不想考虑这样做的后果；相比之下，

Planning still helps when the real world intrudes because it allows us to consider the effects of the unexpected event. Leaving at two o'clock, we hit bad traffic and don't get to Portland until five. We know we usually get there after an hour and a half, so our experience (and plan) tells us to call our friends to put dinner back to half past eight and drop the visit to Freeport. Planning allows us both to adjust what we do and to coordinate with others. The key is to adjust the plan as soon as we know the effect of the event. Our wives would much rather know about our delay at five than at eight, and it would be really annoying to spend time in Freeport and only later realize that we've really screwed up dinner with our Cindies. (We don't even want to contemplate the consequences of that; in comparison, software failures are minor events.)

我们在规划中需要什么

What We Need in Planning

规划是人们在不同规模上所做的事情。您可以计划一天的活动。该团队计划了几周的任务。发展和业务制定了明年的计划。高级管理人员为大型组织制定计划。如果您从波士顿开车到阿卡迪亚，您不会计划道路上的每一个弯道，但您会想要弄清楚走哪条路以及何时从一条路换到另一条路。您不会期望准时到达，但我们知道迟到是有一定限度的，需要打个道歉电话。

Planning is something that people do at various scales. You might plan your day's activities. The team plans out its tasks for a couple of weeks. Development and business lay out a plan for the next year. Senior managers develop plans for a large organization. If you are driving from Boston to Acadia, you won't plan every curve in the road, but you will want to figure out which roads to take and when to change from one to another. You're not going to expect to arrive to the minute, but we know there is some limit of lateness that requires the apologetic phone call.

为了进行协调，准确了解您在计划中的进展情况至关重要。在公路旅行中，这是相当简单的。您可以测量里程，考虑道路的性质，并制定一个粗略的时间表，其中包含沿途的重要点。如果您很晚才到达波特兰，您可以很容易地分辨并估计到达巴尔港的延迟时间。软件的虚拟性质再次与该属性相违背。由于存在所有自由度，因此很难确定您是完成了 70% 还是完成了 30%。这就像公路旅行，您不知道自己走了 30 英里还是 300 英里。没有任何参照系，你会感到不舒服。如果你的晚餐约会对象不知道你们有多亲密，而且已经很晚了，

In order to carry out the coordination it's vital to have an accurate picture of how far you are along in the plan. On a road trip this is fairly straightforward. You can measure mileage, take into account the nature of the roads, and come up with a rough schedule with significant points along the way. If you are very late arriving at Portland, you can easily tell, and thus estimate, the delay in reaching Bar Harbor. Software's virtual nature again conspires against this property. With all the degrees of freedom it can be very difficult to find out whether you are 70 percent done or 30 percent done. It's like taking a road trip where you don't know whether you've gone 30 miles or 300 miles. Without any frame of reference you feel uncomfortable. If your dinner date doesn't know how close you are and it's getting late, she is uncomfortable, too.

任何软件规划技术都必须尝试创建可见性，以便参与项目的每个人都能真正看到项目的进展情况。这意味着您需要明确的里程碑，不可捏造的里程碑，并清楚地代表进展。里程碑还必须是参与项目的每个人（包括客户）都能理解并学会信任的事情。

Any software planning technique must try to create visibility, so everyone involved in the project can really see how far along a project is. This means that you need clear milestones, ones that cannot be fudged, and clearly represent progress. Milestones must also be things that everyone involved in the project, including the customer, can understand and learn to trust.

计划是关于弄清楚事件的可能进程和不可避免的变化的后果。我们需要不同规模的不同计划。然而，计划还必须既易于构建又易于保持最新。庞大而复杂的计划无济于事，因为它们的构建和维护成本太高。由于计划涉及协调，因此每个受计划影响的人都必须能够理解它们——这是简单的另一个原因。

Plans are about figuring out a likely course of events and the consequences of the inevitable changes. We need different plans at different scales. Yet plans must also be both simple to build and simple to keep up-to-date. Large and complex plans are not helpful because they cost too much to build and maintain. Since plans involve coordination, they must be comprehensible to everyone who is affected by the plananother reason for simplicity.

计划必须是诚实的，包括你目前掌握的所有信息。计划应该使任何人都很难被与现实无关的进展报告所愚弄。

Plans must be honest, including all the information you have to date. Plans should make it difficult for anyone to be fooled by reports of progress unrelated to reality.

计划陷阱

The Planning Trap

正是前一段暗示了为什么计划可能是一个陷阱。这是因为人们计划的另一个原因是：证明他们可以控制事件

It's the preceding paragraph that gives us a hint as to why planning can be a trap. This is because there is another reason why people plan: to demonstrate they are in control of events

但是控制事件是矛盾的：你无法控制事件；你无法控制事件。你只能控制你的反应。即使这样，您的控制量也是有限的。事件改变计划。一旦遇到交通堵塞，晚餐或自由港都会受到影响。你不能继续执行计划并假装一切都好。那将是愚蠢的。

But controlling events is an oxymoron: You can't control events; you can only control your reactions. Even then the amount of control you have is limited. Events change plans. Once you hit that traffic jam, either dinner or Freeport is affected. You can't just carry on with the plan and pretend everything is okay. That would be stupid.

然而，我们已经多次看到这种情况发生。如果事情没有按计划进行，那么计划者恐怕会受到指责。这种恐惧促使计划者说计划仍在进行中。计划者可能会承认计划偏离了轨道，但如果计划足够复杂，计划者甚至可以隐藏这一点。没有什么比告诉外界一切仍在按计划进行更重要的了。

Yet we've seen this happen plenty of times. If things don't go according to plan, then the planner is afraid he will be blamed. That fear induces the planner to say that the plan is still on track. The planner might admit to himself that the plan is off track, but if the plan is complicated enough the planner can even hide that. Nothing is more important than to say to the outside world that everything is still going according to plan.

计划偏离现实，变成幻想。更糟糕的是，计划者花费精力试图维持这种错觉。开发人员逐渐失去动力。如果计划是幻觉，为什么要努力去遵循它？

The plan is diverging from reality, turning into an illusion. Worse, the planner spends energy trying to maintain the illusion. Developers gradually lose motivation. If the plan's an illusion, why try to follow it?

也许该项目最终会自行解决。偶尔会这样。也许其他人有更糟糕的问题。更常见的是，幻觉与现实之间的差距越来越大，直到幻觉不可持续。事情变得丑陋。客户很生气，因为她根据幻想制定了自己的计划，做出了无法兑现的承诺。程序员们很生气，因为他们努力工作，尽了最大努力，但现在他们却因为不做不可能的事情而被大声疾呼，让幻想成为现实。

Perhaps the project will sort itself out in the end. Occasionally it does. Perhaps someone else has even worse problems. More often the gap between illusion and reality grows until the illusion is unsustainable. Things get ugly. The customer is angry because she has made her own plans based on the illusion, made promises that she can't keep. The programmers are angry because they've worked hard, done their best, but now they are being shouted at for not doing the impossible and making the illusion real.

事件发生。计划改变。如果事情似乎完全按照计划进行，那通常是麻烦的征兆。项目可能发生的最糟糕的事情是计划与现实之间的差异。所以不要掉进那个陷阱。保持你的计划诚实，并期望他们总是改变。

Events happen. Plans change. If things seems to be going exactly according to plan, that's usually a sign of trouble. The worst thing that can happen to a project is the divergence between the plan and reality. So don't fall into that trap. Keep your plans honest, and expect them to always change.

第 2 章恐惧

Chapter 2. Fear

勇气！是什么让奴隶成为国王？

勇气！是什么让桅杆上的旗帜飘扬？

勇气！是什么让大象在迷雾中或在昏暗的黄昏中咬牙切齿？

是什么让麝香鼠保护他的麝香？

勇气！是什么让狮身人面像成为第七大奇迹？

勇气！是什么让黎明如雷贯耳？

勇气！是什么让霍屯督人如此火爆？

是什么把“猿”放在杏里？

他们有什么我没有的？

——胆小的狮子，绿野仙踪

Courage! What makes a King out of a slave?

Courage!What makes the flag on the mast to wave?

Courage!What makes the elephant charge his tusk, in the misty mist or the dusky dusk?

What makes the muskrat guard his musk?

Courage! What makes the sphinx the seventh wonder?

Courage!What makes the dawn come up like thunder?

Courage!What makes the Hottentot so hot?

What puts the "ape" in apricot?

What have they got that I ain't got?

Cowardly Lion, The Wizard of OZ

软件开发是有风险的。相关人员对可能出现的问题有很多恐惧。为了有效地发展，我们必须承认这些恐惧。

Software development is risky. People involved have many fears of what may go wrong. To develop effectively we must acknowledge these fears.

为什么我们需要软件过程？出于与我们需要法律、政府和税收相同的原因：恐惧。

Why do we need a software process? For the same reason that we need laws, governments, and taxes: fear.

独立宣言说：

The Declaration of Independence says:

这些[权利]包括生命、自由和追求幸福。为了确保这些权利，政府在人们中间建立起来，从被统治者的同意中获得他们的正当权力。

That among these [rights] are life, liberty, and the pursuit of happiness. That to secure these rights, governments are instituted among men, deriving their just powers from the consent of the governed.

尽管这些词的深奥可能会分散我们的注意力，但请考虑安全这个词。我们建立政府是因为我们害怕失去我们的权利。

Though the profundity of these words may distract us, consider the word secure. We institute governments because we are afraid of losing our rights.

出于同样的原因，我们制定软件流程是因为我们害怕。客户害怕

By the same token, we institute software processes because we are afraid. Customers are afraid that

  • 他们不会得到他们所要求的。

  • They won't get what they asked for.

  • 他们会要求错误的东西。

  • They'll ask for the wrong thing.

  • 他们会为太少付出太多。

  • They'll pay too much for too little.

  • 他们必须将对自己职业生涯的控制权交给不在乎的技术人员。

  • They must surrender control of their career to techies who don't care.

  • 他们永远不会看到有意义的计划。

  • They won't ever see a meaningful plan.

  • 他们看到的计划将是童话故事。

  • The plans they do see will be fairy tales.

  • 他们不会知道发生了什么。

  • They won't know what's going on.

  • 他们将坚持自己的第一个决定，无法对业务变化做出反应。

  • They'll be held to their first decisions and won't be able to react to changes in the business.

  • 没有人会告诉他们真相。

  • No one will tell them the truth.

开发商也很害怕。他们担心

Developers are afraid, too. They fear that

  • 他们会被告知要做比他们知道的更多的事情。

  • They will be told to do more than they know how to do.

  • 他们会被告知做一些没有意义的事情。

  • They will be told to do things that don't make sense.

  • 他们太蠢了。

  • They are too stupid.

  • 他们在技术上落后了。

  • They are falling behind technically.

  • 他们将在没有权力的情况下被赋予责任。

  • They will be given responsibility without authority.

  • 他们不会得到需要做什么的明确定义。

  • They won't be given clear definitions of what needs to be done.

  • 他们将不得不为截止日期牺牲质量。

  • They'll have to sacrifice quality for deadlines.

  • 他们将不得不在没有帮助的情况下解决难题。

  • They'll have to solve hard problems without help.

  • 他们将没有足够的时间来取得成功。

  • They won't have enough time to succeed.

未被承认的恐惧是所有软件项目失败的根源

Unacknowledged Fear Is the Source of All Software Project Failures

如果这些担忧没有摆在桌面上并得到解决，那么开发商和客户都会试图通过筑墙来保护自己。他们拒绝分享关键信息：

If these fears are not put on the table and dealt with, then developers and customer each try to protect themselves by building walls. They refuse to share critical information:

“如果我把这件事告诉工程师，他们会花几个月的时间试图弄明白，而不是按照我的要求去做。”

“如果我告诉客户我完成这件事的速度有多快，他就会期望我做任何事情都那么快。”

"If I tell the engineers about this, they'll spend months trying to figure it out instead of doing what I need."

"If I tell the customer how quickly I got this done, he'll expect me to do everything that fast."

他们夸大其词、半真半假、撒谎、掩盖事实并背道而驰。他们建立了庞大的、无用的政治和程序结构，旨在保护而不是成功。

They exaggerate, tell half-truths, lie, cover up, and work at cross-purposes. They build huge, useless political and procedural structures aimed at protection instead of success.

为了取得成功，必须在客户和开发商之间建立一个开发流程，以确保某些不可剥夺的权利。

In order to be successful, a development process must be instituted among customers and developers that secures certain inalienable rights.

客户权利法案

Customer Bill of Rights

  • 您有权制定总体计划，了解可以在何时以何种成本完成哪些工作。

  • You have the right to an overall plan, to know what can be accomplished when and at what cost.

  • 您有权从每个编程周中获得最大可能的价值。

  • You have the right to get the most possible value out of every programming week.

  • 您有权查看正在运行的系统的进展情况，通过您指定的可重复测试证明它可以正常工作。

  • You have the right to see progress in a running system, proven to work by passing repeatable tests that you specify.

  • 您有权改变主意、替换功能和更改优先级，而无需支付高昂的费用。

  • You have the right to change your mind, to substitute functionality, and to change priorities without paying exorbitant costs.

  • 您有权获知日程变更，及时选择如何缩小范围恢复原日期。您可以随时取消并留下一个有用的工作系统来反映迄今为止的投资。

  • You have the right to be informed of schedule changes, in time to choose how to reduce the scope to restore the original date. You can cancel at any time and be left with a useful working system reflecting investment to date.

程序员权利法案

Programmer Bill of Rights

  • 您有权知道需要什么，并明确声明优先级。

  • You have the right to know what is needed, with clear declarations of priority.

  • 您有权随时制作高质量的作品。

  • You have the right to produce quality work at all times.

  • 您有权向同事、经理和客户寻求和接受帮助。

  • You have the right to ask for and receive help from peers, managers, and customers.

  • 您有权做出和更新您自己的估计。

  • You have the right to make and update your own estimates.

  • 您有权接受您的责任，而不是将其分配给您。

  • You have the right to accept your responsibilities instead of having them assigned to you.

如果我们要发展得好，我们必须创造一种文化，使程序员和客户能够承认他们的恐惧并接受他们的权利和责任。没有这样的保证，我们就无法勇敢。我们恐惧地蜷缩在堡垒墙后，将它们建造得越来越坚固，为我们采用的发展过程增加了越来越多的分量。我们不断添加炮弹和城垛、文件和审查、程序和签字、有鳄鱼的护城河、刑讯室和大锅沸腾的油。

If we are going to develop well, we must create a culture that makes it possible for programmers and customers to acknowledge their fears and accept their rights and responsibilities. Without such guarantees, we cannot be courageous. We huddle in fear behind fortress walls, building them ever stronger, adding ever more weight to the development processes we have adopted. We continually add cannonades and battlements, documents and reviews, procedures and sign-offs, moats with crocodiles, torture chambers, and huge pots of boiling oil.

但是当我们的恐惧被承认并且我们的权利被接受时，我们就会变得勇敢。我们可以设定难以实现的目标并合作实现这些目标。我们可以拆除我们因恐惧而建造并阻碍我们的结构。我们将有勇气只做必要的事情，不再做更多的事情，把时间花在重要的事情上，而不是花在保护自己上。

But when our fears are acknowledged and our rights are accepted, then we can be courageous. We can set goals that are hard to reach and collaborate to make those goals. We can tear down the structures that we built out of fear and that impede us. We will have the courage to do only what is necessary and no more, to spend our time on what's important rather than on protecting ourselves.

第 3 章驱动软件

Chapter 3. Driving Software

我当然是个出色的车手。

——雷蒙德，雨人

Of course I'm an excellent driver.

Raymond, Rain Man

我们用驾驶来比喻开发软件。驾驶不是将汽车指向一个方向并保持不动；驾驶就是做很多小的路线修正。

We use driving as a metaphor for developing software. Driving is not about pointing the car in one direction and holding to it; driving is about making lots of little course corrections.

驾驶故事在Extreme Programming Explained中占有突出地位，但它是 XP 的核心，所以我们在这里重复一遍。如果您阅读XPE，您将只想阅读本章以查看我们是否以某种方式设法使故事变得更加戏剧化。

The driving story featured prominently in Extreme Programming Explained, but it is central to XP so we repeat it here. If you read XPE, you'll want to read this chapter only to see if we've somehow managed to make the story a bit more dramatic.

那是一个美丽的晴天。肯特和他妈妈正沿着奇科附近的 I-5 州际公路直行。他大约 12 岁。

It was a beautiful sunny day. Kent and his mom were driving along a straight stretch of I-5 near Chico. He was about 12 years old.

“你该学开车了，”妈妈说。

“真的吗？” 兴奋在肯特的胸膛里沸腾。

“是的。现在，我要你做的就是把车停在两条线之间，并且绝对笔直，”妈妈说。

“我能做到。”

"It's about time you learn how to drive," said Mom.

"Really?" Excitement bubbled in Kent's chest.

"Yes. Now, what I want you to do is get the car right in between the lines and pointed absolutely straight," said Mom.

"I can do that."

肯特非常仔细地将米色梅赛德斯 240D 上的星星对准地平线。他的眉毛微微扬起，因为这种驾驶真的很容易。片刻后，他的目光飘向了路边的一个标志。

Kent very carefully lines up the star on the beige Mercedes 240D dead straight to the horizon. His eyebrows raise a little at just how easy this driving thing really is. After a moment, his eyes drift to a roadside sign.

***ggggrrrrrrrccccchhhh***（嘿，你试着写下一种结合了砾石上的轮子和青春期前的叫喊声的声音）。肯特口干舌燥；他的心怦怦直跳。

***ggggrrrrrrccccchhhh*** (hey, you try to write down a sound that combines wheels on gravel with a preadolescent yelp). Kent's mouth goes dry; his heart pounds.

“好吧，”妈妈说，掩饰着微笑，“这不是你开车的方式。开车不是把车开到正确的方向。开车就是不断地做一些小的修正。你有点漂移这个那样，你往那边转一点。这边，那边，只要你在开车。”

"Okay," says Mom, concealing a smile, "that's not how you drive a car. Driving a car is not about getting the car pointed in the right direction. Driving a car is about constantly making little corrections. You drift a little this way, you steer a little that way. This way, that way, as long as you are driving."

您不会通过将项目指向正确的方向（计划）来推动软件开发。你通过观察自己朝这边漂移一点，朝那边转向一点来推动软件开发。这样，那样，只要你开发软件。

You don't drive software development by getting your project pointed in the right direction (The Plan). You drive software development by seeing that you are drifting a little this way and steering a little that way. This way, that way, as long as you develop the software.

一位非常直言不讳的 XP 反对者曾经说过这样的话：“准备……开火……瞄准！” 意图显然是贬义的。除非你先瞄准，否则你怎么能击中目标呢？然而，关键是我们并不是要击中目标。相反，我们正在努力最大化流程的好处。

One very vocal opponent of XP once used the phrase: "Ready... Fire... Aim!" The intent was clearly pejorative. How can you hit a target unless you aim first? The point, however, is that we are not trying to hit a target. Instead, we are trying to maximize the benefit of a process.

驾驶比喻再次帮助了我们。当你上车时，你的第一个动作不是转动方向盘，让它指向你的目的地。您的第一步通常是打开点火装置。事实上，最初的运动方向与你的目的地关系不大，而与你当地的环境有很大关系。在前往皮奥里亚之前，您可能想要退出车库。尽管您可能心中有一个目的地并计划了一条路线，但该路线和目的地总是会发生变化。收音机可能会警告您交通拥堵，导致您改变路线。您的配偶可能会打来电话让您去取牛奶，从而导致您修改目的地。

The driving metaphor helps us once again. Your first act as you get into the car is not turning the wheel so that it points toward your destination. Your first act is usually to turn on the ignition. Indeed, the initial direction of motion has little to do with your destination and much more to do with your local circumstances. You might want to back out of your garage before heading for Peoria. Though you probably have a destination in mind and a route planned, that route and destination are always subject to change. The radio may warn you of heavy traffic, causing you to change your route. Your spouse may call on the cell phone and ask you to pick up some milk, causing you to modify your destination.

软件开发是一个过程。它可能进展顺利，也可能进展不顺利。为了让它顺利进行，我们必须不断地指导它。要引导它，我们必须经常评估它的前进方向，将其与我们希望它前进的方向进行比较，然后进行仔细的调整。因此，良好的项目管理可以具有以下特征：“准备……开火……瞄准……瞄准……瞄准……瞄准……瞄准……”

Software development is a process. It can go well, or it can go badly. To keep it going well we must continually direct it. To direct it we must frequently assess the direction it is going, compare this to the direction we want it to go, and then make careful adjustments. Thus, good project management can be characterized by: "Ready... Fire... Aim... Aim... Aim... Aim... Aim..."

第 4 章平衡功率

Chapter 4. Balancing Power

“我想要个孩子。”

“你不能生孩子。你是个男人！”

“你不要欺负我！”

——犹太人民阵线，布赖恩的生平

"I want to have a baby."

"You can't have a baby. You're a man!"

"Don't you oppress me!"

The Judean People's Front, The Life of Brian

我们的规划过程依赖于明确区分业务人员和软件人员的角色。这确保业务人员做出所有业务决策，而软件人员做出所有技术决策。

Our planning process relies on clearly separating the roles of business people and software people. This ensures that business people make all the business decisions and software people make all the technical decisions.

项目管理的关键是平衡业务人员和程序员之间的权力。做对了，软件项目管理有

The key to project management is balancing power between the business people and the programmers. Done right, software project management has

  • 做商业决定的商人

  • Business people making business decisions

  • 做技术决策的技术人员

  • Technical people making technical decisions

这不就等于说温斯利代尔是奶酪皇后吗？当然，商界人士会做出商业决策。

Isn't this just like saying that Wensleydale is the Queen of Cheeses? Of course business people make business decisions.

这个如何？

What about this one?

“我们认为这个系统需要六个月的时间来开发。”

“你还有三个月。”

“我们能带走什么？”

“没什么。一切都必须在那里。”

"We think this system will take six months to develop."

"You have three months."

"What can we take out?"

"Nothing. Everything has to be there."

猜测编程可能需要多长时间是一个纯粹的技术决定。程序员将他们在类似项目中的经验集中起来，激发他们对新系统有何不同的理解，然后从飞镖靶中选出一个数字。不，实际上它比那更系统一点（见第 12 章）。然而，尽管估计很难，但程序员比其他任何人都更有能力猜测。所以估计是一个技术决定。

Guessing how long something is likely to take to program is a purely technical decision. The programmers pool their experience on similar projects, stir their understanding of how the new system is different, and pick a number off a dartboard. No, actually it's a little more systematic than that (see Chapter 12). However, tough as estimating is, the programmers are in a much better position to guess than anyone else. So estimating is a technical decision.

在上面的对话中，取自一个实际注定失败的项目，估算是由业务人员出于业务原因进行的。由此产生的估计，即所讨论的工作需要三个月，不可能比程序员估计的六个月好。然而，在没有干预的情况下，每个人都根据严重不准确的信息继续进行下一阶段的计划。由此产生的计划，无论多么便宜、灵活和易于沟通，简单地说都是废话。

In the dialog above, taken from an actual doomed project, estimating was done by a business person for business reasons. The resulting estimate, that the work in question would take three months, cannot possibly have been better than the programmers' estimate of six months. However, without intervention, everyone went on to the next stage of planning based on grossly inaccurate information. The resulting plan, no matter how cheap, flexible, and communicable, was, simply put, tripe.

如果业务人员偶尔会做出技术决策，至少技术人员不会做出业务决策。

If business people occasionally make technical decisions, at least technical people don't make business decisions.

呃，这个怎么样？

Uh, how about this one?

“我有十件事要做。我知道我只会完成其中的五件事。我会先处理这个 DCOM/CORBA 基础设施。它看起来很酷。”

"I have ten things to do. I know I'll only get five of them done. I'll work on this DCOM/CORBA infrastructure first. It looks cool."

停止。选择功能之间的相对优先级是一项业务决策。另一个用户界面功能是否比另一个报告列更重要是一个业务决策。业务人员利用他们对市场的了解，将其与他们对类似系统的经验相结合，然后从飞镖盘中挑选出一个功能。不，实际上它可以比这更系统一些（有时是；有时不是）。尽管很难猜测下一步要执行哪个功能，但业务人员比程序员更有能力做出此决定。

Stop. Choosing the relative priority between features is a business decision. Whether another user interface feature is more important than another report column is a business decision. The business people take what they know of the market, combine it with their experience of similar systems, then pick a feature off a dartboard. No, actually it can be a little more systematic than that (sometimes it is; sometimes it isn't). Tough as it is to guess which feature to do next, the business folks are in a much better position than are the programmers to make this decision.

规划中的业务决策是

Business decisions in planning are

  • 日期

  • Dates

  • 范围

  • Scope

  • 优先事项

  • Priority

规划中的技术决策是

Technical decisions in planning are

  • 估计

  • Estimates

如果我们有合适的人做决定，计划就会尽可能顺利。我们将能够应对我们的灾难。我们将通过尽可能减少灾难的数量、尽快发现灾难以及尽可能长时间地维护尽可能多的选择来做到这一点。

If we have the right people making the decisions, planning will go as well as possible. We'll be able to deal with our disasters. We'll do it by reducing the number of disasters as much as possible, by finding out about the disasters as quickly as possible, and by maintaining as many options as possible for as long as possible.

对于一个简单的项目经理来说，平衡政治权力似乎是一项艰巨的任务。如果经过几千年的共同努力，世界各国之间都做不到，你还有什么机会？

Balancing political power may seem like a tall order for a simple project manager. If the world can't do it between nations after a couple of millennia of concerted effort, what chance do you have?

平衡力量并不像听起来那么难。创建一组简单的规则，使技术人员做出技术决策，让业务人员做出业务决策。

Balancing power is not as tough as it sounds. Create a simple set of rules that tend to cause the technical people to make the technical decisions and the business people to make the business decisions.

顾客

The Customer

在 XP 中，我们经常谈论客户。我们所说的客户是指做出业务决策的人。通常你没有一个真正的客户。你有用户、业务管理人员、运营人员，以及各种各样的客户。如果你做收缩包装软件，你可能有成千上万的客户。然而，要让 XP 发挥作用，客户必须用一种声音说话。有些人称这样的动物为产品经理或需求冠军。我们使用tomer这个词是因为这就是这个人所代表的人。

In XP we talk a lot about the customer. By customer we mean the person who makes the business decisions. Often you don't have a single literal customer. You have users, business management, operations, all sorts of people who are customers. If you do shrink-wrap software you may have thousands of customers. However, for XP to work, the customer must speak with one voice. Some people call such an animal a product manager or a requirements champion. We use the term tomer because that's who this person represents.

许多计划流程将客户视为提供需求的软件开发之外的某种无形实体。你解释、挑逗、进行 JAD 会议——但客户在团队之外。

A lot of planning processes see the customer as some kind of disembodied entity outside of software development who provides requirements. You interpret, tease, do JAD sessionsbut the customer is outside the team.

XP不是这样的。XP 计划假定客户是团队的重要组成部分，即使客户为不同的公司工作而团队的其他成员为承包商工作。客户必须是团队的一员，因为他的角色太重要了，不能让给外人。如果客户无法驾驶，任何 (XP) 项目都将失败。

XP is not like that. XP planning assumes that the customer is very much part of the team, even if the customer works for a different company and the rest of the team works for a contractor. The customer must be part of the team because his role is far too important to leave to an outsider. Any (XP) project will fail if the customer isn't able to steer.

所以客户的工作是一项巨大的责任。当客户达不到要求时，世界上所有最好的人才、技术和流程都会失败。可悲的是，这也是我们无法提供特别明智建议的角色。毕竟，我们是书呆子，不是商人。但这是我们可以肯定的。

So the customer's job is a huge responsibility. All the best talent and technology and process in the world will fail when the customer isn't up to scratch. Sadly, it's also a role on which we can't offer particularly sage advice. After all, we're nerds, not business people. But here's what we know for sure.

寻找客户

Finding a Customer

因为客户是一个如此重要的角色，所以找到一个能很好地扮演这个角色的人是很重要的。好客户

Because the customer is such a critical role, it's important to find someone who will play it well. A good customer

  • 通过在该领域工作以及了解它的工作原理（并不总是一回事）来很好地理解该领域

  • Understands the domain well by working in that domain, and also by understanding how it works (not always the same thing)

  • 可以理解，在开发的帮助下，软件如何在领域中提供商业价值

  • Can understand, with development's help, how software can provide business value in the domain

  • 决心定期交付价值，不怕交付太少而不是什么都不交付

  • Is determined to deliver value regularly and is not afraid to deliver too little rather than nothing

  • 可以决定现在需要什么和以后需要什么

  • Can make decisions about what's needed now and what's needed later

  • 愿意为项目的成败承担最终责任

  • Is willing to accept ultimate responsibility for the success or failure of the project

为项目的成败承担责任似乎是这个角色最困难的部分。与团队保持距离对客户来说有一定的安慰。后面三尺需求文档差不多就对了。在 XP 中这是行不通的。如果你迷路了，那不是车的错，而是司机的错。

Accepting responsibility for the success or failure of the project seems to be the most difficult part of the role. There is a certain comfort for the customer in maintaining a distance from the team. Behind three feet of requirements documents is about right. In XP this won't work. If you get lost driving, it isn't the car's fault, it's the driver's.

对于客户来说，XP 最棘手的事情是习惯定期交付的节奏。很多流程都要求客户提供他们想要的一切。相反，客户要求，团队交付，尽可能少——刚好足以提供价值。有一种观点认为，如果您找不到愿意以这种方式工作的客户，那么您根本就不应该尝试 XP。

The trickiest thing about XP for a customer is getting used to the rhythm of regular delivery. A lot of processes ask the customer for everything they want. Instead, the customer asks for, and the team delivers, as little as possiblejust enough to provide value. There's an argument that says if you can't find a customer who wants to work that way you shouldn't try XP at all.

引导客户

Guiding the Customer

如果您是阅读本文的客户，请记住以下重要事项。

If you're a customer reading this, then here are some important things to remember.

随时问自己，“接下来最有价值的功能是什么？” 长期规划可能很有趣，但只有定期、少量的交付才能让资金持续流入。

Ask yourself at all times, "What is the most valuable functionality to have next?" Long-term planning can be fun, but it's regular, little deliveries that keep the money coming in.

相信开发人员的估计，但请记住他们只是估计，他们会弄错的。估计软件开发是困难的；他们正在尽力而为，他们会变得更好。

Trust the developers' estimates, yet remember they're only estimates and they will get it wrong. Estimating software development is hard; they're doing the best they can and they will get better.

永远不要错过约会。推迟日期是软件开发中最糟糕的习惯之一。你只滑了一两次，过了一会儿你就上瘾了。推迟约会并不完全违反规则，只是 XP 方法要求您每次这样做时都要砍掉自己的一根手指。

Never let a date slip. Slipping dates is one of the worst habits in software development. You slip just one or two and after a while you're addicted. It isn't completely against the rules to slip a date, it's just that the XP methodology requires you to chop one of your own fingers off each time you do it.

每次发布都提供一点有价值的功能，并尽可能经常地向真实客户发布。不要害怕发布还不够的东西。发挥你的创造力，寻找方法将一个大的新功能分解成小块，这样你就可以继续交付。如果您发布的频率足够高，您将无需等待很长时间就能获得更多您想要的内容。

Provide a little valuable functionality every single release, and release to real customers as often as you can. Don't be afraid to release something that's not enough yet. Use your creativity to look for ways that you can take a large new capability and break it up into little pieces so you can keep delivering. If you release frequently enough, you won't have long to wait before you get more of what you want.

第 5 章概述

Chapter 5. Overviews

XP 流程的发布需要几个月的时间，分为两周的迭代，分为需要几天的任务。计划将故事（功能块）分配给发布和迭代，以响应开发的现实。

The XP process has releases that take a few months, that divide into two-week iterations, that divide into tasks that take a few days. Planning allocates stories (chunks of function) to releases and iterations in reaction to the realities of development.

我们将以两种方式概述 XP。如果您想在进入细节之前有一个整体的了解，请先阅读以下部分。如果您想从小到大，请先阅读本章的第二部分。

We're going to outline XP in two ways. If you like an overall understanding before going into details, read the following section first. If you like to go from smaller to larger scale, read the second section of this chapter first.

自顶向下

Top Down

在春天种植；秋天收获。世界以循环运转。软件开发也不例外。规划挑战在于我们需要适应和同步两个周期——业务周期和开发周期。

Plant in the spring; harvest in the fall. The world works on cycles. Software development is no different. The planning challenge is that there are two cycles that we need to accommodate and synchronizethe business cycle and the development cycle.

商业周期围绕着商业活动：

The business cycle revolves around the activities of business:

  • 新闻稿

  • Press releases

  • 软件发布、制造和安装

  • Software release, manufacturing, and installation

  • 训练

  • Training

  • 计费

  • Billing

在过去，这个周期是悠闲的两到三年。最近，在广泛的电信和软件交付技术进步的推动下，这个周期已经大大收紧。尽管如此，商业周期至少长达数月。我们将这些一到六个月的业务周期中的一个称为发布。

In the old days this cycle was a leisurely two to three years long. Recently, the cycle has tightened enormously, driven by widespread telecommunications and technical advances in the delivery of software. Still, the business cycle is at least months long. We will call one of these one- to six-month turns of the business crank a release.

开发周期一直比商业周期短。缩短周期的目的是在中途纠正项目。有时，临时可交付成果记录了某些类型的决策，例如瀑布的需求、分析和设计文档。有时它们是部分功能系统或子系统，如在增量开发中。

The development cycle has always been shorter than the business cycle. The intent of having a shorter cycle was to correct projects in midcourse. Sometimes the interim deliverables documented certain kinds of decisions, as in the requirements, analysis, and design documents of a waterfall. Sometimes they were partly functional systems or subsystems, as in incremental development.

商业周期的收缩需要开发周期的类似收缩。如果我们每隔几个月发布一次，那么如果我们希望能够进行中途修正，就必须将开发周期缩短到不超过几周。我们将这些一到三周的开发周期之一称为迭代。

The contraction of the business cycle requires a similar contraction of the development cycle. If we release every few months, then if we want to be able to make midcourse corrections we must shrink the development cycle to no more than a few weeks. We will call one of these one- to three-week development cycles an iteration.

几周一个周期的问题是，几周内不可能完成任何事情。您无法完成分析，无法构建基础设施或设置框架。我们必须使用其他一些衡量进展的方法。由于客户为软件付费，我们将使用他们理解的衡量标准——故事。一个故事代表客户希望在软件中具有的功能，一个他们希望能够告诉他们的朋友他们正在使用的这个伟大系统的故事。

The problem with a cycle of a few weeks is that it is impossible to complete anything in a few weeks. You can't complete the analysis, or build the infrastructure, or set up the framework. We have to use some other measure of progress. Since the customers are paying for the software, we'll use a measure they understandthe story. A story represents a feature customers want in the software, a story they would like to be able to tell their friends about this great system they are using.

对于适合迭代的几个故事，故事必须相当小。一个故事应该需要程序员几天到几周的时间来实现。

For a few stories to fit into an iteration, the stories have to be fairly small. A story should take a programmer a few days to a few weeks to implement.

迭代的结果是什么？完成发布工程和将其交付给客户之间的任何活动都存在风险。我们讨厌风险。因此，迭代的结果必须是一个经过全面测试的、生产就绪的系统。

What is the result of an iteration? Any activity that comes between finishing the engineering of a release and delivering it to customers represents a risk. We hate risk. So the result of an iteration must be a fully tested, production-ready system.

这听起来不可能。但是第一次迭代时，故事的数量很少。如果系统足够小，您可以在迭代期间对其进行测试和验证。如果您投资使验证自动化，那么当您完成第二次迭代时，验证两组故事的增量成本再次变小。如果您从不“拖欠付款”，如果每次迭代的结果都准备好使用，那么维持准备就绪的成本仍然是合理的。

This may sound impossible. But the first time you go through an iteration, the number of stories is small. If a system is small enough you can test and verify it during the iteration. If you invest in making the verification automatic, when you finish the second iteration the incremental cost of verifying both sets of stories is again small. If you never "get behind on your payments," if the result of each iteration is ready to be used, then the cost of maintaining readiness remains reasonable.

自下而上

Bottom Up

如果我们将整个软件开发生命周期缩小到微观尺寸，比如两周，会怎样？我们仍然需要解决我们以前必须解决的所有问题——规范、设计、实施、测试、集成、部署、培训、文档——但现在它们将是小问题，而不是大问题，其中一些可能会完全消失.

What if we shrunk the whole software development life cycle to microscopic size, say two weeks? We would still have to solve all the problems we had to solve beforespecification, design, implementation, testing, integration, deployment, training, documentationbut now they would be small problems, not big problems, and some of them might disappear entirely.

各种开发活动不会在我们为期两周的小项目中分阶段进行（我们称其为迭代，只是为了方便）。我们每天都必须做一点。

The various development activities won't be phases inside our little two-week project (let's call it an iteration, just to be conventional). We will have to do a little of each of them every day.

每次迭代都包含全面开发的所有要素。最后，我们有了可交付的软件，可以部署了。它只是不包含很多功能。也许它只包含一个功能。因此，我们将不得不进行另一次迭代，一次又一次（我们认为因此得名）。每次迭代都将包含更多功能。

Each iteration contains all the elements of full-scale development. At the end we have shippable software, ready to deploy. It just doesn't contain many features. Maybe it will contain only one feature. So we will have to do another iteration and another and another (hence the name, we suppose). Each iteration will contain a few more features.

还有一件事，图片就完成了。计划的目的之一是确保我们始终在任何给定时间处理最有价值的事情。我们不能随意挑选特征并期望它们是最有价值的。我们必须通过快速查看所有可能有价值的东西来开始开发，将所有卡片都放在桌面上。在每次迭代开始时，业务（记住权力的平衡）将为下一次迭代挑选最有价值的特性。

One more thing and the picture is complete. One of the purposes of planning is to ensure we always work on the most valuable thing possible at any given time. We can't pick features at random and expect them to be most valuable. We have to begin development by taking a quick look at everything that might be valuable, putting all our cards on the table. At the beginning of each iteration the business (remember the balance of power) will pick the most valuable features for the next iteration.

现在我们有了一个流程，计划可以在其中发挥适当的作用。该过程通过规划整个开发过程确保我们有一个尽可能好的开始。该过程通过每隔几周挑选一次新需求来降低需求风险。该过程通过将计划分解成足够小的部分来降低实施风险，当一个部分破裂时，它会尽快影响整体计划。

Now we have a process where planning can do its proper job. The process makes sure we get off to as good a start as possible by laying out the whole of development. The process mitigates requirements risk by picking new requirements every few weeks. The process mitigates implementation risk by breaking planning up into small enough pieces that when one piece blows up it will affect the overall plan as quickly and visibly as possible.

第 6 章太多事情要做

Chapter 6. Too Much to Do

当你超负荷工作时，不要认为时间不够；认为它有太多事情要做。你不能给自己更多的时间，但你可以少给自己做事，至少目前是这样。

When you are overloaded, don't think of it as not having enough time; think of it as having too much to do. You can't give yourself more time, but you can give yourself less to do, at least for the moment.

一旦团队从即将被遗忘的状态中解救出来，我们就一起进行了一个项目。在第一次发布之前，有一段时间每个人都清楚我们不会确定发布日期。有一天，我们召开了一次站立会议来讨论这个问题。我们绕着圈子回答“是什么阻止我们投入生产？”这个问题。

We were on a project together once that the team had rescued from impending oblivion. Toward the first release there came a time when it was clear to everyone that we weren't going to make the release date. One day we had a stand-up meeting to discuss the problem. We went around the circle answering the question "What is preventing us from going into production?"

“我没有足够的时间。”

“我没有足够的时间。”

“我没有足够的时间。”

"I don't have enough time."

"I don't have enough time."

"I don't have enough time."

没有人有足够的时间。但没有明显的答案。每个人都回家了。

Nobody had enough time. But there was no obvious answer. Everybody went home.

那天晚上吃韩国菜（我们总是吃韩国菜；这似乎对大脑有好处），我们在谈论会议。突然，宇宙射线与一块泡菜相撞，我们看到了真正的问题。

Over Korean food that night (we always ate Korean; it seems to be good for the brain), we were talking about the meeting. Suddenly a cosmic ray collided with a piece of kimchee and we saw the real problem.

第二天早上，我们召开了另一场站立会议。

The next morning we called another stand-up.

“跟着我重复——我有太多事要做。”

"Repeat after meI have too much to do."

耸耸肩，但管他呢。

Shrugs all around, but what the heck.

“我有太多事情要做。”

“我有太多事情要做。”

“我有太多事情要做。”

"I have too much to do."

"I have too much to do."

"I have too much to do."

依此类推，直到我们到达理查德。

And so on around the circle until we got to Richard.

“我有太多事情要做。你有什么意思？”

"I have too much to do. What is your point?"

关键是当你没有足够的时间时，你就不走运了。你不能腾出更多的时间。没有足够的时间是一种绝望的境地。绝望滋生挫折、错误、倦怠和失败。

The point is that when you don't have enough time you are out of luck. You can't make more time. Not having enough time is a position of hopelessness. And hopelessness breeds frustration, mistakes, burnout, and failure.

然而，我们都知道有太多事情要做。当你有太多事情要做时，你可以

Having too much to do, however, is a situation we all know. When you have too much to do you can

  • 优先考虑而不做某些事情

  • Prioritize and not do some things

  • 减少你做的一些事情的规模

  • Reduce the size of some of the things you do

  • 要求别人做一些事情

  • Ask someone else to do some things

有太多事情要做会滋生希望。我们可能不喜欢在那里，但至少我们知道该怎么做。

Having too much to do breeds hope. We may not like being there, but at least we know what to do.

第 7 章四个变量

Chapter 7. Four Variables

我可以改变物理定律。我必须有三十分钟，船长。

——Scottyk，Star Tre

I canna change the laws of physics. I've got to have thirty minutes, Captain.

Scottyk, Star Tre

我们使用四个变量来帮助我们思考如何控制项目：成本、质量、时间和范围。它们相互关联，但又以奇怪的方式相互影响。

We use four variables to help us think about how to control a project: cost, quality, time, and scope. They are interrelated but affect each other in strange ways.

我们都听过诸如“成本、时间、质量：任选其二”之类的说法。很多人都有自己的方式来谈论完成某件事时如何涉及这些变量，而你无法同时控制它们。在规划软件项目时，我们必须添加一个变量才能控制我们的项目：

We've all heard statements like "Cost, time, quality: pick any two." Plenty of people have ways in which they talk about how there are these variables involved in getting something done, and that you can't control them all at once. In planning software projects, we had to add a variable before we could bring our projects under control:

  • 成本

  • Cost

  • 质量

  • Quality

  • 时间

  • Time

  • 范围

  • Scope

我们喜欢将它们视为维多利亚时代大型蒸汽机上的四个杠杆。四个杠杆控制机器（我们的项目）。如果你移动任何杠杆，其他杠杆也会移动。你可以锁定任何你喜欢的杠杆，但如果你锁定了三个杠杆，你就不能移动第四个。

We like to think of them as four levers on some big Victorian steam machine. The four levers control the machine (our project). If you move any lever the others move. You can lock any lever you like, but if you lock three levers you cannot move the fourth.

然而，要注意的是，移动杠杆的效果是延迟的和非线性的。您不能只是将成本加倍，其他一切保持不变，而时间却减半。所以每个杠杆都有自己的小说明书。（好消息是这本手册不是维多利亚时代二流小说家写的。）

The catch, however, is that the effect of moving a lever is both delayed and nonlinear. You can't just double the cost, hold everything else the same, and halve the time. So each lever gets its own little instruction manual. (The good news is that the manual wasn't written by a second-rate Victorian novelist.)

成本

Cost

成本杠杆实际上是几个主要是独立的杠杆。移动它们中的任何一个都可以增加或减少您的成本，但每个杠杆对其他三个主要杠杆都有不同的影响。

The cost lever is actually several mostly independent levers. Moving any of them can increase or reduce your costs, but each lever has a different effect on the three other primary levers.

最强大的杠杆是人。你可以通过让更多的人参与项目来增加这个杠杆。然而，该杠杆具有非线性效应和较长的延迟。

The most powerful lever is people. You increase this lever by putting more people on the project. This lever, however, suffers from having both a nonlinear effect and a long delay.

非线性来自拥有更多人的通信开销。将你的团队加倍并不会使你的速度加倍，因为它增加了需要继续进行的沟通量。在这方面我们真的没有太多指导，部分是因为没有数据，部分是因为有太多其他因素会产生影响。您所能做的就是添加一些人并衡量效果。

The nonlinearity comes from the communication overhead of having more people. Doubling your team doesn't make you go twice as fast because it increases the amount of communication that needs to go on. There isn't really much guidance we can give you on this, partly because there isn't the data and partly because so many other factors have an effect. All you can do is add some people and measure the effect.

问题是您必须等待才能真正看到效果，因为添加人员会导致一些需要时间才能完成的更改。直接的影响是令人震惊的景象没有任何变化，甚至更糟的是放缓。当一个新人加入一个跑步团队时，他最初的价值不大，因为他不了解系统或团队。事实上，他可以放慢速度，因为他在别人教他这些事情时浪费了他们的时间。您添加的人越多，这种减速效果就越大。添加足够多的人，项目就会戛然而止。这就是 Brooks 定律的由来，“将人员添加到已延迟的项目只会让项目变得更晚。” [1]

The trouble is you'll have to wait to really see the effect, since adding people causes several changes that take time to play out. The immediate effect is the alarming sight of nothing changing, or even worse, a slowing down. When a new person joins a running team he will initially be of little value because he doesn't know the system or the team. Indeed, he can slow things down because he drains time from other people as they teach him about these things. The more people you add, the bigger this slowdown effect is. Add enough people and the project can come to a big crunching halt. This is the origin for Brooks' Law, "Adding people to a late project just makes it later."[1]

[1] Frederick P. Brooks, Jr.，《人月神话：软件工程论文集》，（马萨诸塞州雷丁市：Addison-Wesley，1995 年）。

[1] Frederick P. Brooks, Jr., The Mythical Man-Month: Essays on Software Engineering, (Reading, MA: Addison-Wesley, 1995).

还有其他花钱的方法。花在工具上就像增加人一样。但是随着人们学习如何使用这些工具，你会放慢速度，只有当他们熟悉这些工具时，你才会知道它们是否有用。

There are other ways to spend money. Spending on tools can be like adding people. But you will slow down as people learn how to use the tools, and only when they become comfortable with the tools will you know whether they will help.

花一些钱可以获得很好的回报：更快的电脑、更大的显示器。不要害怕花钱来保持动力。积极性高的开发人员比积极性低下的人更有效率。

Spending some money can have a very good return: faster computers, bigger monitors. Don't be afraid to spend money to keep motivation up. Well- motivated developers are much more effective than people whose motivation sags.

加班没有用。虽然在很短的时间内它确实加快了团队的速度，但如果你这样做任何时间长度，你都会受到严重的伤害。最大的杀手是动力。让一个积极进取的程序员工作 7 小时比让一个疲倦、心烦意乱的程序员工作 10 小时要好得多。即使程序员想长时间工作，这也不是一个好主意。长时间工作会使人疲倦，疲倦的人会犯错误，而错误需要时间来修复。我们都在早上拜访了客户，并花了一整天的时间来追查前一天晚上 10 点出现的错误。特别是对于年轻的硅谷团队来说，加班是一种非常重要的部落习惯，我们必须努力让人们不要加班。如果他们真的没有生活，那就让他们在晚上玩电脑游戏。它'

Overtime doesn't help. Although in the very short term it does speed up the team, if you do it for any length of time you will get bitten badly. The big killer is motivation. It's much better to have a motivated programmer work seven hours than a tired, distracted programmer work ten. Even if the programmers want to work long hours it's not a good idea. Long hours make people tired, tired people make mistakes, and mistakes take time to fix. We've both gone into clients in the morning and spent all day chasing a bug that was put in at ten o'clock the previous night. Particularly with young Silicon Valley teams, where long hours are such an important tribal ritual, we have to work hard to get people not to do overtime. If they really have no life, get them to play computer games in the evening instead. It's much more productive to have castles mown down by trebuchets than it is to slip bugs into complicated software.

质量

Quality

质量实际上是两个杠杆：外部质量和内部质量。外部质量是客户感知的质量。这包括错误，但也可能包括非功能性要求，例如 GUI 的外观和软件的速度。

Quality is really two levers: external and internal quality. External quality is the quality perceived by the customer. This includes bugs but may also include nonfunctional requirements such as how the GUI looks and how fast the software is.

尝试将非功能性需求移至范围。为诸如“使用户界面更令人愉悦”或“将平均索赔处理时间控制在 300 毫秒以下”之类的内容编一个故事。正如我们稍后将看到的，范围是最好的操作杠杆。

Try to move nonfunctional requirements over to scope. Make a story for something like "Make the user interface more pleasing" or "Get average claim processing time to under 300 ms." As we'll see later, scope is the best lever to operate.

错误通常也是一个范围界定问题。通常您可能不得不用缺陷换取故事。我们将在第 22 章中详细讨论这一点。

Bugs are often also a scoping issue. Often you may have to trade defects for stories. We'll talk about this more in Chapter 22.

另一个杠杆是内部质量。这反映了系统内部的质量：它的设计有多好，内部测试有多好，等等。这是一个非常危险的杠杆。如果您允许内部质量下降，您会立即获得小幅速度提升，随后速度会大幅下降。因此，您必须密切注视这个杠杆，并确保它始终保持在尽可能高的位置。没有什么比糟糕的内部质量更有效地扼杀速度。这就是极限编程如此重视测试和重构等实践的原因。如果你保持高内部质量，你可以看到你在哪里，并预测你可以去哪里。

The other lever is internal quality. This reflects the quality of the internals of the system: how well it is designed, how good the internal tests are, and so on. This is a very dangerous lever to play with. If you allow internal quality to drop you'll get a small immediate increase in speed, rapidly followed by a much bigger decrease in speed. As a result you must keep an eagle eye on this lever and make sure it is always up as far as it can go. Nothing kills speed more effectively than poor internal quality. That's why Extreme Programming puts so much attention on practices like testing and refactoring. If you keep internal quality high you can see where you are and predict where you can go.

时间和范围

Time and Scope

因此，前两个杠杆充其量也很难发挥作用，而且肯定不可能施加任何短期控制。时间和范围是最好的操作杠杆。在我们的大部分计划中，我们假设质量和成本是固定的。

So the first two levers are difficult to work with at best, and certainly impossible for exerting any short-term control. Time and scope are left as the best levers to operate. With most of our planning, we assume that qualtity and cost are fixed.

问题是我们如何最好地操作时间和范围杠杆？

The question is how do we best operate the time and scope levers?

这两个杠杆的复杂之处在于它们位于机器的不同部分。示波器杆就在您的面前，喜欢被推上去。每次你通过机器时，你都想将杠杆向上推一点，并为项目添加另一个小故事。机器会发出可爱的咯咯声作为即时奖励。“是的，长官，我们也能做到，长官。”

The complicated thing about these two levers is that they are placed on very different parts of the machine. The scope lever is right in front of you and just loves to be pushed up. Every time you pass the machine you want to push that lever up a bit and add another little story to the project. The machine responds with a cute little gurgle as an instant reward. "Yes, sir, we can do that, too, sir."

然而，时间杠杆真的很尴尬。你必须用手和膝盖爬行，伸长脖子，然后打开标有“小心豹子”的门。因为添加作用域对时间的影响很难看到，所以人们通常直到为时已晚并且机器失控时才意识到发生了什么。

The time lever, however, is really awkwardly placed. You have to crawl on your hands and knees, crane your neck, and flip open the door labeled "Beware of the leopard." Because the effects on time when adding scope are so hard to see, people don't usually realize what's happening until it's too late and the machine is out of control.

规划必须让时间杠杆可见，这样每次增加范围时，您都可以立即看到及时的效果。你只需要安排镜子来避免烟雾。

Planning must make the time lever visible, so that every time you add scope you can immediately see the effects on time. You just need to arrange the mirrors to avoid the smoke.

当你在项目结束时，你才真正知道你在哪里。所以你需要每隔几周结束一次项目——这就是我们使用迭代的原因。迭代迫使我们每隔几周查看一次时间杠杆，因此我们无法避免看到更改范围的后果。

You only really know where you are when you are at the end of project. So you need to end the project every few weeksthat's why we use iterations. The iterations force us to look at the time lever every few weeks so we can't avoid seeing the consequences of changing scope.

规划现在变成了弄清楚在每次迭代中构建哪些故事的问题。

Planning now becomes a matter of figuring out which stories to build in each iteration.

我们需要一种规划风格

We need a planning style that

  • 保持程序员对计划可行的信心

  • Preserves the programmers' confidence that the plan is possible

  • 保持客户的信心，即他们会尽可能多地获得

  • Preserves the customers' confidence that they are getting as much as they can

  • 执行成本尽可能低（因为我们会经常计划，但没有人为计划买单；他们为结果买单）

  • Costs as little to execute as possible (because we'll be planning often, but nobody pays for plans; they pay for results)

在这一点上，我们对维多利亚时代的机器感到厌倦，并感到另一个类比即将到来。

At this point we are getting tired of our Victorian machine and feel another analogy coming on.

购买故事

Shopping for Stories

如果规划一款软件就像购物一样呢？当你一周去杂货店购物时，你有一个预算。你走进商店，环顾四周，查看商品及其价格，然后思考你需要完成什么。如果你要喂养一大群青少年，你倾向于选择大米和豆类。如果老板过来吃晚饭，你可以吃一晚牛排，然后在接下来的一周里过得很轻松。

What if planning for a piece of software was like shopping? When you go grocery shopping for the week, you have a budget. You go into the store and look around at the items and their prices, and you think about what you need to accomplish. If you are feeding a horde of teenagers, you tend toward rice and beans. If the boss if coming over for dinner, you get steak for one night and go easy the rest of the week.

类比的要素是

The elements of the analogy are

  • 这几项

  • The items

  • 价格

  • The prices

  • 预算

  • The budget

  • 约束条件

  • The constraints

将类比应用于规划：

Applying the analogy to planning:

  • 物品就是故事。

  • Items are the stories.

  • 价格是对每个故事的估计。

  • Prices are the estimates on each story.

  • 预算是团队根据这些估算得出的衡量进度。

  • Budget is the team's measured progress in terms of these estimates.

  • 约束是客户和团队发现的业务和技术约束。

  • Constraints are the business and technology constraints as they are discovered by the customer and the team.

购物类比可以让我们更进一步。

The shopping analogy can carry us a little further.

  • 销售——如果报告比预期更容易实施，那就是销售报告。“注意软件购物者。14 号过道上的报告是二比一。”

  • SalesIf reports turn out to be easier to implement than expected, that's having a sale on reports. "Attention software shoppers. Reports are going two for one on aisle 14."

  • Rain check——如果你不得不在发布过程中放弃一个新向导以保存结束日期，那就是在进行 rain check。“欠一个巫师。”

  • Rain checkIf you have to discard a new wizard in the middle of a release to save the end date, that's taking a rain check. "IOU one wizard."

  • 通货膨胀——如果图形比预期更难添加，价格就会上涨。“由于我们无法控制的情况，图形现在每磅 1.49 美元。”

  • InflationIf graphics are harder to add than expected, the prices go up. "Due to circumstances beyond our control, graphics are now $1.49 per pound."

任何时候我们必须决定做什么，我们都会去购物。谁来选择商品的大小，谁来定价，都会有所不同，但策略是一样的。我们将购买价值 500 万美元的软件，并将购买下周的任务。

Any time we have to decide what to do, we will go shopping. Who chooses how big the items are and who sets the prices will all vary, but the strategy is the same. We will shop for $5 million worth of software and we will shop for next week's tasks.

第 8 章 昨天的天气

Chapter 8. Yesterday's Weather

你不能在一个五磅重的袋子里装十磅屎。

——任何尝试过的人

You can't put ten pounds of shit in a five-pound bag.

Anyone who has tried

作为你计划的基础，假设你这周做的和上周一样多。

As the basis for your planning, assume you'll do as much this week as you did last week.

包有多大？这个购物比喻很好，但预算是多少？您承诺在接下来的n个月内完成多少工作？

How big is the bag? This shopping metaphor is all well and good, but what is the budget? How much do you commit to doing in the next n months?

如果你承诺太多，开发就会在云中进行。程序员知道他们注定要失败。他们没有尽力而为。他们没有清楚地沟通。老练的政治家玩“日程鸡”游戏，第一个指出前面任务不可能完成的人被贴上失败者的标签，而不是“有团队精神的人”。

If you commit to too much, development proceeds under a cloud. The programmers know they are doomed. They don't do their best work. They don't communicate clearly. The political sophisticates play Schedule Chicken, where the first person to point out the impossibility of the task ahead is labeled a loser, not a "team player."

好吧，我们不想那样做。我们也不想承诺不足。如果事实证明我们可以比我们想象的快两倍，那么业务将需要一段时间才能赶上。新闻稿不会提及一半很酷的新功能。销售人员不会了解产品中的所有内容。程序员付出 100% 的努力是一件值得骄傲的事情。

Okay, we don't want to do that. Neither do we want to undercommit. If it turns out we can go twice as fast as we thought we could, the business will take a while to catch up. The press releases won't mention half of the cool new features. Sales won't understand what all is in the product. And it is a matter of pride for programmers to put out 100 percent.

我们如何才能驾驭这样一个情感和商业雷区？我们怎样才能想出一个复杂的规则制定装置来准确地捕捉和平衡所有可用的技术和情感信息？

How can we navigate such an emotional and business minefield? How can we come up with a complicated rule-making apparatus that accurately captures and balances all the technical and emotional information that is available?

我们不——惊喜，惊喜。相反，我们选择一个在大多数情况下都能很好地工作的简单规则：

We don'tsurprise, surprise. Instead we opt for a simple rule that works pretty well in most circumstances:

假设你明天要做的和今天实际完成的一样多。

Say you'll do as much tomorrow as you actually got done today.

故事

The Story

这是一个杜撰的故事。某些国家/地区的气象服务（不是您的，也许是我们的）花费了数十亿美元用于复杂的新天气预报系统。灯光闪烁，卡片喷出，磁带旋转，然后出现了大约 70% 准确率的预测。授权花费数十亿美元的人印象深刻。

Here is an apocryphal story. Some country's weather service (not yours, but perhaps ours) spent a bazillion dollars on a sophisticated new weather prediction system. Lights flashed, cards spewed, tapes spun, and out came predictions that were about 70 percent accurate. The people who authorized spending the bazillion dollars were quite impressed.

然后有一天有人注意到一种更简单的方法来获得相同的准确性。每天都预测明天的天气会和今天完全一样。

Then one day someone noticed a simpler way to get the same accuracy. Every day predict that tomorrow's weather will be exactly the same as today's.

这就是为什么我们称我们的规则为昨天的天气。

That's why we call our rule Yesterday's Weather.

怎么运行的

How It Works

暂时假设您要实现的每个功能都需要付出相同的努力（请参阅第 12 章了解我们的实际工作）。如果我们上个月做了五个功能，当我们被问及这个月我们能做多少时，我们会说“五个”。如果我们在一段时间内每两周完成了三个功能，然后我们被问到在接下来的六个月里我们可以做多少，我们会说“3 个功能/迭代 × 2 次迭代/月 × 6 个月 = 36 个功能”。

Assume for the moment that each feature you are going to implement takes the same amount of effort (see Chapter 12 for what we really do). If we did five features last month and we're asked how much we can do this month, we say "five." If we have gotten three features done every two weeks for a while and we're asked how much we can do in the next six months, we say "3 features/iteration × 2 iterations/month × 6 months = 36 features."

以下是此规则的一些涌现属性：

Here are some of the emergent properties of this rule:

  • 我们不会习惯性地高估自己的能力。我们要用实际的成绩。如果我们高估了一次，我们将无法进行下一次。

  • We won't habitually overestimate our abilities. We have to use actual accomplishment. If we overestimate once, we won't be able to the next time.

  • 如果我们过度投入，我们将倾向于尝试在任何给定时间段内完成一些项目，而不是完成所有项目的一半。告诉客户他们下次可以零功能真是太尴尬了。

  • If we are overcommitted, we will tend to try to finish some items in any given time period instead of half finishing them all. It is so embarrassing to tell the customer they can have zero features next time.

  • 另一方面，如果我们经历了灾难性的时期，我们可以保证有一点喘息的空间来恢复。

  • On the other hand, if we have a disastrous period, we are guaranteed a little breathing space to recover.

  • 每个人都学会相信我们的数字，因为它们很容易解释。

  • Everyone learns to trust our numbers because they are so easy to explain.

  • 我们的估算会自动跟踪各种变化——团队变化、新技术、产品方向的巨大变化。

  • Our estimates automatically track all kinds of changeschanges to the team, new technology, dramatic changes in product direction.

第 9 章确定项目范围

Chapter 9. Scoping a Project

它比面包盒大吗？

——二十个问题

Is it bigger than a breadbox?

Twenty Questions

要快速了解项目有多大，请粗略地运行规划过程。

To get a quick feel for how big the project is, run the planning process at coarse resolution.

假设到目前为止，您是该项目中唯一的人。第一步是什么？您如何使用购物来实现项目？

Let's say you're the only one on the project so far. What's the first step? How can you use shopping to bring a project into existence?

  • 项目- 

    大故事

  • Items 

    Big stories

  • 价格- 

    粗略估计每个故事的实现时间

  • Prices 

    Rough estimates of the time to implement each story

  • 预算- 

    大概有多少人在这个项目上工作

  • Budget 

    Roughly how many people you have to work on the project

  • 约束—— 

    由具有业务知识的人提供

  • Constraints 

    Supplied by someone with business knowledge

第一个计划的目的是快速回答“该项目是否有意义？”这个问题。通常这些健全的计划是在项目中有任何技术人员之前制定的。不要担心得到完美的数字。如果该项目有意义，那么您将投入足够的资金来准备您有信心的计划。

The purpose of this first plan is to quickly answer the question "Does the project make any sense at all?" Often these sanity plans are made before there are any technical people on the project at all. Don't worry about getting perfect numbers. If the project makes any sense then you'll invest enough to prepare a plan you have some confidence in.

如果我们要实施太空时代旅行系统怎么办？（有关系统的完整故事，请参阅故事示例。）我们可能会想到一些大故事。在我们为它们指定价格之前，我们必须对系统有更多的了解。我们问几个问题：

What if we were to implement a space-age travel system? (For the full story of the system see Example of Stories.) We might have a few big stories in mind. Before we can assign prices to them, we have to know a little more about the system. We ask a few questions:

  • 我们需要处理多少预订？

  • How many reservations do we need to handle?

  • 我们需要多少时间让系统可用？

  • How much of the time do we need to have the system available?

  • 将使用什么样的机器来访问系统？

  • What kind of machines will be used to access the system?

考虑到这一点，我们可以猜测一个十人团队需要多长时间来实现每个功能，如表 9.1所示。

With that in mind, we can guess at how long a team of ten would need to implement each feature as shown in Table 9.1.

表 9.1。故事
故事 估计
预订太空飞行 2个月
预定一间旅馆 1个月
查看行程 1个月
探险之旅 2个月
全息行星模拟 6个月
跨物种定位 4个月
自动翻译器 8个月

我们在进行过程中做了一些简化的假设。

We make some simplifying assumptions as we go along.

  • 这些故事彼此完全独立。

  • The stories are completely independent of each other.

  • 我们将随着故事开发必要的基础设施，但仅限于该故事绝对需要的基础设施。

  • We will develop the necessary infrastructure along with the story, but only the infrastructure absolutely needed for that story.

我们知道这些假设并不完全准确，但话又说回来。如果我们试图预测未来，这会让我们担心。因为我们不是，所以它没有。

We know these assumptions aren't exactly accurate, but then again neither is anything else. If we were trying to predict the future, this would worry us. Since we aren't, it doesn't.

所以，底线是我们可以在 24 个月内实施该系统。

So, the bottom line is that we can implement the system in 24 months.

喊叫声开始了。“我们必须在六个月内上市，否则我们就完蛋了。” 是的，我们明白。“如果你做不到，我们会雇用能做到的人。” 你应该这样做，但也许我们可以先谈谈。“你们这些程序员不能告诉我该怎么做。” 当然不是，但也许您想知道您不能做什么。

The shouting starts. "We have to go to market in six months, tops, or we're dead." Yes, we understand. "If you can't do it, we'll hire someone who can." You should do that, but perhaps we can talk a little first. "You programmers can't tell me what to do." Of course not, but perhaps you would like to know what you can't do.

现在谈判开始了。“如果我们先做一个预订系统呢？我们需要前三个故事。那是四个月。但如果没有全息模拟，我们就无法启动。两个月后你能给我什么？”

Now the negotiation starts. "What if we just made a booking system first? We'd need the first three stories. That's four months. But we can't launch without the holographic simulation. What can you give me in two months?"

在几小时或几天内，我们就有了一个可以继续前进的粗略计划。

Within a few hours or days, we have a rough plan from which we can move forward.

制定大计划

Making the Big Plan

大计划的目的是回答“我们应该投资更多吗？”的问题。我们从三个方面来回答这个问题：

The purpose of the big plan is to answer the question "Should we invest more?" We address this question in three ways:

  • 把问题分解成碎片。

  • Break the problem into pieces.

  • 通过估计它们来聚焦这些部分。

  • Bring the pieces into focus by estimating them.

  • 推迟价值较低的部分。

  • Defer less valuable pieces.

从关于系统的对话开始（如果您至少涉及一个其他人，这最有效）。在你说话的时候，写下你的想法，每张索引卡一个。如果您的想法变得过于详细，请停止写作，直到您再次变得抽象为止。

Start with a conversation about the system (this works best if you involve at least one other person). As you talk, write down your thoughts, one per index card. If your thoughts get too detailed, stop writing until you get abstract again.

一些卡片将包含业务功能。这些都是故事。把它们放在一张大桌子的中间。一些卡片将包含与上下文相关的想法——吞吐量、可靠性、预算、满意客户的草图。将这些设置到一侧。

Some cards will contain business functionality. These are stories. Lay these out in the middle of a big table. Some of the cards will contain ideas that are contextthroughput, reliability, budget, sketches of happy customers. Set these to one side.

现在您需要估计每个故事需要您的团队实施多长时间（首先猜测一个大小）。给自己足够的填充。以后会有足够的时间来面对冷酷的现实。暂时沉浸在无限可能的光芒中。

Now you need to estimate how long each story would take your team to implement (just guess at a size at first). Give yourself plenty of padding. There will be plenty of time for stone-cold reality later. Bask in the glow of infinite possibilities for the moment.

如果您的估计太小（例如几天或几周），您就陷入了细节领域。将这些卡片放在一边，然后重新开始。如果你无法想象能够估计一个故事（“易于使用”是典型的例子），把它放在一边。更好的是，考虑一些可以使系统易于使用的特定事物，并将它们转化为故事（例如，“个人资料”）。

If your estimates are too small (like days or weeks), you've slipped into detail land. Put those cards to one side and start over. If you can't imagine being able to estimate a story ("Easy to Use" is the classic example), put it to one side. Better yet, think about some specific things that would make the system easy to use, and turn them into stories (for example, "Personal Profiles").

你只能根据经验来估计。如果没有经验怎么办？那你最好假装。写一个小原型。请教知道的朋友。邀请程序员加入对话。

You can only estimate from experience. What if you don't have any experience? Then you'd better fake it. Write a little prototype. Ask a friend who knows. Invite a programmer into the conversation.

快速移动。您在这里画草图，试图快速捕获整个系统的图片。在您的第一个粗略计划上花费的时间不要超过几个小时。

Move fast. You're sketching here, trying to quickly capture a picture of the whole system. Don't spend more than a few hours on your first rough plan.

什么，我担心？

What, Me Worry?

肯特有一个客户，其商业计划基于一系列与上述故事非常相似的大故事（自然是不同的主题，因为太空旅行似乎有点冒险，即使对风险资本家来说也是如此）。当团队开始实施这些故事时，他们衡量的进度大约为原计划的 40%。

Kent has a client that based its business plan on a set of big stories much like the ones above (different topic, naturally, since space travel seemed a bit dicey, even to venture capitalists). When the team began implementing the stories, they measured their progress at about 40 percent of the original plan.

讲故事的时间

Story Time

唐威尔斯给我们发了这个故事：

Don Wells sent us this story:

这让我想起了我在通用动力公司度过的一段时间。我们试图创造一种车辆，可以在整个欧洲从一个地方自动驾驶到另一个地方，而无需任何人为干预。许多大学也在研究完全相同的问题。

This reminds me of some time I spent at General Dynamics. We were trying to create a vehicle that could drive itself from one place to another all over Europe with no human intervention whatsoever. Many universities were also working on exactly that same problem.

我们的经理来到我的团队，给了我们一些鼓舞，并给我们安排了一年后的约会，让一辆汽车以每小时 10 英里的速度从一个城市自动驾驶到另一个城市。我告诉经理，世界上最优秀的人才已经在麻省理工学院、卡内基梅隆大学和斯坦福大学等机构研究同样的问题多年，但他们在解决这个问题时遇到了严重的麻烦。这位经理在大约一年后被提升为总监，他直视着我的眼睛，毫不退缩地说：“我知道这将是一个挑战，但如果有人能做到，你也能做到。” 结果是每个人大部分时间都找到了其他事情要做。在车辆上做的工作很少。合同给了我们的竞争对手，他们也没有解决问题，

Our manager came to my team and gave us a little pep talk and assigned us a date one year away for having a vehicle drive itself from city to city at 10 miles per hour. I told the manager that the very best minds in the world had already been working on this same problem for years at institutions like MIT, Carnegie-Mellon, and Stanford and they were having serious troubling getting it to work. This manager, who about a year later was promoted to director, looked me straight in the eyes without flinching and said: "I know it's going to be a challenge, but if anyone can do it you can." The result was that everyone found something else to work on most of the time. Very little work was done on the vehicle.
