The contract went to our competitors who had not solved the problem either, but did get their vehicle to follow a painted line on black asphalt around a parking lot at 1 mile per hour.

我们本可以做到这一点，甚至更多，但这不是要求我们做的。鼓舞士气的谈话不能替代每个人都相信的计划。

We could have done that and perhaps more, but that was not what was asked of us. A pep talk is no substitute for a plan that everyone believes in.

令人惊讶的是，这完全没问题！没有人会因为他或她的进度比计划慢而感到高兴，但团队的进展不会让公司面临风险。离得很远。因为他们可以定期展示他们的进步，并且因为他们可以随着市场变化做出反应，投资者和客户相信公司将继续做伟大的事情。实际实现的功能中大约有一半是在最初的计划中，另一半是为响应真实客户而引入或发明的。

Amazingly, this is perfectly okay! Nobody is happy that he or she is going slower than the plan, but the team's progress is not putting the company at risk. Far from it. Because they can demonstrate their progress regularly, and because they can react as the market changes, investors and customers believe the company will continue to do great things. About half the functionality actually implemented was in the original plan, and the other half has been brought in or invented in response to real customers.

必须热爱互联网。完成原计划的 20% 还能让你成为超级巨星吗？

Gotta love the Internet. Where else does accomplishing 20 percent of your original plan make you a superstar?

第 10 章发布计划

Chapter 10. Release Planning

在发布计划中，客户选择几个月的故事，通常集中在公开发布上。

In release planning the customer chooses a few months' worth of stories, typically focusing on a public release.

大计划帮助我们决定投资该项目并非显而易见的愚蠢。现在我们需要将项目与业务同步。我们必须同步项目的两个方面：

The big plan helped us decide that it wasn't patently stupid to invest in the project. Now we need to synchronize the project with the business. We have to synchronize two aspects of the project:

  • 日期

  • Date

  • 范围

  • Scope

通常，项目的重要日期来自公司外部：

Often, important dates for a project come from outside the company:

  • 合同上的日期

  • The date on the contract

  • COMDEX

  • COMDEX

  • 风投的钱什么时候用完

  • When the VC money will run out

即使下一次发布的日期是内部生成的，也会出于业务原因进行设置。您希望经常发布以在竞争中保持领先地位，但如果您发布得太频繁，您将永远没有足够的新功能值得发布新闻稿、新一轮的销售电话或为程序员开香槟。

Even if the date of the next release is internally generated, it will be set for business reasons. You want to release often to stay ahead of your competition, but if you release too often, you won't ever have enough new functionality to merit a press release, a new round of sales calls, or champagne for the programmers.

发布计划将用户故事分配给发布和迭代——我们应该首先做什么？我们以后会做什么？您将使用的策略类似于首先制定大计划：

Release planning allocates user stories to releases and iterationswhat should we work on first? what will we work on later? The strategies you will use are similar to making the big plan in the first place:

  • 将大故事分解成小故事。

  • Break the big stories into smaller stories.

  • 通过估计每个故事需要多长时间来加强对故事的关注。

  • Sharpen the focus on the stories by estimating how long each will take.

  • 推迟不那么有价值的故事，直到剩下的适合可用的时间。

  • Defer less valuable stories until what is left fits in the time available.

谁负责发布计划？

Who Does Release Planning?

发布计划是客户和程序员之间的共同努力。客户推动发布计划，程序员帮助导航。客户选择将哪些故事放在发布中以及稍后实施哪些故事，而程序员则提供进行合理分配所需的估算。

Release planning is a joint effort between the customer and the programmers. The customer drives release planning, and the programmers help navigate. The customer chooses which stories to place in the release and which stories to implement later, while the programmers provide the estimates required to make a sensible allocation.

顾客

The customer

  • 定义用户故事

  • Defines the user stories

  • 决定故事的商业价值

  • Decides what business value the stories have

  • 决定在此版本中构建哪些故事

  • Decides what stories to build in this release

程序员

The programmers

  • 估计构建每个故事需要多长时间

  • Estimate how long it will take to build each story

  • 警告客户重大技术风险

  • Warn the customer about significant technical risks

  • 衡量他们的团队进度，为客户提供总体预算

  • Measure their team progress to provide the customer with an overall budget

发布计划有多稳定？

How Stable Is the Release Plan?

一点也不。

Not at all.

关于计划，我们唯一确定的是开发不会按照计划进行。所以发布计划一直在进行。每当客户改变对需求和优先级的看法时，计划就会随之改变。每当开发人员了解有关做事速度的新知识时，这就会改变计划。

The only thing we know for certain about a plan is that development won't go according to it. So release planning happens all the time. Every time the customer changes his mind about the requirements and his priority, this changes the plan. Every time the developers learn something new about the speed of doing things, this changes the plan.

因此，该计划只是对将要做的事情的当前看法的一个快照。此快照可帮助人们了解会发生什么，但这并不是确定性声明。会经常修改。每个人——开发人员、客户和管理人员——都需要接受不断的变化。

The plan is therefore just a snapshot of the current view of what things will be done. This snapshot helps people get an idea of what to expect, but it is no statement of certainty. It will be revised frequently. Everyonedevelopers, customers, and managementneeds to accept constant change.

您计划提前多长时间？

How Far in Advance Do You Plan?

您提前多长时间制定发布计划？我们知道，我们计划的时间越长，我们的准确性就越低，因此对于未来数年的详细信息毫无意义。我们更喜欢提前计划一两次迭代，提前计划一两次发布。

How far in advance do you build a release plan for? We know that the further ahead we plan, the less accurate we will be, so there's little point going into great detail for years into the future. We prefer to plan one or two iterations in advance and one or two releases in advance.

专注于一两次迭代意味着程序员显然需要知道他们当前正在处理的迭代中有哪些故事。了解下一次迭代中的内容也很有用。除此之外，迭代分配不是那么有用。

Focusing on one or two iterations means that the programmers clearly need to know what stories are in the iteration they are currently working on. It's also useful to know what's in the next iteration. Beyond that the iteration allocation is not so useful.

但是，企业需要知道此版本中当前包含哪些内容，了解之后的版本中将包含哪些内容很有用。

However, the business needs to know what is currently in this release, and it's useful to have an idea of what will be in the release after that.

决定提前多长时间进行计划的真正决定因素是使计划保持最新的成本与当您知道计划本质上不稳定时获得的收益。与计划的波动性相比，您必须诚实地评估价值。

The real decider for how far in advance you should plan is the cost of keeping the plan up-to-date versus the benefit you get when you know that plans are inherently unstable. You have to honestly assess the value compared to the volatility of the plans.

您如何规划基础设施？

How Do You Plan Infrastructure?

当您以面向功能的方式进行规划时，就像我们建议的那样，显而易见的问题是如何处理基础设施。在我们开始构建功能之前，我们必须将分布式对象消息传递基础结构、数据库持久性基础结构和动态 GUI 框架放在一起。这建议了一个计划，在交付任何客户功能之前，您需要花费几个月的时间来构建基础架构组件。

When you plan in a function-oriented way, such as we suggest, the obvious question is how to deal with infrastructure. Before we can start building functionality we have to put together the distributed object messaging infrastructure, the database persistence infrastructure, and the dynamic GUI frameworks. This suggests a plan where you spend several months building the infrastructure components before you deliver any customer functionality.

这种开发风格是我们所见过的已死和垂死项目的共同特征——我们认为这不是巧合。在没有客户功能的情况下做基础设施会导致以下风险：

This style of development is a common feature of the dead and dying projects we've seenand we don't think it's a coincidence. Doing infrastructure without customer function leads to the following risks:

  • 你花了很多时间没有交付对客户有价值的东西，这使与客户的关系变得紧张。

  • You spend a lot of time not delivering things that are valuable to the customer, which strains the relationship with the customer.

  • 你试图让基础设施涵盖你认为可能需要的一切，这导致基础设施过于复杂。

  • You try to make the infrastructure cover everything you think you might need, which leads to an overly complex infrastructure.

因此，在构建功能时改进基础架构。对于每次迭代，只为该迭代中的故事构建足够的基础设施。您不会构建比您需要的更复杂的基础架构，并且客户参与构建基础架构是因为她看到了相关功能的发展。

Therefore, evolve the infrastructure as you build the functionality. For each iteration, build just enough infrastructure for the stories in that iteration. You won't build a more complex infrastructure than you need, and the customer is engaged in building the infrastructure because she sees the dependent functionality as it's evolving.

您如何存储发布计划？

How Do You Store the Release Plan?

我们首选的发布计划形式是一套卡片。每张卡片代表一个用户故事，并包含描述故事内容的基本信息。您将卡片组合在一起以显示此版本中的故事。用粘合剂将故事布置在墙上，或将它们钉在软木板上。用橡皮筋把未来的故事包起来，然后安全地放在抽屉里。

Our preferred form of release plan is a set of cards. Each card represents a user story and contains the essential information to describe what the story is about. You group the cards together to show which stories are in this release. Lay out stories with adhesive on a wall, or pin them up on a cork board. Wrap future stories with a rubber band and stick them safely in a drawer.

我们喜欢卡片，因为它们是简单的物理设备，鼓励每个人操作它们。人们查看和操作存储在计算机中的东西总是有点困难。

We like cards because they are simple, physical devices that encourage everyone to manipulate them. It's always that little bit harder for people to see and manipulate things that are stored in a computer.

然而，如果你想把你的故事放在电脑里，那就去做吧。只需以简单的方式进行即可。一个简单的电子表格通常是最好的。使用复杂项目管理包的人很容易在应该与其他人交流时花时间摆弄包。

However, if you want to put your stories in a computer, go ahead. Just do it in a simple way. A simple spreadsheet often does the job best. People who use complicated project management packages are prone to spending time fiddling with the package when they should be communicating with other people.

许多人使用的另一种计算机格式是 Wiki，这是一种由 Ward Cunningham (c2.com) 发明的协作 Web 工具。团队在 Wiki 灵活的记录故事、任务和状态的格式内迅速发展约定。

Another computer format that many people are using is Wiki, a collaborative Web tool invented by Ward Cunningham (c2.com). Teams rapidly evolve conventions within Wiki's flexible format for recording stories, tasks, and status.

您可以在发布中投入多少？

How Much Can You Put into a Release?

如果你有故事、迭代和发布，你需要知道在每次迭代和发布中你可以做多少故事。我们使用术语速度来表示团队在一次迭代中可以做多少。我们衡量团队的速度并估计每个故事所需的工作量（有关我们如何做的详细信息，请参见第 12 章）。

If you have stories, iterations, and releases, you need to know how many stories you can do in each iteration and release. We use the term velocity to represent how much the team can do in an iteration. We measure the velocity of the team and estimate the amount of effort required for each story (see Chapter 12 for details on how we do this).

你想做的所有工作的努力总和不能超过可用的努力。当您计划迭代时，故事估计的总和不能超过团队的速度。当您计划发布时，故事估计的总和不能超过团队的速度乘以迭代次数。

The sum of the effort for all the work you want to do cannot exceed the available effort. When you are planning an iteration, the sum of the story estimates cannot exceed the team's velocity. When you are planning a release, the sum of the story estimates cannot exceed the team's velocity times the number of iterations.

发布计划章节

Release Planning Chapters

接下来的几章将更详细地讨论发布计划的各种要素。

The next few chapters discuss the various elements of release planning in more detail.

  • 第 11 章讨论如何编写故事，以便将系统的功能分解成有用的块。它还讨论了为什么故事不需要太详细。

  • Chapter 11 discusses how to write stories so that you can break up the features of the system into useful chunks. It also talks about why the stories don't need to be too detailed.

  • 第 12 章讨论了如何估计实现一个故事需要多少时间，以及如何衡量团队的速度。

  • Chapter 12 talks about how to estimate how much time it will take to implement a story and how you can measure the team's velocity.

  • 第 13 章包含有关实现故事的顺序的建议——首先制作高价值的故事，但对技术风险略加关注。

  • Chapter 13 contains advice on the order in which you should implement your storiesdo the high-value stories first but with half an eye on technical risks.

  • 第 14 章讨论了导致您在发布过程中进行更多发布计划的各种事件。

  • Chapter 14 talks about the various events that cause you to do more release planning in the middle of a release.

  • 第 15 章讨论如何提出第一个计划，这个计划总是最难也最不准确。

  • Chapter 15 talks about how to come up with the first plan, which is always both the hardest and the least accurate.

  • 第 16 章讨论了发布计划过程的常见变化。

  • Chapter 16 talks about common variations on the release planning process.

您会注意到，我们首先讨论您如何在项目中期进行计划，然后讨论您如何提出第一个计划。您可能会发现这令人沮丧，因为您可能首先需要一个第一个计划。但是我们注意到，随着连续计划，第一个计划实际上很奇怪。所以 XP 使以后的计划更容易；第一个方案是特例。

You'll notice that we begin by talking about how you plan in the middle of the project and later talk about how you come up with a first plan. You may find this frustrating as you probably will need a first plan first. But we noticed that with continuous planning, the first plan is actually quite an oddity. So XP makes later plans easier; the first plan is a special case.

即使您从第一个计划开始，重要的是要熟悉开始时的计划。一旦您进行了几次迭代，您会发现计划将变得更加容易和准确。如果您对流程的感受有所了解，您可能会发现更容易克服不可避免的初始颠簸。

Even though you start with a first plan, it's important to be familiar with what planning will look like when you get going. You'll find planning will get both easier and more accurate once you have a few iterations under your belt. If you have an idea of how the process should feel, you may find it easier to get over the inevitable initial bumps.

第 11 章写故事

Chapter 11. Writing Stories

“给我讲个故事。”

——每个孩子在某个时候

"Tell a me story."

Every child at some point

故事是 XP 项目中的功能单元。我们通过交付实现故事的经过测试的集成代码来展示进展。一个故事应该对客户和开发人员来说是可以理解的、可测试的、对客户有价值的，并且足够小以便程序员可以在一次迭代中构建六个。

The story is the unit of functionality in an XP project. We demonstate progress by delivering tested, integrated code that implements a story. A story should be understandable to customers and developers, testable, valuable to the customer, and small enough so that the programmers can build half a dozen in an iteration.

用户故事是对客户有价值的一大块功能（有些人使用功能这个词）。它为开发人员和客户提供了一种简单的方法来分割系统需要做的事情，以便系统可以分段交付。

A user story is a chunk of functionality (some people use the word feature) that is of value to the customer. It provides a simple way for developers and customers to chop up what the system needs to do so the system can be delivered in pieces.

强调简单这个词是必不可少的。有许多书籍详细介绍了需求工程、用例设计和类似主题。这些提供了一些有用的想法，但与以往一样，XP 寻找可能可行的最简单方法。因此，当我们看故事时，请记住，重点是让它们太简单而无法工作，希望我们可以摆脱它。

The emphasis on the word simple is essential. There are many books out there that go into great detail about requirements engineering, use case design, and similar topics. These present some useful ideas, but as ever XP looks for the simplest approach that could possibly work. So as we look at stories, remember that the whole point is to make them too simple to work in the hope that we might just get away with it.

好故事的原则

Principles of Good Stories

客户必须能够理解故事。让需求变得如此难以编写和组织是没有好处的，以至于您需要多年的需求工程培训才能理解它们。故事的语言是简单的英语（或任何您当地的语言）。每个人都能说自然语言；其他任何事情都是，嗯，不自然。

Stories must be understandable to the customer. It's no good making the requirements so difficult to write and organize that you need years of training in requirements engineering to be able to understand them. The language for a story is plain English (or whatever your local language is). Everyone can speak natural language; anything else is just, um, unnatural.

我们喜欢在索引卡上写用户故事。卡片使故事简洁明了，也使它们在计划会议期间易于操作。开发人员和客户可以来回传递卡片，将其放在桌子上的特定位置，将其放回甲板上，将其固定在软木板上，等等。操作卡片上的概念比操作打印的项目列表要容易得多。

We like to write user stories on index cards. Cards keep stories terse and also make them easy to manipulate during planning sessions. Developers and customers can pass a card back and forth, put it in a certain location on the table, put it back in the deck, pin it up on a cork board, and so forth. It is much easier to manipulate concepts on cards than it is to manipulate a printed list of items.

（如果您决定将故事放入计算机，请采用可以使用标准打印机卡片纸轻松将它们打印在卡片上的方式。）

(If you're determined to put stories into a computer, do so in such a way that you can easily print them out on cards using standard printer card stock.)

最好的用户故事是描述对客户重要的事情的一两句话。例如：

The best user story is a sentence or two that describes something important to the customer. For example:

系统应检查评论字段中输入的所有单词的拼写。

The system should check the spelling of all words entered in the comments field.

故事越短越好。这个故事代表一个概念，而不是一个详细的规范。用户故事只不过是客户和开发人员将一起讨论功能的协议。如果客户可以在编程时与程序员一起工作，那么就没有必要编写可怕的书面细节。当需要制定迭代计划和构建故事时，您正试图降低出现令人讨厌的意外的可能性。

The shorter the story the better. The story represents a concept and is not a detailed specification. A user story is nothing more than an agreement that the customer and developers will talk together about a feature. Hideous written detail is not necessary if the customer can work with the programmers while they are programming. You are trying to reduce the probability of nasty surprises when the time comes to do the iteration plan and build the story.

这并不是说您不需要所有这些细节。你只是不需要他们都在前面。当您需要构建故事时，您需要更多的细节（参见第 17 章）。但是无论你做什么来让故事更详细，都应该在你需要细节的时候去做。这给您留下了一些不确定性，但我们发现更多的细节并不能避免不确定性，它所做的只是给人一种确定性的错觉——我们认为这更糟。

It's not that you don't need all of those details. You just don't need them all up front. When you need to build the stories, then you need more details (see Chapter 17). But whatever you do to make the story more detailed, do it when you need the details. This leaves you with some uncertainty, but we've found that more detail doesn't ward off uncertainty, all it does is give the illusion of certaintywhich we think is worse.

每个故事都必须为客户提供有价值的东西。如果客户没有从一项活动中获得价值，他为什么要付钱给你去做呢？任何技术基础设施都必须与故事一起构建，并且必须开发以支持故事的需要。这有助于避免项目花费数周或数月时间提供并非真正需要的智能基础设施。

Each story must provide something of value to the customer. If the customer isn't getting value from an activity, why would he want to pay you to do it? Any technical infrastructure must be built in conjunction with the stories and must be developed to support what the stories need. This helps to avoid projects spending weeks or months providing clever infrastructure that isn't really needed.

开发人员不编写用户故事。开发人员想出的任何“好主意”或“精巧的新功能”都不会出现在用户故事中，除非客户同意这个想法是好的，或者功能是精巧的。客户全权负责向团队提供用户故事，任何人都不能篡夺这一责任。欢迎开发人员提出故事建议，但他们应该将大部分注意力放在技术决策上。

Developers do not write user stories. Any "good idea" or "neat new feature" that a developer dreams up will not appear on a user story unless the customer agrees that the idea is good, or that the feature is neat. The customer has the sole responsibility for supplying the team with user stories, and no one can usurp this responsibility. Developers are welcome to suggest stories, but they should spend most of their attention on technical decisions.

关于故事最困难的事情之一就是将它们制作成多大。故事的大小需要使您可以在每次迭代中构建其中的一些故事。这种规模使您能够通过在迭代之间转移故事来进行引导。这也意味着开发人员应该能够估计完成一个故事需要多长时间。如果他们不能，这通常意味着故事需要分解成更小的部分。

One of the hardest things about stories is how big to make them. Stories need to be of a size that you can build a few of them in each iteration. This size gives you the ability to steer by shifting stories between iterations. It also means that the developers should be able to estimate how long it will take to do a story. If they can't, it usually means the story needs to be broken down into smaller parts.

这些故事需要客户和开发人员之间的沟通。客户必须写故事；开发人员然后估计这个故事。为此，双方必须进行协作和沟通。

The stories require communication between the customer and developers. The customer must write the story; the developers then estimate the story. The two parties must collaborate and communicate to do this.

故事应该相互独立。这使我们可以自由地以任何顺序构建它们。这当然是不可能的。但在实践中，我们发现，如果我们假装这是可能的，大多数时候我们就可以侥幸逃脱。我们确实得到了依赖性，但它们很少会导致规划过程出现问题。如果有一种效果会根据故事的完成顺序改变估计值，那么我们可以将其写在卡片上。我们发现我们没有得到很多。

Stories should be independent of each other. This allows us the freedom to build them in any order. This is, of course, impossible. But in practice we find that if we pretend it is possible, most of the time we get away with it. We do get dependencies, but rarely will they cause a problem with the planning process. If there's an effect that would change the estimates depending on what order the stories are done, then we can just write that on the card. We find we don't get many of them.

构建故事后，能够知道它是否有效将很重要。所以每个故事都必须是可测试的。您不必现在就编写测试，但您应该能够弄清楚如何测试故事是否存在。

When the story gets built it will be important to be able to know that it works. So each story must be testable. You don't have to write the test right now, but you should be able to figure out how to test whether the story is there or not.

估算反馈

Feedback from Estimation

在第 12 章中，我们讨论了如何估计一个故事。一旦开始写故事，就应该开始获得估算。您想要这样做的主要原因是为了获得一些关于正确的估算详细程度的反馈。

In Chapter 12 we talk about how you estimate a story. You should start getting estimates as soon as you start writing stories. The main reason you want to do this is to get some feedback as to the right level of detail for estimation.

用户写一个不容易估计的故事是很常见的。例如：

It is very common for a user to write a story that cannot be easily estimated. For example:

用户应该很容易诊断出故障。

It should be easy for the user to diagnose a failure.

这是什么意思？我们如何估计它？因为不知道是什么意思，所以无法估计。因此，我们要求客户解释什么可以使诊断故障变得容易，以及过去使故障诊断变得困难的原因。我们要求客户描述她设想的哪些操作可以简化流程。例如：

What does this mean? How can we estimate it? Because we don't know what it means, we cannot estimate it. Thus we ask the customer to explain what would make diagnosing a failure easy and what has made it hard in the past. We ask the customer to describe what operations she envisions that would make the process easy. For example:

无论系统状态如何，用户都应该能够对启动诊断过程的故障设备的图标执行某些操作。

Regardless of the state of the system, the user should be able to do something to the icon of a failed device that starts the diagnosis process.

客户已经说清楚了几件事。首先，“易于诊断”的真正含义是“易于启动诊断过程”。其次，客户设想屏幕上的设备图标。她还认为用户能够对这些图标进行操作也很重要。这为我们提供了足够的背景来估计故事。

The customer has made several things clear. First, "easy to diagnose" really means "easy to start the diagnosis process." Second, the customer envisions device icons on the screen. She also thinks it's important that the users be able to do things to those icons. This gives us enough context to estimate the story.

程序员不需要无限的细节来进行估算；他们只需要客户将她的需求转化为他们可以采取行动的具体事物。

Programmers don't need infinite detail in order to estimate; they just need the customer to translate her needs into something concrete that they can take action on.

优先考虑用户故事

Prioritizing User Stories

要求高、中、低等故事的绝对排名并没有什么帮助。所有的故事最终都是高调的，否则客户就不会写了，现在是吗？相反，客户需要准备回答“您希望我们先实现什么，我们稍后实现什么？”这个问题。

It doesn't really help to ask for absolute rankings of stories such as high, medium, and low. All the stories end up being high or the customer wouldn't have written them, now would they? Instead, the customer needs to prepare to answer the question "What would you like us to implement first, and what will we implement later?"

故事经常混合优先级。例如：

Stories often mix priorities. For example:

结果必须在 10 秒内显示，并且必须包含发货声明以及所有测量和导出的读数。

Results must be displayed within 10 seconds and must contain the dispatch statement and all measured and derived readings.

客户真正认为故事中最重要的是在 10 秒内出现派遣声明。如果显示测量和导出的读数需要更长的时间，那不是问题。不过在时间紧迫的情况下，客户会发现什么是重要的，什么不是。

What the customer really considers to be of high priority within the story is the appearance of the dispatch statement within 10 seconds. If it takes longer for the measured and derived readings to appear, that's not a problem. Under the press of limited time though, the customer will discover what's important and what isn't.

想要早点找到这种包袱几乎是不可能的。通常发生的情况是，程序员会在迭代计划甚至开发过程中挑战故事中各个元素的优先级。一旦检测到行李，无论何时，都可以拆分故事。

It is almost impossible to find this kind of baggage early on. What usually happens is that the programmers will challenge the priority of individual elements of a story during iteration planning, or even development. Once the baggage is detected, regardless of when, the story can be split.

可追溯性

Traceability

最终，客户将不得不指定验收测试，验收测试的执行将决定用户故事是否已成功实施。因此，所有用户故事都必须是可测试的。程序员和客户都必须同意有具体的测试可以证明用户故事已经成功实施。

Eventually the customer will have to specify acceptance tests whose execution will determine whether the user stories have been successfully implemented. Thus all user stories must be testable. The programmers and the customer alike must agree that there are concrete tests that will demonstrate that the user story has been successfully implemented.

验收测试也是我们对可追溯性的回答。我们认为不值得尝试将需求跟踪到系统中实现需求的类。文书工作太多了。即使您有工具，要使所有信息保持一致仍然需要付出太多努力。相反，我们更喜欢故事和验收测试之间更简单的跟踪。如果验收测试有效，我们可以安全地假设存在一些映射到故事的代码。如果我们稍后以破坏故事的方式更改该代码，那么测试将失败。这是可追溯性的终极体现。

Acceptance testing is also our answer to traceability. We don't think it's worth trying to trace requirements to classes in the system that implement the requirement. That's too much paperwork. Even if you have a tool, it's still too much effort to keep all the information consistent. Instead, we prefer the simpler trace between story and the acceptance tests. If the acceptance tests work, we can safely assume that some code exists that maps to the story. If we change that code later in such a way that breaks the story, then the test will fail. This is the ultimate in traceability.

拆分用户故事

Splitting User Stories

将一个用户故事拆分为两个或多个更小的用户故事是非常常见的。机制很简单：客户将概念分成两个或更多更小的概念，写下新卡片，然后扔掉旧卡片。开发人员然后估计新故事，客户优先考虑它们。

Splitting a user story into two or more smaller user stories is extremely common. The mechanism is simple: The customer divides the concept into two or more smaller concepts, writes the new cards, and throws the old card away. The developers then estimate the new stories, and the customers prioritize them.

调度语句必须在 10 秒内显示。

所有测量和导出的读数必须在 30 秒内显示。

The dispatch statement must be displayed within 10 seconds.

All measured and derived readings must be displayed within 30 seconds.

许多事件都可以触发分裂。

Many events can trigger a split.

  • 当您编写最初的故事时，开发人员可能会说故事太大了。

  • When you're writing the initial stories the developers may say that a story is too large.

  • 当您进行发布计划时，您会发现无法将所有故事都放入一个迭代中。然后您可以拆分故事，以便其中的一部分可以在迭代中完成。

  • When you're doing release planning you find you cannot fit all of a story into an iteration. Then you can split the story so that part of it can be done in the iteration.

  • 当您跟踪迭代时，您会意识到自己有太多事情要做。

  • As you're tracking an iteration you realize you have too much to do.

要拆分故事，客户首先建议拆分。客户应该按照优先顺序进行拆分，将一些不太重要的工作分解出来，可以等到下一次迭代。一旦客户进行了试拆分，开发人员就会将这两个部分作为单独的故事进行估算。

To split a story a customer begins by suggesting a split. The customer should make the split along priority lines, factoring out some less vital work that can wait till the next iteration. Once the customer has made the trial split, the developers then estimate the two parts as if they were separate stories.

当然，这不太可能第一次就成功。如果拆分后优先级较低的部分太小，则客户需要将更多工作转移到优先级较低的部分。如果低优先级的部分太大，客户可能会将一些工作移到高优先级的部分，或者他可以保持原样并将其他工作移入迭代以弥补差异。

Of course, this is not likely to work out just right the first time. If the split leaves the lower-priority part too small, the customer needs to move more work into the lower-priority piece. If the low-priority piece is too big, the customer may move some work to the higher-priority piece or he could leave it as it is and move some other work into the iteration to make up for the difference.

你会在这个问题上来来回回几次，但如果每个人都在房间里，很快就会了解是什么让故事变得美好。

You'll go back and forth a few times on this, but if everyone is in the room together it won't take too long to get a feel for what makes stories good.

用户故事装饰

User Story Adornments

我们更愿意让我们的用户故事保持整洁。它们只包含三部分数据：名称、故事本身和估计。毫无疑问，可以发明其他数据项。可能性的清单几乎是无穷无尽的。但我们建议您不要使用“如果是不是很好”和“如果是可能会很方便”。写在卡片上的整洁故事易于操作，与偶尔缺乏方便数据的成本相比，将节省时间和精力。

We prefer to keep our user stories uncluttered. They contain only three pieces of data: the name, the story itself, and estimates. There is no doubt that other data items could be invented. The list of possibilities is nearly endless. But we recommend that you refrain from "wouldn't it be nice ifs" and "it might be convenient ifs." Uncluttered stories written on a card are easy to manipulate, and will save time and effort compared to the cost of the occasional lack of convenient data.

故事写作过程

The Story Writing Process

编写一本简单的小食谱很有诱惑力，只需 30 分钟即可完成出色的用户故事。这将使您的客户的工作更加轻松。除了我们做不到的那部分——就像你不能写一本伟大的文学故事讲述的食谱一样。我们能做的最好的事情就是告诉你如何发现坏故事，并建议你在摸索的时候花很多时间在客户和程序员之间来回穿梭。

It is tempting to write a simple little cookbook, Great User Stories in Just 30 Minutes. It would make your customer's job much easier. All except that part where we can't do itany more than you can write a cookbook for great literary storytelling. The best we can do is tell you how to spot bad stories and suggest that you spend a lot of time going back and forth between customer and programmer while you're feeling your way.

写故事的过程是反复的，需要大量的反馈。客户会向程序员提出一个故事。程序员会问自己这个故事是否可以测试和估计，它的大小是否合适。如果无法估计故事，程序员会要求客户澄清故事。如果故事太大，开发人员会要求客户拆分故事。

The process of writing stories is iterative, requiring lots of feedback. Customers will propose a story to the programmers. The programmers will ask themselves if the story can be tested and estimated, and if it is of appropriate size. If the story cannot be estimated, the programmers will ask the customer to clarify the story. If the story is too big, the developers will ask the customer to split the story.

故事应该一次写几个。程序员应该和客户坐下来，想出两到五个故事，然后停下来。程序员然后估计这些故事。程序员在估算的时候，肯定会想和客户谈谈细节和问题。所以程序员和客户一直在沟通。

Stories should be written a few at a time. The programmers should sit down with the customer, figure out between two and five stories, and then stop. The programmers then estimate those stories. While the programmers are estimating, they will certainly want to talk to the customer about the details and issues. So the programmers and the customer are in constant communication.

在某些情况下，估计值可能是显而易见的。也许这个故事与其他已经完成的故事相似。在其他情况下，故事可能很难估计，可能需要探索性编程。这种探索很少需要超过一天的时间，并且您应该始终重写您在进行探索性编程时编写的任何代码。

In some cases the estimates may be obvious. Perhaps the story is similar to others that have already been completed. In other cases the story may be very difficult to estimate and may require exploratory programming. Such exploration rarely takes longer than a day, and you should always rewrite any code that you wrote while doing the exploratory programming.

一旦对前几个故事进行了估算，程序员和客户就会更好地理解什么是好故事。系统的形象开始在她脑海中形成。从这个优越的角度来看，客户已准备好编写接下来的几个故事并重复该过程。

Once the first few stories have been estimated, the programmers and the customer will have a better understanding of what makes for good stories. An image of the system is beginning to form in her mind. From this superior viewpoint, the customer is ready to write the next few stories and repeat the process.

不要对你的故事印象太深。写故事不是重点。沟通是重点。我们见过太多的需求文档写下来了却不涉及沟通。

Don't be too impressed with your stories. Writing the stories is not the point. Communicating is the point. We've seen too many requirements documents that are written down but don't involve communication.

你什么时候写完故事？

When Are You Done Writing Stories?

永远不会，或者至少在项目被取消之前不会。软件项目随着时间的推移而增长和变化。虽然故事写作在项目的早期阶段最为丰富，但它永远不会结束。

Never, or at least not until the project is cancelled. Software projects grow and change over time. While story writing will be most prolific during the early phases of the project, it will never end.

您什么时候完成了足够多的用户故事才能开始开发？当客户确定最重要的故事已经确定并且您有足够的故事进行几个月的开发时。应该有足够的故事，以便客户可以做出有意义的选择。

When have you done enough user stories to begin developing? When the customer is certain that the most important stories have been identified and you have enough stories for several months' worth of development. There should be enough stories so the customer can make meaningful choices.

每个人（尤其是在项目开始时）都需要被倾听。如果客户需要写（快速写）两年的故事才能让他感到被倾听，那就这样吧。快速完成它，让故事尽可能大，然后将注意力重新集中在你应该首先处理的事情上，以及必须等待的事情上。

Everyone (especially at the beginning of projects) needs to feel heard. If the customer needs to write (quickly write) two years' worth of stories before he feels listened to, so be it. Get it over with quickly, make the stories as big as possible, then focus back in on what you should work on first, and what will have to wait.

通常项目开始的特点是编写大量的故事，因为您试图对系统的所需功能有一个广泛的了解。故事列表将推动最初的发布计划。

Usually the start of the project is characterized by a lot of story writing as you try to get a broad feel of the desired functionality of the system. The list of stories will drive the initial release plan.

然而，最初的故事只是一个开始。随着项目的进行，故事将一直被添加、删除和拆分。这不仅是正常的；这是XP的重点。目的是在每次发布时交付符合需求的软件，而不是满足在项目开始时被误解的需求。

However the initial stories are only a start. As the project goes on stories will be added, dropped, and split all the time. Not only is this normal; it is the whole point of XP. The aim is to deliver software that matches the requirements at every release, not to match the requirements as they were misunderstood at the beginning of the project.

用户故事的配置

The Disposition of User Stories

一旦用户故事已经实施并且其验收测试正在运行，故事本身就没有进一步的用途。开发团队的成员可能会考虑用故事卡片铺地板或贴墙纸；但丢弃它们可能是最好的选择。请记住，这些故事在验收测试中的编码更加详细和准确，因此即使卡片本身被销毁也不会丢失任何信息。

Once a user story has been implemented and its acceptance tests are running, the story itself serves no further purpose. Members of the development team might think of tiling their floors or papering their walls with story cards; but discarding them is probably the best option. Remember that the stories are encoded in far more detail and accuracy in the acceptance tests, so no information will be lost if the cards themselves are destroyed.

例子

Example

故事

Stories

谈论故事的问题之一是举例。由于客户机密，我们通常不能展示真实项目的示例。这就有点问题了。

One of the problems about talking about stories is giving examples. We can't usually show examples from real projects because of client confidentiality. This presents a bit of a problem.

然而，对于这本书，我们很幸运。肯特在俄勒冈州的农场清理一些树木时遇到了一个倒转时间胶囊。胶囊包含我们在 24 世纪所做的旅行预订项目的项目信息。（或者是“会做”吗？跨时间时态会变得非常混乱。）

For this book, however, we got lucky. Kent was clearing some trees from his farm in Oregon when he came across a reverse time capsule. The capsule contained project information about a travel booking project that we did in the twenty-fourth century. (Or is that "will do"? trans-temporal tense can get very confusing.)

这个时间囊中的东西包括项目的故事卡。

Among the things inside this time capsule were story cards for the project.

查找最低票价。

Find lowest fare.

向客户展示特定路线的十个最低票价。

Present to the customer the ten lowest fares for a particular route.

显示可用航班。

Show available flights.

显示任意两个行星之间可能的飞行（有连接）。

Show possible flights (with connections) between any two planets.

按方便程度对可用航班进行排序。

Sort available flights by convenience.

当您显示航班时，按方便程度对它们进行排序：旅行时间、更改次数、与所需出发时间和到达时间的接近程度。

When you're showing the flights, sort them by convenience: time of journey, number of changes, closeness to desired departure and arrival time.

购票。

Purchase ticket.

购票通过信用卡收费。执行此操作时检查信用卡的有效性。还要检查广泛的移民规则（没有 Oolavoos 去 Traal 等）

Purchase ticket charging to a credit card. Check credit card validity when doing this. Also check broad immigration rules (no Oolavoos to go to Traal etc.)

做客户档案。

Do customer profile.

保留客户详细信息以供快速参考，例如信用卡信息、家庭住址、饮食和重力需求。

Keep customer details for quick reference, for example, credit card info, home address, dietary and gravitational needs.

查看行程。

Review itineraries.

显示客户在系统中的所有行程。

Show all itineraries the customer has in the system.

取消行程。

Cancel itinerary.

如果客户取消行程，取消所有航班、酒店等。

If a customer cancels an itinerary, cancel all flights, hotels, etc.

打印移民文件。

Print immigration paperwork.

打印离开和到达行星所需的文书工作——仅适用于较容易的行星（例如，不是 Vogon）。

Print paperwork required to leave and arrive at a planetonly for the easier planets (e.g., not Vogon).

显示酒店。

Show hotels.

显示某个地点附近的酒店。

Show hotels near a place.

显示酒店可用性。

Show hotel availability.

显示在行程指定的时间段内可用的酒店。

Show hotels that are available for the period indicated by the itinerary.

提供完善的酒店搜索。

Offer sophisticated hotel search.

允许客户使用多个日期和位置搜索酒店。这将包括设施、服务水平、成本和建议。

Allow customer to search for hotels using more than dates and location. This would include facilities, level of service, costs, and recommendations.

预订酒店。

Book a photel.

预定一间旅馆。向信用卡收费并检查信用卡的有效性。

Book a hotel. Charge to credit card and check credit card validity.

提供酒店/太空线计划。

Provide hotel/spaceline programs.

显示与客户正在使用的空间线有联合销售协议的酒店。显示价格，包括这些计划提供的折扣——仅适用于现阶段积极与我们合作的 spacelines。

Show hotels that have joint sales agreements with the spaceline the customer is using. Show the prices including the discounts that are available with these programsonly for spacelines that are actively collaborating with us at this stage.

提供飞机租赁服务。

Offer airplane hire.

允许客户在他或她在星球上时租用飞机。链接太空飞行中的日期。增强客户档案以包括飞机偏好（保险选择、手动与自动等）

Allow the customer to hire an airplane while he or she is on a planet. Link the dates in from the space flight. Enhance the customer profile to include airplane preferences (insurance selection, manual versus automatic, etc.)

这些故事通过示例展示了我们目前讨论的原则。每一个都很短，短到不能作为编程的详细规范。然而，他们提供了足够的信息来提供共同的期望。对于任何使用过基于 Web 的旅行预订系统的人来说，这些故事确实很好地描述了每个阶段的需求。对于没有这种背景的人，您可能需要更多的信息，但在这个阶段我们仍然应该避免太详细。

The stories show by example the principles we've discussed so far. Each one is short, too short to act as a detailed specification for programming. However, they give enough information to provide a common expectation. For anyone who has used a Web-based travel reservation system, the stories do give a good picture of what is needed at each stage. For people without that background, you may well need a little more information, but we should still avoid great detail at this stage.

请注意根本没有讨论依赖关系。您可能会争辩说，要“提供复杂的酒店搜索”，您需要执行“显示酒店可用性”。你处理它们的顺序可能会影响估计。但基本上我们不担心它。如果顺序确实对估计产生重大影响，并且对计划过程有影响，那么一个简单的注释就可以解决问题。

Notice how there is no discussion at all of dependencies. You could well argue that to "Offer sophisticated hotel search" you would need to do "Show hotel availability." The order in which you tackle them might affect the estimates. But essentially we don't worry about it. If order does make a significant difference to the estimates, and that has an effect on the planning process, then a simple note will do the trick.

第 12 章估计

Chapter 12. Estimation

根据您已经完成的类似故事来估算您的故事。这个故事将花费与可比故事大致相同的时间。

Base your story estimates on a similar story you've already done. This story will take about the same amount of time as a comparable story.

您如何得出估算值？我们已经看到很多专门讨论这个话题的词。我们已经看到了很多数学公式。其中最好的是基于尚未编写的代码行。这些可以告诉你开发这么多几千行代码需要多少时间。这特别有用，因为在开始编写解决方案之前很容易准确地估计出解决方案需要多少行代码。（发现讽刺了吗？）

How do you come up with estimates? We've seen a lot of words devoted to this topic. We've seen quite a few mathematical formulae. The best of these are based on the lines of code yet to be written. These can tell you how much time it will take to develop so many thousand lines of code. This is particularly useful since it's so easy to estimate precisely how many lines of code a solution will require before you start writing it. (Spotted the sarcasm yet?)

让我们明确一点，估算充其量是一门艺术。无论您多么努力，您都不会获得准确的数字。然而，只要稍加努力，您就可以获得足够好的数字，并且随着时间的推移，您可以获得更好的数字。

Let's be clear, estimation is an art at best. You're not going to get accurate figures however hard you try. With a little bit of effort you can, however, get good enough numbers, and you can get better numbers over time.

有效估算的三个关键：

There are three keys to effective estimation:

  • 把事情简单化。

  • Keep it simple.

  • 使用过去发生的事情。

  • Use what happened in the past.

  • 从经验中学习。

  • Learn from experience.

估计未来的最佳指南是寻找过去发生的与未来大致相同的事情。那么假设历史会重演。它经常发生。如果当时和现在之间存在显着差异，则使用一种非常简单的方法将其考虑在内。不要试图过于复杂；无论您多么努力，估计都只能是近似值。

The best guide to estimating the future is to look for something that happened in the past that was about the same as the future thing. Then just assume that history will repeat itself. It often does. If there's a significant difference between then and now, then use a very simple way to factor it in. Don't try to be too sophisticated; estimates will never be anything other than approximate, however hard you try.

估计故事的大小

Estimating the Size of a Story

估算故事大小的一种简单有效的方法是查找您已经发布的类似故事。然后查看您的记录，了解构建所需的时间。然后假设新故事将花费相同的努力。“哦，又是一份报告。报告总是需要我们一周的时间。”

A simple, effective way to estimate the size of a story is to look for a similar story that you've already delivered. Then look at your records to see how long it took to build. Then assume the new story will take the same amount of effort. "Oh, another report. Reports always take us a week."

如果找不到大小相同的故事，请寻找一半大或两倍大的故事。适当乘或除。不要担心 Martin 可能因为他不幸的习惯在本应除法的时候乘以 2 而未能在他的 Further Maths A level 中获得 A。你比他聪明得多。

If you can't find a story that is the same size, look for something half as big or twice as big. Multiply or divide as appropriate. Do not worry that Martin probably failed to get an A in his Further Maths A level because of his unfortunate habit of multiplying by two when he should have divided. You're a lot cleverer than he is.

你用什么单位来表达估计实际上并不重要。唯一重要的是你总是使用相同的单位。在本书中，我们使用理想周。理想周数是如果程序员可以将 100% 的时间投入到故事中，则该故事将需要实施的人周数。

It doesn't actually matter what units you express the estimate in. The only important thing is that you always use the same unit. In this book we use ideal weeks. Ideal weeks are the number of person weeks that the story would take to implement if the programmers could dedicate 100 percent of their time to it.

（你会注意到这种方法的一个小缺陷。当你还没有构建任何东西并且没有任何东西可以与之比较时，你如何估计？请参阅第 15 章以了解对这个问题的完全不满意的解决方案。）

(You'll notice a slight flaw in this approach. How do you estimate when you haven't built anything yet and you don't have anything to compare it to? See Chapter 15 for a thoroughly unsatisfactory solution to this problem.)

估计是一个团队的努力。团队讨论故事，考虑实施可能需要多长时间，然后做出估算。团队成员可能不同意估计。有些人可能认为这个故事很难，需要很长时间才能发展。其他人可能认为这很容易并且需要很短的时间来开发。我们遵循“乐观取胜”的规则。也就是说，如果经过合理的讨论，分歧仍然存在，我们选择最短的估计。

Estimation is a team effort. The team discusses the story, considers how long it may take to implement, and decides upon an estimate. The team members may disagree regarding the estimate. Some may think the story is hard and will take a long time to develop. Others may think it is easy and will take a short time to develop. We follow the rule "Optimism wins." That is, if after reasonable discussion the disagreement persists, we choose the shortest estimate.

请记住，估算不是承诺。一些错误的估计并不是灾难。我们的目标是不断提高我们的估算能力。通过选择最乐观的估计，我们完成了两件事：我们在估计中保持紧张，这样它们就不会长得可怕；我们在团队中保持紧张，这样团队就不会过于乐观。曾经因乐观情绪而伤及团队的团队成员将学会缓和这种乐观情绪。

Remember, estimates are not commitments. And a couple of bad estimates are not disasters. What we are aiming for is to continuously improve our ability to make estimates. By choosing the most optimistic estimate we accomplish two things: We keep tension in the estimates so that they don't grow hideously long, and we keep tension in the team so that the team learns not to be too optimistic. Team members whose optimism burned the team once will learn to temper that optimism.

另一个让很多人担心的问题是故事之间的依赖关系。正如我们在第 13 章中所说，您几乎可以忽略依赖性。但是，大多数并不意味着总是。在某些情况下，您会说“用 flooping the thingummy 需要六周时间，但如果我们在 bubble the foobar 之后再做，则只需要四个星期。” 在这种情况下，根据其位置使用适当的数字进行 flooping 并记下假设。你将只有其中的一些。

Another issue that worries many people is dependencies between the stories. As we say in Chapter 13, you can mostly ignore dependencies. However, mostly doesn't mean always. You will get some cases where you say "Flooping the thingummy will take six weeks, but if we do it after we burble the foobar it'll take only four weeks." In this case use the appropriate number for flooping depending on its position and make a note of the assumption. You will have only a few of these.

您将定期重新评估每个故事，这使您有机会合并其他信息，例如已删除的依赖项或结果证明困难（或我们认为容易）的技术。

Periodically you will reestimate every story, which gives you a chance to incorporate additional information such as dependencies that have been erased or technologies that turn out to be difficult (or easy, we suppose).

估计在一次迭代中你能做多少

Estimating How Much You Can Do in an Iteration

您可以将每次迭代视为一个盒子，每个盒子可以容纳有限数量的酒瓶。对任何品酒师来说，关键问题是一个盒子里能装多少瓶酒？你可以测量盒子、瓶子并做一些几何分析，你可以组成一个由权威人士组成的委员会，或者你可以试试看。

You can think of each iteration as a box, each of which can hold a limited number of wine bottles. The key question to any oenophile is how many bottles can you fit in a box? You could measure the box, measure the bottles and do some geometric analysis, you could form a committee of august persons, or you could just try it and see.

我们使用后一种方法：昨天的天气。在每次迭代结束时，我们测量完成了多少工作，并假设这次我们将完成相同的工作。然而，当我们谈到昨天的天气时，我们只是谈到了总的原则。要将其应用于发布计划，我们需要弄清楚如何衡量这些东西。我们可以只计算我们所做的故事的数量，但并非所有故事的大小都相同。

We use the latter approach: Yesterday's Weather. At the end of each iteration we measure how much stuff got done and assume we'll get the same work done this time. However, when we talked about Yesterday's Weather, we just talked about the general principle. To apply it to release planning we need to figure out how to measure the stuff. We could just count the number of stories we do, but not all stories are the same size.

所以我们必须衡量每个故事的大小。在每次迭代结束时，我们会查看所有已完成的故事，并记录完成每个故事所需的理想时间有多少周。然后我们将所有故事中的所有理想时间相加，这告诉我们每次迭代中有多少理想时间。

So we have to measure the size of each story. At the end of each iteration we look at all the stories that got done, and we record how many weeks of ideal time it took to do each story. We then add up all the ideal time in all the stories, and that tells us how much ideal time there is in each iteration.

遵循这个简单的规则违反了项目管理的格言之一：工作会扩展以填充可用空间。这对于某些活动来说可能是正确的，但是当您拥有积极主动且有能力的软件开发人员时，情况就不是这样了。

Following this simple rule violates one of the dictums of project management: Work expands to fill the available space. That may be true for some activities, but it isn't true when you have motivated and capabable software developers.

谨慎调整速度以应对团队规模的变化。正如我们在第 7 章中讨论的那样，改变团队的组成会对速度产生非线性和延迟的影响。不要预测效果；测量它。预测增加人员的效果特别困难，因为您很少知道新人员需要多长时间才能开始提供帮助。

Be wary of adjusting velocity to cope with changes in a team's size. As we discussed in Chapter 7, changing the composition of a team has a nonlinear and delayed effect on velocity. Don't predict the effect; measure it. Predicting the effect of adding people is particularly difficult, because you rarely know how long it will take for the new people to begin helping.

我们还为个人开发人员使用速度。我们可以说一个程序员的速度是 5 天的理想时间。这意味着该程序员可以在每次迭代中注册 5 个理想的工作日。大多数开发人员将具有相同的速度。但是，兼职工作的人或团队的新人的速度会较低。

We also use velocity for individual developers. We might say that one programmer has a velocity of 5 ideal days. That means that that programmer can sign up for 5 ideal days of work in each iteration. Most developers will have the same velocity. However, someone working parttime, or someone who is new to the team, will have a lower velocity.

你必须小心，不要给速度赋予太多意义。假设您有两个规模相同、迭代长度相同但速度不同的团队。这是什么意思？

You have to be careful not to attach too much meaning to velocity. Say you have two teams of the same size with the same iteration lengths but different velocities. What does this mean?

答案是各种各样的事情纠缠在一起。这可能意味着一个团队更有才华，或者一个团队拥有更好的工具。但这也可能意味着一个团队倾向于使用比另一个团队更乐观的估计，并且需要更小的速度来补偿。最后，所有这些关于理想时间的东西都是一种万能的软糖，以弥补估计软件开发的困难。

The answer is all sorts of things tangled up together. It might mean one team is more talented or that one team had better tools. But it might also mean that one team tended to use more optimistic estimates than the other and needed a smaller velocity to compensate. In the end, all of this stuff about ideal time is one almighty fudge to compensate for the difficulty of estimating software development.

理想时间的意义

The Meaning of Ideal Time

在 XP 社区中已经有很多关于我们应该使用哪些工作量单位的讨论。

There's been a fair bit of discussion in the XP community about what units of effort we should use.

在许多方面，最简单的单位是基于日历时间的日历工作量。

In many ways, the simplest unit would be calendar effort, which is based on calendar time.

日历时间是熟悉的时间流逝，经过修改以处理工作日。如果您在周一至周五工作，那么 4 个日历周等于 20 个日历日。

Calendar time is the familiar passage of time, modified to handle working days. If you are working Mondays to Fridays, then four calendar weeks is equal to 20 calendar days.

日历工作量是人数乘以日历时间。一个六人团队每个日历周有 30 个日历开发日的工作时间。在四个星期内，他们将有 24 个日历开发周可用。如果团队中有一个人半职工作，那么在同样的四个星期内，团队将有 22 个日历开发周的工作时间。

Calendar effort is the number of people times calendar time. A team of six people has 30 calendar development days of effort available per calendar week. In four weeks they would have 24 calendar development weeks of effort available. If one person on the team worked half-time, the team would have 22 calendar development weeks of effort available in that same four-week period.

大多数人根据日历工作量来衡量所有任务。这是有道理的，因为它很容易衡量。但是，它使估计变得更加困难。如果您认为人们以合理的效率工作，那么估算就会简单得多。通常这意味着他们不会被打扰和分心。从长远来看，分心往往会趋于平衡，但会在一两周的短时间内产生重大影响。因此，它们确实把历史数据弄得一团糟，而这是一个好的估算系统的支柱。

Most people measure all tasks in terms of calendar effort. This makes sense because it's easy to measure. However, it makes estimating harder. Estimating is much simpler if you think of people as working at reasonable efficiency. Typically this means they don't get interrupted and distracted. Distractions tend to even out over the long haul but can have a big effect in short periods of a week or two. As such they really make a mess of historical data, which is the backbone of a good estimation system.

所以在XP中我们提出了第二种时间：理想时间。理想的时间是不受打扰的时间，您可以专注于自己的工作，并且感觉工作效率很高。我们使用理想时间来衡量和估计，因为这使我们能够比较任务而不用担心中断。如果我们查看一项任务，发现它与上周耗时理想两天的任务一样复杂，我们可以估计本周将耗费两天理想时间。经过的时间可能会有很大不同，但这是我们单独监控的内容。

So in XP we come up with a second kind of time: ideal time.Ideal time is time without interruption where you can concentrate on your work and you feel fully productive. We measure and estimate using ideal time, because that allows us to compare tasks without worrying about interruptions. If we look at a task and see it is about as complicated as one that took two ideal days last week, we can estimate it will take two ideal days this week. The elapsed time could well be very different, but that is something we monitor separately.

我们使用术语“理想时间”，但实际上它是理想的努力。一个六人团队每周可能有 10 个理想的开发日。通常，当人们谈论任务长度时，他们会说，“这将需要三天的理想时间。” 他们真正的意思是需要“三个理想的开发日”，但这太啰嗦了。

We use the term "ideal time," but really it's ideal effort. A team of six people might have ten ideal development days of effort available a week. Typically when people talk of task lengths they say, "That'll take three ideal days." What they really mean is that it will take "three ideal development days," but that's too much of a mouthful.

理想时间的概念与时间关系不大。事实上，有些人喜欢使用故事点数、任务点数或软糖熊之类的东西来衡量故事和任务的工作量。这是可行的，因为唯一重要的是，您对过去测量的实际故事使用的单位与今天用于估算的单位相同。

The notion of ideal time has little to do with time. Indeed some people like to use something like story points, task points, or Gummi Bears to measure the effort for stories and tasks. This works because the only important thing is that you use the same unit for the actual stories you measured in the past as you use for your estimates today.

（Francesco Cirillo 告诉我们他买了一个番茄形状的半小时厨房计时器，所以他们现在指的是“六个番茄任务”。）

(Francesco Cirillo told us he bought a half-hour kitchen timer in the shape of a tomato, so they now refer to a "six-tomato task.")

我们喜欢使用理想周，因为这个概念与熟悉的事物有一些对应，但理想这个词提醒我们事情并不完美。它还可以帮助您尽早制定第一个计划（第 15 章）。

We like using ideal weeks because the concept has some correspondence to the familiar, yet the word ideal is there to remind us that things aren't perfect. It also can help early on when doing your first plan (Chapter 15).

理想时间是您花在您已承担责任的任务上的时间。理想时间不包括你花在帮助别人上的时间，比如结对编程。您可能认为您需要明确考虑花费在编程之外的时间，但事实证明昨天的天气会跟踪您在自己的任务上花费的时间。

Ideal time is the time you spend on tasks you have accepted responsibility for. Ideal time doesn't include time you spend helping someone else, such as pair programming. You might think you need to take explicit account of time spent not programming, but it turns out Yesterday's Weather takes care of tracking how much time you spend on your own tasks.

（如果你读过一些关于 XP 的旧东西，你会遇到术语负载因子。负载因子是迭代中的日历工作量与速度的比率。所以一个有五个人的团队使用两周的迭代已经十个过去了每个迭代的编程周数。如果团队的速度为 4，那么团队的负载因子为 2.5 (10/4)。我们过去常常在计划中使用负载因子，但从那以后我们了解到只使用速度更容易.)

(If you've read some older stuff on XP you'll come across the term load factor.Load factor is the ratio of the calendar effort in an iteration to velocity. So a team with five people using two-week iterations has ten elapsed programming weeks per iteration. If the team's velocity is four then the team has a load factor of 2.5 (10/4). We used to use load factor a lot in planning, but since then we have learned that it's easier to just use velocity.)

改进你的估计

Improving Your Estimates

关于估计过程的好消息是它趋于改进。当你做的越频繁，当你建立越多的准确数据时，团队中的每个人都会变得更擅长估算。鼓励这个过程。不要对早期估计抱有太大期望，但要期待它们会有所改善。

The good news about the estimation process is that it tends to improve. As you do it more often, as you build up more acutal figures, everyone on the team gets better at estimation. Encourage this process. Don't expect too much of early estimates, but do expect them to improve.

为此，您需要跟踪您的实际情况。确保记录下完成一个故事所花费的时间。记录不应该比你的计划精度更精确，所以估计到最接近的理想周就可以了。建立一套良好的实际情况对于改进规划过程至关重要。

For this to work you need to track your actuals. Make sure you record how long it took to do a story. The record shouldn't be any more precise than your planning precision, so estimating to the nearest ideal week will be fine. Building up a good set of actuals is essential to improving the planning process.

第 13 章故事排序

Chapter 13. Ordering the Stories

首先要做的最重要的故事是那些包含最高商业价值的故事。谨防基于技术依赖性的故事排序。大多数情况下，依赖项不如值重要。

The most important stories to do first are the ones that contain the highest business value. Beware of sequencing stories based on technical dependencies. Most of the time the dependencies are less important than the value.

计划的关键部分之一是决定你应该按什么顺序做事。永远不会缺少要做的事情。我们今天应该做什么？

One of the key parts of planning is deciding in what order you should do things. There is never any shortage of things to do. What should we do today?

有时软件太复杂了，所以让我们考虑一些既平凡又重要的东西。在烹饪中，您可以通过查看食谱中的时间和顺序来回答这个问题。通常会涉及到相当严格的顺序：在放入鸡肉之前，您必须将洋葱炸成金黄色。

Sometimes software is just too complicated, so instead let's consider something that is both more mundane and more essential. In cooking you answer this question by looking at the timing and sequencing in the recipe. Often there is quite a strong ordering involved: You have to fry the onions golden before you put in the chicken.

这种排序的概念是大多数规划的主要方面。在大型工程项目中，这就是导致依赖性分析和 PERT 图实践的原因。任务之间的依赖关系支配着计划。如果您选择接受它，您的任务就是找到浏览依赖项的最佳方法。

This notion of ordering is the dominant aspect of most kinds of planning. On big engineering projects this is what leads to the practice of dependency analysis and PERT charts. Dependencies between tasks dominate planning. Your mission, should you choose to accept it, is to find the best way of navigating through the dependencies.

要以这种方式进行计划，您需要列出任务列表并捕获活动之间的依赖关系。通过查看这些并查看活动的持续时间，您可以找出关键路径上的关键活动，延迟将影响整个项目。如果您学习项目管理课程，您通常会花费大量时间进行此类分析，以及资源均衡等主题。您很可能会使用计算机工具来帮助处理所有这些问题。

To plan in this style you need to lay out a list of tasks and capture the dependencies between the activities. By looking at these and looking at the duration of the activities you can figure out the key activities on the critical path where a delay will affect the whole project. If you do a course on project management you'll usually spend a good bit of time on this kind of analysis, together with such topics as resource leveling. You may well use a computer tool to help deal with all of this.

所有这些技术在 XP 项目中都几乎没有用。它们是无用的，因为任务之间的依赖关系并不强烈，因为强调最小的技术承诺和设计的不断增长。大多数时候故事之间没有必要的顺序。您可以按照您喜欢的任何顺序构建它们。我们没有这方面的证据，但是，像大多数软件专家一样，这从未阻止我们做出勇敢的断言。我们的证据很简单，几乎每次有人提出排序约束时，我们都可以将其否决。

All of these techniques are pretty much useless on an XP project. They are useless because dependencies between tasks do not figure strongly, because of the emphasis on minimal technical commitment and constant growth in the design. Most of the time there is no necessary ordering between the stories. You can build them in any order you like. We don't have proof of this, but, like most software pundits, that never stopped us from making a brave assertion. Our evidence is simply that nearly every time someone comes up with an ordering constraint, we can shoot it down.

一个很好的例子是 Martin 为工厂系统进行成本分析时遇到的一个项目。成本模型很复杂而且很新，所以没有被很好地理解。他们在大量数据上运行。项目团队推断，由于模型需要数据，因此需要首先编写输入数据的软件。这意味着要构建大量用于输入和验证数据的 GUI 屏幕。

A good example is a project Martin ran into for doing costing analysis for a factory system. The cost models were complicated and very new, so they were not well understood. They ran on a large amount of data. The project team reasoned that since the models needed the data, the software to enter the data needed to be written first. This meant building a lot of GUI screens for entering and validating the data.

那是一种错误的依赖。可以使用原始 SQL 将数据放入数据库中。这种方法可以让他们使用成本核算模型并弄清楚模型的真正含义。在更好地理解模型之前，他们不知道需要什么数据。运行模型毕竟是应用程序的重点，数据仅用于为模型服务。

That was a false dependency. The data could have been put into the database using raw SQL. This method would have allowed them to work with the costing models and figure out what the models were really about. Until they understood the models better, they didn't know what data they needed. Running the models was the point of the application after all, the data was there only to serve the models.

大多数排序依赖项都是错误的。当然，大多数不是全部。在您确实获得依赖性的情况下，它们很容易根据具体情况进行处理，无论是在您可以控制的迭代中还是通过在中途修改估计。它们不会对整体计划产生太大影响。

Most ordering dependencies are false. Of course, most isn't all. The cases where you do get dependencies, they are easy to deal with on a case by case basis, either inside an iteration where you have control or by modifying estimates midstream. They don't affect the overall plan much.

一个合乎逻辑但天真的读者会认为这种缺乏约束是一种好处。但通常情况并非如此。相反，我们看到人们正在寻找依赖关系，并且下定决心要找到它们，以至于他们找到了不存在的依赖关系。毕竟，如果没有顺序约束，我们如何选择以什么顺序做事呢？

A logical, yet na¨ive, reader would see this lack of constraints as a benefit. But often it isn't. Instead, we see people who are looking for dependencies and are so determined to find them that they find dependencies that don't exist. After all, if there is no ordering constraint, how do we choose in what order to do things?

商业价值

Business Value

所以我们需要不同的因素来做出选择。首先是商业价值。先做那些能给客户带来最大利益的故事。这似乎很明显，我们几乎觉得没有必要指出原因。但以防万一，我们还是会这样做。

So we need different factors for making our choice. The first of these is business value. Do those stories first that yield the most benefit to the customers. This seems so obvious that we hardly feel the need to point out why. But just in case, we'll do it anyway.

我们希望尽快向客户发布。我们希望此版本对客户尽可能有价值。这样客户就会喜欢我们并不断给我们喂饼干。所以我们给她她最想要的东西。这样我们就可以快速发布，客户也能感受到好处。如果一切都在计划的最后失败了，那也没关系，因为有风险的故事不如我们已经完成的故事重要。

We want to get a release to the customer as soon as possible. We want this release to be as valuable to the customer as possible. That way the customer will like us and keep feeding us cookies. So we give her the things she wants most. That way we can release quickly and the customer feels the benefit. Should everything go to pot at the end of the schedule, it's okay, because the stories at risk are less important than the stories we have already completed.

即使我们不能快速发布，如果我们先做最有价值的事情，客户也会更开心。这表明我们在倾听，并且真的在努力解决她的问题。一旦她看到出现的内容的价值，它也可能会促使客户选择更早的版本。早期发布会吓到做原型的人，因为原型不是生产质量。但 XP 从不构建任何它不能引以为豪的东西，因此我们可以随时交付。

Even if we can't release quickly, the customer will be happier if we do the most valuable things first. It shows we are listening, and really trying to solve her problems. It also may prompt the customer to go for an earlier release once she sees the value of what appears. Early releases scare people who do prototyping, because prototypes aren't production quality. But XP never builds anything it can't be proud of, so we can deliver at any moment.

我们如何衡量故事的商业价值？简短的回答是我们没有。也就是说，开发人员和项目经理不需要。确定业务价值完全属于业务人员的范围。这是他们的事；他们知道价值是什么。至少，他们比我们更有能力猜测。如果他们错了，好吧，他们正在为此付出代价。如果你有足够的钱，你就有权犯错。开发人员可以提出替代方案并提出问题。但最终，商业价值始终是商业电话。

How do we measure the business value of a story? The short answer is that we don't; that is, the developers and project managers don't. Determining business value is a decision entirely within the realm of the business people. It's their business; they know what the value is. At least, they are better positioned to guess than we are. If they're wrong, well, they're paying for it. If you have enough dollars you have the right to be wrong. The developers can suggest alternatives and ask questions. But in the end business value is always a business call.

你应该多仔细地计算出故事的价值？你不需要把它换成美元；事实上，通常根本不值得尝试用美元来衡量它的价值。相对值才是最重要的，你只需要对相对性有一个粗略的了解。

How carefully should you figure out the value of stories? You don't need to get it to the dollar; indeed, it usually isn't worth trying to put a dollar value on it at all. The relative values are what counts, and you need only a rough sense of the relativity.

这足以开始。在执行发布计划时，您会将故事分配到迭代中，这将导致更好地确定业务价值。但为了做到这一点，企业需要更多信息。

This is enough to start with. As you play out the release plan, you'll allocate the stories into iterations, and that will lead to a finer determination of business value. But in order to do that the business needs some more information.

想象一下，您正站在垂涎多年的新车前。终于，老旧的垃圾堆扔了一根棍子，你可以用一年的新车气味来奖励自己。您正在敲定交易，推销员问道：“先生，您想要那个可选的天窗吗？” 你怎么回答？

Imagine you're standing in front of the new car that you've been salivating over for years. Finally the old heap has thrown a rod and you can reward yourself with a year of that new car smell. You're finalizing the deal and the salesman asks, "Would you like the optional sunroof with that, sir?" What do you answer?

除非你非常便宜或非常富有（或者非常反对新鲜空气），否则你会想要一条信息：漫游者的那个窗户多少钱？如果成本是 10 美元，你可能会接受。如果是 10,000 美元，您可能会通过。但如果范围那么大，不考虑成本就无法决定。

Unless you're either incredibly cheap or incredibly rich (or incredibly against fresh air) you'll want one piece of information: How much is that window in the Rover? If the cost is $10 you'd probably take it. If it's $10,000 you'll probably pass. But if the range is that big, you can't decide without the cost.

对于大多数软件来说，范围就这么大。

For most software, the range is that big.

那么谁来分配成本呢？开发人员陈述成本，他们通过估计需要付出多少努力来陈述成本（参见第 12 章）。

So who gets to allocate the cost? Developers state the cost, and they state it by estimating how much effort it will take (see Chapter 12).

技术风险

Technical Risk

当开发人员查看故事时，他们将不可避免地开始考虑如何构建它们。当他们这样做的时候，他们会有各种各样的感受，从“没问题”到“做不到”。这些感受很重要，因为它们是项目可能偏离轨道的表现。当开发人员感到紧张时，每个人都应该倾听。

As the developers look at the stories they will inevitably start thinking about how they will build them. As they do this they will run the gamut of feelings, all the way from "no problem" to "can't be done." These feelings are important, because they are the manifestation of where the project could go off the rails. When developers feel nervous, everyone should listen.

紧张来自多个方面：

The nervousness comes from a number of sources:

  • 开发人员可能不确定他们能否将故事估计到所需的精度。

  • The developers may not be confident that they can estimate the story to the required precision.

  • 故事可能依赖于不受信任的第三方软件。

  • A story may depend on an untrusted third-party piece of software.

  • 开发人员可能不知道如何使整个系统足够快以应对未来的负载。

  • The developers may not know how to make the whole system fast enough for future loads.

  • 开发人员今天可能不知道如何设计，因此可以在不重新设计大部分系统的情况下添加预期的功能。

  • The developers may not know how to design today so an expected feature can be added without reworking most of the system.

一般来说，程序员都想先做高风险的故事。这样，如果出现问题，您会在还有时间处理时及早发现。

In general, programmers want to do higher-risk stories first. That way, if something goes wrong, you find out early while you still have time to deal with it.

两者之间的谈判

Negotiating Between the Two

你注意到我们有两个不同的标准，由两组不同的人设定。我们如何解决他们两个？程序员希望首先处理高风险的故事，而客户希望首先处理高价值的故事。很多时候必须解决这些相互冲突的优先事项。

You notice we have two different criteria set by two different groups of people. How do we resolve the two of them? Programmers want to tackle high-risk stories first, and customers want to tackle high-value stories first. There are plenty of times when these conflicting priorities have to be resolved.

企业应该对故事进行排序。商界人士了解估算中的不确定性。他们在财务预测方面一直面临风险。他们还了解在返工成为问题的情况下返工的成本。如果他们现在想冒险以获得更好的价值，那真的是他们的决定。程序员的任务是让风险可见，而不是为客户做出决定。

Business should sequence stories. Business people understand uncertainty in estimates. They face risk all the time with financial projections. They also understand the cost of reworking in the cases where reworking is an issue. If they wish to run a risk in order to get better value now, it is really their call. It is the programmers' task to make the risk visible, not to make the decision for the customer.

虽然这种安排是理想的，但有时您需要一些额外的东西才能使其发挥作用，也许允许开发人员在每次迭代中选择一定数量的故事，以便他们可以将风险提前。

While this arrangement is the ideal, sometimes you need something extra to make it work, perhaps allowing developers to choose a certain amount of stories per iteration so that they can bring the risk forward.

我们需要强调的是，您不必过分担心返工问题。XP 的做法都是为了将​​返工成本降低到可管理的水平。如果您发现自己处于返工成本过高的境地，那么您要么不使用 XP，要么应该使用使返工更容易的环境。

We need to stress that you shouldn't worry too much about the issue of reworking. XP's practices are all about reducing the cost of reworking to manageable levels. If you find yourself in a situation where the cost of reworking is prohibitive, then you should either not use XP or you should use an environment that makes rework easier.

我们承认我们在这一点上会有一点分歧。由于风险，马丁比肯特更倾向于提出故事。肯特认为马丁是这种态度的胆小鬼。马丁同意。

We'll confess that we disagree a little on this. Martin is much more inclined to bring stories forward due to risk than Kent is. Kent considers Martin a coward for this attitude. Martin agrees.

示例发布计划

Example Release Plan

让我们从时间胶囊中看一下发布计划。这些信息在卡片上做了注释，但我们已将其全部转换为方便您使用的表格（参见表13.1）。

Let's take a look at the release plan from the time capsule. The information was annotated on the cards, but we've transposed it all into a handy table for you (see Table 13.1).

表 13.1。时间胶囊发布计划
故事 时间估计（理想周） 分配的迭代# 分配的版本号
查找最低票价。 3个 2个 1个
