[a] 如果“Show hotels”不存在则为 4

[a] Is 4 if "Show hotels" isn't already there

我们测量了团队在每次迭代六个理想周内的速度。如您所见，故事已分配给迭代。在前两次迭代之后有一个版本，在两次迭代之后有一个进一步的版本。（发布的内容有点短，但这足以作为示例。而且无论如何，保密协议禁止我们在开始前两个世纪展示整个计划。）

We measured the team's velocity at six ideal weeks per iteration. As you can see, stories have been assigned to iterations. There's a release after the first two iterations and a further release two iterations later. (The releases are a little short, but this is enough for an example. And in any case, there's this confidentiality agreement that prohibits us from showing the whole plan two centuries before we begin.)

有几点值得注意：

There are a few things worth noting:

  • “Do customer profile”故事被分成两个不同优先级的部分。在这种情况下，估计不会相加。他们经常这样做，但有时他们不这样做。那不是错误。每个故事都应该独立估计，所以它确实发生了。也许把它拆开让我们意识到它比我们想象的要大，或者分开做它们会花更长的时间。原因通常并不重要，因此无需记录。

  • The "Do customer profile" story has been split up into two parts with different priorities. The estimates don't add up in this case. Often they do, but from time to time they don't. That's not an error. Each story should be estimated independently, so it does happen. Maybe breaking it apart made us realize it was bigger than we thought, or maybe doing them separately would take longer. The reason usually isn't important, so there's no need to document it.

  • 第二次迭代只有五个理想的故事周分配给它，即使速度是六。没关系——额外的工作，无论是新故事还是后续故事的片段，很可能会在接近迭代日期时添加。

  • The second iteration only has five ideal weeks of stories assigned to it even though the velocity is six. That's okayadditional work, either new stories or pieces of later stories, may well get added closer to the iteration's date.

  • 卡片上的“显示酒店可用性”注释表明估计取决于其他工作。这并不少见，但不值得大惊小怪。它可能只是在客户弄清楚要在迭代 2 中放入什么时才记录下来。

  • A note on the card for "Show hotel availability" indicates that the estimate depends on other work. That's not uncommon, but it isn't worth making a fuss about. It was probably only recorded as the customer was figuring out what to put in iteration 2.

  • 当尚未分配“显示酒店”时，将“预订酒店”分配给迭代 2 可能看起来很奇怪。看不到名单怎么订酒店呢？这里的要点是，该功能尚不可供用户使用，但将内置到系统中，并且可以进行功能测试以使客户满意。并非所有行为都必须可供用户使用才能包含在迭代中；关键标准是它是可测试的。在需要在核心业务逻辑中构建功能但直到稍后的迭代才添加用户界面的情况下，您经常会发现这种情况。

  • It may look odd that "Book a hotel" is assigned to iteration 2 when "Show hotels" isn't assigned yet. How can you book a hotel if you can't see the list? The point here is that the functionality won't be available to the user yet but will be built into the system and can be functionally tested to the satisfaction of the customer. Not all behavior has to be usable by the user to be included in the iteration; the key criteria is that it is testable. You'll often find this in cases where you need to build functionality in the core business logic but don't add the user interface until a later iteration.

  • 您会注意到没有关于迭代长度或团队规模的详细信息。这是故意指出您实际上不需要基本发布计划的信息。您所需要的只是估计的故事和速度。显然，您需要当前日期和迭代长度来告诉人们迭代何时完成。如表 13.2所示

  • You'll notice there are no details about the iteration length or size of team. This is deliberate to point out that you actually don't need that information for the basic release plan. All you need is the estimated stories and the velocity. Obviously you'll need the current date and the iteration length to tell people when an iteration will be done. Something along these lines as shown in Table 13.2

  • 令人欣慰的是，即使在二十四世纪，人们也会使用两位数字来表示年份。

  • It's comforting to know that even in the twenty-fourth century people will be using two digits for the year.

表 13.2。迭代完成日期
事件 日期
开始 29 年 4 月 1 日
第 1 版完成 29 年 4 月 19 日
第 2 版完成 29 年 5 月 10 日

第 14 章发布计划事件

Chapter 14. Release Planning Events

生活就是当你忙于制定其他计划时发生在你身上的事情。

-约翰列侬

Life is what happens to you while you're busy making other plans.

John Lennon

各种事件导致团队进行一些发布计划。客户添加和更改故事的优先级，开发人员估计故事，并且团队会注意到它是否有太多或太少要做。

Various events cause the team to do a little release planning. The customer adds and changes the priorities of stories, developers estimate stories, and the team notices if it has too much or too little to do.

在进行发布计划时，您会发现需要做几件事。在本章中，我们将讨论发布计划中的各种事件以及您如何应对它们。

As you are doing release planning, you'll find there are several things you need to do. In this chapter we talk about the various events in release planning and how you react to them.

改变故事的优先级

Changing the Priorities of Stories

企业经常改变他们的优先事项。通过一次只承诺一个迭代的故事价值，可以保证客户有机会根据关于故事的优先级和成本的最新信息做出优先级决策。

Businesses often change their priorities. By only committing to one iteration's worth of stories at a time the customer is guaranteed a chance to make priority decisions based on up-to-the-minute information about the priority and cost of the stories.

添加故事

Adding a Story

如果您将 XP 与现有的许多其他方法进行比较，对客户来说最大的不同是他们不必在开发开始之前就他们想要的一切做出详细的规范。需求蠕变是完全合理和合理的，甚至是有价值的。只要我们知道他们要去哪里并且客户知道后果，这些要求就可以随心所欲地蔓延。事实上，我们鼓励需求四处爬行并找到客户需要的任何东西。

If you compare XP to many of the other methodologies out there, the biggest difference to customers is that they don't have to commit to a detailed specification of everything they want before development begins. Requirements creep is perfectly reasonable and rational, even valuable. The requirements can creep wherever they like as long as we know where they are going and the customer is informed of the consequences. Indeed, we encourage the requirements to crawl around and find whatever it is the customer needs.

客户可以随时添加新故事。他写了我们在第 11 章中描述的故事。开发然后以理想的方式估计故事。现在，客户可以为任何迭代选择故事，但要遵守通常的规则，即迭代故事的估计总和不能超过团队的速度。客户可以随心所欲地移动故事，为新故事腾出空间。

The customer can add a new story at any time. He writes the story as we describe in Chapter 11. Development then estimates the story in ideal effort. Now the customer can pick the story for any iteration, subject to the usual rule that the sum of the estimates of the stories for an iteration cannot exceed the velocity of the team. The customer moves stories as much as he likes to make room for the new story.

重建发布计划

Rebuild the Release Plan

我们谈论的大多数事情都是对计划的小规模更改。你必须推迟一些故事，移动一些故事。像这样的小改动可以使计划保持良好状态，但有时您需要一些更重要的东西。

Most of the things we talk about are small-scale changes to a plan. You have to defer a few stories, move some stories about. Little changes like this keep the plan in good shape, but sometimes you need something a good bit more significant.

以下情况需要重建计划：

You need to rebuild the plan in the following circumstances:

  • 当延迟的故事堆变得太高时。一些推迟到以后的故事不值得重建，但如果它们中的足够多，你确定你不会把所有事情都完成，那么是时候做点什么了。

  • When the pile of deferred stories has grown too high. A few stories deferred till later is not worth rebuilding for, but if enough of them mount up that you are sure you aren't going to get everything done, it's time to do something about it.

  • 如果团队的速度发生变化，那么发布计划的所有假设都会被打破，您需要一个新的发布计划。

  • If the team's velocity changes, then all the assumptions for the release plan are broken and you need a new release plan.

重建从重新评估故事的开发开始。最初的估计在当时是一个很好的猜测。从那时起，每个人都会学会。重建是考虑这种学习的好时机。在重新估算期间，开发人员可以使用最近故事中的实际数字来更好地校准他们的估算。重新估计在开发早期尤为重要，因为早期发布计划最不准确。

A rebuild begins with development reestimating the stories. The original estimates were a good guess at the time. Since then everyone will have learned. A rebuild is a good time to take this learning into account. During the reestimating, developers can use the actual figures from recent stories to better calibrate their estimates. Reestimating is particularly important early in development as the early release plans will be the least accurate.

一旦开发人员重新评估了故事，客户就会选择一堆合适的故事。只需捏住你的鼻子并做数学。如果您在每个迭代中运行大约 8 周的故事，并且您有 3 个迭代要进行，那么客户会为该版本选择 24 周的故事。他将在发布后尽快获得其余的故事。

Once development has reestimated the stories, the customer picks a pile of stories that will fit. Just hold your nose and do the math. If you are running at around 8 weeks' worth of stories per iteration and you have three iterations to go, then the customer picks 24 weeks' worth of stories for this release. He will get the rest of the stories as soon after the release as possible.

您应该期望每三到四次迭代重建计划。你不想一直这样做，因为这需要相当多的时间，但它确实需要定期进行。把它想象成换油。你不必这样做，但你不这样做是愚蠢的。

You should expect to rebuild the plan every three or four iterations. You don't want to do it all the time, as it takes a fair amount of time, but it does need doing regularly. Think of it as changing the oil. You don't have to do it, but you'd be stupid not to.

第十五章 第一个计划

Chapter 15. The First Plan

第一个计划是发布计划中最难和最不准确的部分。幸运的是，您只需要做一次。

The first plan is the hardest and least accurate part of release planning. Fortunately you only have to do it once.

制定第一个计划

Making the First Plan

所以现在您知道发布计划是什么样子以及如何使用它了。应该清楚的是，计划的准确性取决于其估算的准确性，而估算的准确性取决于项目的历史。第一个计划没有历史，所以你的估计是不稳定的。第一个计划是什么？

So now you know what a release plan looks like and how you use it. It should be clear that the accuracy of the plan depends on the accuracy of its estimates, and the accuracy of the estimates depends on the history of the project. The first plan has no history, so your estimates are flaky. What does this make the first plan?

片状。（想想喝太多咖啡的克莱默。）

Flaky. (Think Kramer with too much coffee.)

但是您仍然需要一个计划才能开始。该计划为您提供了一些可跟踪的东西，以便您可以评估进度。它为您提供了一个故事框架，使您可以注意到发生了什么并建立历史记录以更好地制定以后的计划。然而，第一个计划总是期望值高，交付率通常低。

But you still need a plan to even get started. The plan gives you something to track against so you can assess progress. It gives you a framework of stories that allow you to notice what happens and build up the history to make the later plans better. The first plan, however, is always high on expectations and usually low on delivery.

第一个计划有两个主要的不确定领域：团队的速度和故事的大小。以下是关于如何在这种情况下尽力而为的一些提示。

The first plan has two main areas of uncertainty: the velocity of the team and size of the stories. Here are a few tips on how to do the best you can under the circumstances.

测量速度。在对项目进行几次迭代之前，您不会对速度有一个像样的了解。在你可以测量之前，你能做的最好的就是猜测。

Velocity is measured. You won't get a decent picture of velocity until several iterations into the project. Before you can measure, the best you can do is guess.

猜测速度的一种方法是在编写和估算第一个故事时衡量进度。在探索过程中，尽可能按照迭代计划使用任务。监控进度并跟踪人们报告的理想时间，就像您对迭代跟踪所做的那样。查看人们完成工作的理想时间，并以此为基础。每次程序员说，“我会在一天内完成”，请注意实际需要多长时间。如果“一天的工作量”在日历上通常需要三天，那么您可以猜测团队的速度为人数×周/迭代/3。

One way to guess velocity is to measure progress while you are writing and estimating the first stories. During exploration, use tasks much along the lines of an iteration plan. Monitor progress and track the ideal time people report, much as you do with iteration tracking. See how much ideal time people get done and use that as a basis. Every time a programmer says, "I'll get that done in a day," notice how long it actually takes. If "a day's worth of work" generally takes three days on the calendar, then you could guess the team's velocity as number people × weeks/iteration/3.

如果您的组织中有类似的项目，您可以使用团队的速度来帮助估算您的速度。他们有六个人进行为期三周的迭代。即每次迭代 18 个日历周。他们的速度是六。你有四个人，正在进行两周的迭代。这是每次迭代八个日历编程周。所以猜测你的速度是 6 × 8/18，大约是 2。

If there's a similar project in your organization, you could use the team's velocity to help estimate yours. They have six people on three-week iterations. That's 18 calendar weeks per iteration. Their velocity is six. You have four people and are doing two-week iterations. That's eight calendar programming weeks per iteration. So a guess at your velocity is 6 × 8/18 which is about 2.

一开始很难估计故事。我们最幸运的方法是让团队从他们认为最适合估算的故事开始。为了估计最初的几个故事，人们问自己：“如果这个故事就是我要做的全部，而且我没有分心，我认为它需要多长时间？” 一旦他们完成了舒适的故事，就可以通过比较来完成其他故事，就像您对历史估计所做的那样。

Story estimates are tough at first. The approach we've had the best luck with is to get the team to start with the stories they feel the most comfortable estimating. To estimate those first few stories, have people ask themselves, "If this story was all I had to do, and I had no distractions, how long do I think it would take?" Once they have done the comfortable stories, do the others by comparison, much as you would with historical estimates.

您可能有另一个团队完成了类似的工作。你如何利用这种经验？不要让他们为您估算故事。这打破了那些做的人应该是那些估计的人的规则。坚持别人的估计会导致缺乏承诺和士气下降。不要那样做。

You may have another team that's done similar work. How can you use that experience? Don't get them to estimate the stories for you. That breaks the rule that those who do should be those who estimate. Being held to someone else's estimates will lead to lack of commitment and falling morale. Don't do that.

您可以让您的团队查看其他团队的历史记录，并在此基础上得出自己的衡量标准。但是你必须小心，不要让比较变得太棘手。一旦你开始推理一个团队与另一个团队相比有多快，你就会得到各种各样的情绪反应，这些反应会扭曲每个人的想法。它有助于解决所有可能出现的问题。在比较任务之间的工作量时也很方便：“将对象连接到关系数据库又花费了他们一半的时间，所以让我们从相同的比例开始吧。”

You can have your team look at the history of the other team and come up with its own gauge based on that. But you have to be careful not to let comparisons get too sticky. Once you start reasoning about how fast one team is compared with another you'll get all sorts of emotional reactions that will distort everyone's thinking. It can be helpful in flushing out all the issues that may come up. It can also be handy in comparing effort between tasks: "It took them half as much again to get the objects hooked into the relational database, so let's start with the same proportions for us."

选择你的迭代长度

Choosing Your Iteration Length

迭代应该多长时间？有很多人赞成迭代开发，但他们并不是都以同样的方式回答这个问题。有人说一个迭代可以长达六个月。我们往另一个方向走。迭代应该很短——在一到三周之间。我们赞成两周，最近对 XP eGroup ( http://www.egroups.com/group/extremeprogramming ) 进行的一项调查显示，两周和三周是最受欢迎的选择。

How long should an iteration be? There are a lot of people who favor iterative development, but they don't all answer this question the same way. Some people say that an iteration can be as long as six months. We go in the other direction. Iterations should be shortbetween one and three weeks. We favor two, and a recent survey on the XP eGroup (http://www.egroups.com/group/extremeprogramming) showed that two and three weeks were the most popular choices.

表 15.1。问题：您的迭代持续多长时间？[A]

选择

Choices

票数

Votes

百分

Percent

<1 周 0 0% 1 周 7 19% 2 周 14 38% 3 周 12 32% 4 周 3 8% 1 个月 1 3% >1 个月 0 0%

[a] 基于 37 个回复

[a] Based on 37 replies

为什么让它们这么短？我们希望从计划中获得的关键内容之一是进度指示：我们已经走了多远，我们还要走多远？迭代开发帮助我们判断进度，因为每次迭代都会交付工作的、经过测试的代码——这是很难捏造的。但里程碑只发生在迭代结束时。迭代时间越长，滑出一点点失控的风险就越大。您希望每次迭代都尽可能短，以便您尽可能频繁地知道自己在哪里。

Why make them so short? One of the key things we want from a plan is an indication of progress: how far have we come, how far have we to go? Iterative development helps us judge progress, because each iteration delivers working, tested codewhich is hard to fudge. But milestones only occur at the end of an iteration. The longer the iteration, the more risk you run of sliding just a little bit out of control. You want each iteration to be as short as possible, so that you know where you are as frequently as possible.

但也有太短这样的事情。每次迭代都意味着一些开销：

But there is such a thing as too short. Each iteration implies some overhead:

  • 确保验收测试正在运行

  • Making sure the acceptance tests are running

  • 规划迭代

  • Planning the iteration

  • 向管理层汇报

  • Reporting to management

我们不希望开销大于我们在迭代中尝试做的事情。如果是，我们将停止计划和迭代。

We don't want the overhead to be bigger than what we are trying to do in the iteration. If it is, we will stop planning and iterating.

不要太纠结于选择正确的迭代长度。如果您选择三周迭代而不是两周迭代，世界就不会结束。只要您准备好了解迭代长度的影响，并准备好在发现问题时进行试验，您几乎可以从任何地方开始。所以从两周的迭代开始。

Don't get too hung up about choosing the right iteration length. The world isn't going to end if you pick three-week iterations instead of two-week iterations. As long as you are prepared to be aware of the effects of iteration length, and prepared to experiment when you spot a problem, you can start most anywhere. So start with two-week iterations.

一个相关的问题是什么时候开始迭代。我们对有多少球队没有在周一开始感到惊讶。正如 Kent 的一位客户雄辩地说的那样，“星期一糟透了。计划糟透了。为什么要把它们放在一起？” 这个客户在星期二开始迭代，并且对这个选择很满意。团队成员可以在迭代的最后一个星期一进行整理、准备演示和编写更多测试。第二天，他们准备出发了。

A related question is when do you start the iterations. We've been surprised by how many teams don't start on Monday. As one of Kent's clients so eloquently put it, "Mondays suck. Planning sucks. Why put them together?" This client starts iterations on Tuesday, and has been happy with the choice. Team members can spend the last Monday of the iteration tidying up, readying demos, and writing even more tests. The next day, they are ready to go.

入门

Getting Started

有了计划后，如何开始编程？如果只有一个班，你就不能很好地分工。

Once you have the plan, how do you get started programming? You can't very well divide up the work if there's only one class.

我们在一个大房间里成功地连接了一台投影仪和电脑。召集整个团队——程序员、客户和经理。花几天时间实施测试用例、满足它们并改进设计。在那段时间结束时，你应该有足够的棋子，三到四对可以独立工作。

We've had success in a big room with a projector connected to the computer. Bring the whole teamprogrammers, customers, and managers. Spend a couple of days implementing test cases, satisfying them, and evolving the design. At the end of that time you should have enough pieces that three or four pairs can work independently.

另一个入门想法（感谢 Michael Hill）是零功能迭代。在开始编程之前，通常需要完成一些小的技术基础设施任务：

Another idea (thanks to Michael Hill) for getting started is the zero functionality iteration. There are often a bunch of little technical infrastructure tasks to get done before you can begin programming:

  • 让测试框架工作

  • Getting the testing framework working

  • 让自动构建结构工作

  • Getting the automated build structure working

  • 使用所有适当的权限启动并运行网络

  • Getting the network up and running with all the appropriate permissions

  • 设置基本安装脚本

  • Getting the basic install scripts set up

您不希望在第一次迭代中就致力于功能，结果却让客户失望，因为您无法让 framdoozle 与 whatzit 交谈。如果您以前没有使用过您的技术，请考虑在开始编程之前花两周时间让机制正常工作。

You'd hate to commit to functionality in a first iteration only to disappoint the customer because you couldn't get the framdoozle talking to the whatzit. If you haven't worked with your technology before, consider spending two weeks getting the mechanism working just right before you begin programming.

第 16 章发布计划变化

Chapter 16. Release Planning Variations

发行计划的一些本地改编是较短的发行、较长的发行和较短的故事。

Some local adaptations of the release planning are shorter releases, longer releases, and shorter stories.

在采用 XP 的任何地方，它都会经历快速的发展（参见第 27 章）。以下是我们遇到的一些变体。

Everywhere XP is adopted, it undergoes rapid evolution (see Chapter 27). Here are a few variations we have encountered.

短片

Short Releases

有时您可以更频繁地发布，也许是每次迭代。这可能发生在内部开发中，也可能发生在应用程序服务提供商那里，您的用户距离很远但使用瘦客户端并且您可以密切控制服务器。

Sometimes you can release much more often, maybe every iteration. This can happen for in-house development and also for application service providers where your users are distant but using thin clients and you have close control over the server.

这大部分是好消息。每个迭代都已准备好投入生产，并且每次迭代都投入生产是完全可行的。这通常意味着您需要对您的测试和非常自动化的构建过程有高度的信心，但如果您使用的是 XP，您无论如何都应该拥有这些。

Most of this is good news. Each iteration is ready for production, and going into production with each iteration is perfectly feasible. This usually means that you need to have high confidence in your tests and a very automated build process, but if you are doing XP you should have these anyway.

对于短版本，您实际上根本不需要任何版本的概念。您可以迭代到迭代，提前计划一个或两个迭代。这使您能够对客户做出快速响应，让客户控制流程并快速反馈以查看结果。

With short releases you don't really need any notion of a release at all. You can work iteration to iteration, planning one or two iterations ahead. This allows you to be very responsive to the customer, giving the customer control of the process with rapid feedback to see the results.

但是，永远不会“释放”是有危险的。客户可能会失去对软件需要走向何方的战略眼光。在这种情况下，客户会花费大量时间来选择短期功能，而忽略了重要的长期需求。

However, there is a danger to never having "a release." The customer may lose strategic vision of where the software needs to go. In this case the customer spends so much time choosing features for the short term that she misses important long-term needs.

该版本可以作为一个长期里程碑回归。到下个季度末，我们希望能到达这里，到下个季度末，我们希望能到达那里。因此，即使您每次迭代都将产品发布到生产环境中，仍然要考虑按季度计划发布。尽管由此产生的计划对于预测未来不是很有帮助，但规划那些较长版本的行为是至关重要的。（不是有将军说过类似的话吗？）

The release can come back as a longer-term milestone. By the end of the next quarter we hope to be here, and by the end of the following quarter we want to be there. So even if you release into production every iteration, still think about planning out a release on a quarterly scale. Even though the resulting plan isn't very helpful as a predictor of the future, the act of planning those longer releases is vital. (Didn't some general say something like that?)

长期发布

Long Releases

如果您每年只能发布一次会怎样？

What happens if you can only release once a year?

我们对这一现实的第一反应是质疑它。也许有一些方法可以更频繁地发布。

Our first reaction to this reality is to question it. Maybe there is some way to release more frequently.

长版本的常见情况是替换现有系统。因为您必须做旧系统必须做的所有事情，所以您不能发布仅具有某些功能的东西。

A common case for long releases is in replacing an existing system. Because you have to do all the things the old system had to do, you can't release something with only some of the features.

在这种情况下想办法让新旧共存。用旧系统管理一些合同，用新系统管理一些合同，随着每个版本的发布逐渐转移合同。这可能涉及在系统之间迁移数据和集成用户界面的额外工作，但由此带来的风险降低通常是值得的。

In this case look for a way to let the old and the new coexist. Manage some contracts with the old system and some with the new, gradually moving the contracts over with each release. This may involve extra work to migrate data between the systems and to integrate the user interfaces, but the resulting drop in risk is usually worth it.

另一种情况是收缩包装软件。许多用户只是不想每个季度都升级他们的软件，营销部门也不会应对由此产生的变化。在这种情况下，寻找一种方法将中间版本发送给那些可能对这些版本更感兴趣的客户。称它们为服务包或其他名称。这样至少您的一些用户会在生产中使用该系统，并且您会得到您需要的反馈。

Another case is with shrink-wrap software. Many users just will not want to upgrade their software every quarter, nor will the marketing department cope with the resulting flux. In this case look for a way to send intermediate releases to those customers that may be more interested in these versions. Call them service packs or something. That way at least some of your users will use the system in production, and you'll get the feedback you need.

频繁发布固然好，但如果不能经常发布，就不必完全放弃 XP。您可能需要创建仅在内部可用的临时版本。这些足以让友好的用户在受控条件下玩耍，并为规划目的提供焦点。

Frequent releases are good, but if you can't release frequently you don't have to abandon XP completely. You may need to create interim releases that are only available internally. These will be enough for the friendly users to play with in controlled conditions and to provide a focus for planning purposes.

小故事

Small Stories

有些团队喜欢有更多的小故事。他们将计划 25 个为期两天的故事，而不是四五个两周的故事。这使客户可以更好地控制团队的活动，但代价是团队的一些灵活性和客户的更多参与。

Some teams like to have more smaller stories. Instead of four or five two-week stories, they will plan 25 two-day stories. This gives the customer finer control over the activities of the team, at the cost of some of the flexibility of the team and more involvement by the customer.

空间推理

Spatial Reasoning

James Goebel 发送了这个故事：

James Goebel sent this story:

Interface Systems 的 Java Factory 有一个产品经理负责规划长期发布，一个咨询团队根据客户需求生成短期需求，还有一个客户服务经理负责排定产品错误和调度他们的维修。

Interface Systems' Java Factory has a situation where there is a product manager responsible for planning long-term releases, a consulting team that generates short-term requirements based on customer needs, and a customer service manager who is responsible for qualifying product bugs and scheduling their repairs.

为了适应这些多种声音，我们创建了一些简单的工具。第一个明显的工具是现在每个故事卡都列出了赞助客户，这样程序员可以很容易地记住在出现问题时要与谁交谈。我们创建的第二个工具是用于规划游戏的游戏桌，每次迭代都有 8.5" × 11" 的空缺位置，等于可以适合下一个两周迭代的两周故事的数量。

In order to accommodate these multiple voices we created a few simple tools. The first obvious tool is that each story card now lists the sponsoring customer so that programmers can easily remember with whom to talk when a question arises. The second tool we created is a game table for the planning game that has for each iteration a number of 8.5" × 11" open positions equal to the number of two-week stories that can be fit into the next two-week iteration.

在团队估算完所有故事后，物理故事卡的副本与所有其他故事卡的大小成比例：三周故事为 8.5" × 16"，两周故事为 8.5" × 11"，一周故事为8.5" × 5.5"，半周故事为8.5" × 2.75"，依此类推。然后“委员会客户”开会决定如何在棋盘上组织故事片段。通过调整各个部分的大小，以便可以使用目视检查快速完成所有数学运算，这次会议可以继续专注于竞争性业务问题，由此产生的发布计划可以在几个小时内完成。这个相同的游戏桌在整个迭代周期中保持可用，因此如果创建了一个需要立即关注的新故事，相同的“委员会客户”

After all the stories have been estimated by the team, a copy of the physical story card is sized proportionally to all the other story cards: three-week stories are 8.5" × 16", two-week stories are 8.5" × 11", one-week stories are 8.5" × 5.5", half-week stories are 8.5" × 2.75", and so on. The "committee customer" then meets to decide how to organize the story pieces on the playing board. By sizing the pieces so that all math can be done quickly using visual inspection, this meeting can remain focused on the competing business issues where the resulting release plan can be completed in only a couple of hours. This same game table remains available throughout the iteration cycle so that if a new story is created that requires immediate attention, the same "committee customer" can quickly decide how to adjust the plan to accommodate the reassignment of resources.

第 17 章迭代计划

Chapter 17. Iteration Planning

每个迭代都是通过将迭代的故事分解为任务来计划的。通过要求程序员注册他们想要的任务，然后要求他们估计他们的任务，然后在必要时重新平衡来安排任务。

Each iteration is planned by breaking down the stories for that iteration into tasks. Tasks are scheduled by asking programmers to sign up for the tasks they want, then asking them to estimate their tasks, then rebalancing as necessary.

发布计划与业务节奏同步。它为业务人员提供了一种思考故事集的方式，这些故事集一起向市场讲述了一个好故事。迭代计划与编程节奏同步。两周足够长

The release plan is synchronized to the rhythms of business. It gives the business people a way of thinking about sets of stories that together tell a good story to the market. The iteration plan is synchronized to the rhythms of programming. Two weeks is long enough to

  • 开发一些新功能

  • Develop some new functionality

  • 进行实质性重构

  • Do a substantial refactoring

  • 开发一些基础设施

  • Develop some infrastructure

  • 尝试一些实验

  • Try some experiments

  • 从小小的失望中恢复过来

  • Recover from little disappointments

与发布计划不同，迭代计划在很大程度上是开发人员的。他们决定如何做事以及按什么顺序做事。客户仍然参与其中。在迭代中期报告进度很重要，这样客户可以看到正在发生的事情并了解实际会发生什么。如果团队发现要做的事情太多而您需要缩小范围，客户也会参与进来。

Unlike the release plan, the iteration plan is very much the developers'. They decide how to do things and in what order. The customer is still involved. It's important to report progress mid-iteration so that the customer can see what's happening and get a sense for what will actually happen. The customer will also get involved if the team finds there is too much to do and you need to cut scope.

迭代的正式开始是迭代计划会议，程序员聚在一起将迭代的故事分解为任务。我们这样做是因为我们需要比故事更小的单位来追踪。每项任务大约需要一到三天的理想时间。虽然让程序员负责从头到尾完成一个故事通常是值得的，但人们最好报名参加较小的任务，让他们有机会表达自己的专长。故事可以共享工作，我们可以通过让它们共享任务来更好地处理这个问题。最后，必须在迭代内部处理使大多数计划者发疯的那种依赖性。

The formal start of the iteration is the iteration planning meeting, where the programmers get together to break down the stories for that iteration into tasks. We do this because we need smaller units to track than the stories. Each task is about one to three ideal days long. While it's often worthwhile to have a programmer responsible for seeing a story through to completion, it is better for people to sign up for the smaller tasks to give them a chance to express their specializations. Stories can share work, and we can handle this better by having them share tasks. Finally, the kind of dependencies that drive most planners crazy must be dealt with inside of iterations.

在迭代计划会议之后，有人负责跟踪迭代（第 19 章）。这个人，跟踪者，密切关注完成了哪些任务以及未完成任务还剩下多少。她的工作是提醒团队注意可能出现的问题：要做的事情太多、要做的太少、人们过度投入或投入不足。团队每天都有一个简短的站立会议，这样每个人都可以看到其他人在做什么。这有助于保持整个团队的沟通顺畅。

After the iteration planning meeting someone takes on the responsibility of tracking the iteration (Chapter 19). This person, the tracker, keeps an eye on which tasks are done and how much is left on outstanding tasks. Her job is to alert the team to problems that might come up: having too much to do, too little to do, people overcommitted or undercommitted. Every day the team has a short stand-up meeting so everyone can see what everyone else is doing. This helps keep communication flowing across the whole team.

永远不要错过日期

Never Slip the Date

规划极限编程最重要的原则之一是日期是固定日期，但范围会有所不同。在每个项目中，您都会遇到有太多事情要做的情况，并且您会忍不住稍微推迟迭代日期以容纳更多功能。

One of the most important principles in planning for Extreme Programming is that the dates are hard dates, but scope will vary. In every project you'll run into the situation where there is too much to do and you'll be tempted to slip the date of an iteration just a little bit to accommodate a little more functionality.

不要那样做。

Don't do that.

推迟约会是那些既容易上瘾又有害的坏习惯之一。损害实际上来自于它很容易做到的事实。然而，在某些时候，您要么会失误太多以至于失去所有可信度（以及项目），要么会遇到一个非常痛苦的日期，比如发布日期。如果推迟日期是人们唯一知道该怎么做的事情，那么这就是会发生的事情，而且痛苦是巨大的。

Slipping dates is one of those bad habits that is both addictive and damaging. The damage really comes from the fact that it's so easy to do. At some point, however, you'll either slip so much that you'll lose all credibility (and the project, too), or you'll run into some date that's very painful to slip, like a release date. If slipping dates is the only thing people know how to do, then that's what will happen, and the pain is great.

处理太多事情的更难但更可靠的方法是推迟功能。因为它更难，所以练习它更重要。只有当团队（尤其是客户）在每次迭代中都实践这一点时，每个人都准备好在真正重要的日期到来时这样做。最重要的故事是客户决定暂时可以没有的故事。这些故事可以挽救项目。

The harder but surer way to cope with too much to do is to defer functionality. Because it's harder it's more important to practice doing it. Only if the team (and especially the customer) practices this for every iteration will everyone be ready to do this when the really important date comes along. The most important stories are the ones the customer decides he can live without for the moment. Those stories can save projects.

有时推迟发布日期可能会更好。那是客户的决定。它会涉及项目规划范围之外的许多问题。只有每个人都实践了延迟功能，客户才能真正在日期和功能之间做出选择。当一个重要的约会迫在眉睫时，客户可以不用多少“基本”功能而感到惊讶。

Sometimes it may be better to slip a release date. That's the customer's decision. It will involve many issues outside the scope of project planning. Only if everyone has practiced deferring function will the customer have a genuine choice between date and function. We are constantly surprised by how much "essential" functionality customers can do without when a big date looms.

通常你只能在重要日期出现时才能做出那些艰难的选择，如果不练习，你就无法在压力下做出选择。正如 Jim Highsmith 所说，“我过去认为时间盒是关于时间的，但我了解到它是关于在整个项目中强制做出艰难的权衡决定。”

Often you can make those hard choices only when the big dates appear, and without practice you can't do it under pressure. As Jim Highsmith says, "I used to think time-boxing was about time, but I've learned that instead it is about forcing hard tradeoff decisions throughout the project."

另一个不推迟日期的原因是你会失去控制。迭代中总是存在一些不确定性。只有在迭代结束时，您才真正知道自己在哪里。所以你永远不想推迟那个时间。

The other reason not to slip dates is that you lose control. There's always some uncertainty within the iteration. Only at the end of an iteration do you really know where you are. So you never want to put that time off.

第 18 章迭代计划会议

Chapter 18. Iteration Planning Meeting

在迭代开始时，团队创建迭代计划。这个计划将迭代分解为几天的开发任务，每个任务都有一个程序员负责完成。

At the beginning of an iteration the team creates an iteration plan. This plan breaks down the iteration into development tasks of a few days, each with a programmer responsible for its completion.

迭代计划会议是您在迭代中做的第一件事。应该不会超过一天，大多数团队会在一天内完成。所有团队成员以及客户都应参加。找一个有足够白板空间的舒适房间。

The iteration planning meeting is the first thing you do in the iteration. It shouldn't take any more than a day, and most teams will do it in under a day. All of the team should attend, as well as the customer. Find a comfortable room with plenty of whiteboard space.

这是序列的概述。（这只是一个总结。我们稍后会描述它的含义。）

Here's an overview of the sequence. (This is just a summary. We'll describe what it all means in a moment.)

  • 读出本次迭代的故事。

  • Read out the stories for this iteration.

  • 在白板上写下每个故事需要完成的所有任务。

  • Write on the whiteboard all the tasks that need to be done for each story.

  • 将需要完成的任何技术任务添加到列表中。

  • Add to the list any technical tasks that need doing.

  • 开发人员注册并根据他们的个人速度评估任务。

  • Developers sign up and estimate tasks up to their individual velocity.

  • 如果任何故事未完全注册，客户将被要求推迟一些故事。

  • If any story isn't completely signed up for, the customer is asked to defer some stories.

  • 如果有多余的时间，则要求客户添加故事。

  • If there is extra time, the customer is asked to add stories.

了解故事

Understanding the Story

要做的第一件事是提醒大家这次迭代的菜单上有什么。让客户朗读故事通常是个好主意，这样每个人都可以从客户的角度来听。

The first thing to do is to remind everyone what's on the menu for this iteration. It's often a good idea for the customer to read out the stories so that everyone hears them from the customer's perspective.

卡片上的一句话足以作为故事的标记和提醒。计划一个故事肯定是不够的，更不用说编写代码了。因此，客户需要通过深入了解故事的更多细节来为迭代计划会议做准备。我们有几种方法可以做到这一点。

A short sentence on a card is enough to act as marker and reminder for a story. It certainly isn't enough to plan out a story, let alone write the code. So the customer needs to prepare for the iteration planning session by going into more detail about the stories. We've several ways of doing this.

  • 最简单的是让客户简短地讲述一下这个故事。这很简单，口头表达，通常效果很好

  • The simplest is for the customer to give a short talk about the story. This is simple and verbal and often works just fine

  • 下一个最简单的方法是让客户对故事的细节进行书面描述。这是证实细节的几页。我们称之为叙事。（在我们付印时，Martin 的当前项目在下一次迭代中的叙述不会超过四页。）

  • The next simplest is for the customer to produce a written description of the details of the story. This is a few pages of corroborating detail. We call this a narrative. (As we go to press, Martin's current project has no narratives longer than four pages in the next iteration.)

  • 最详细的方法是为故事提供全套验收测试。

  • The most detailed approach is to provide a full set of acceptance tests for the story.

您最终将需要验收测试，因此测试是证实细节的最佳形式。似乎不可能在迭代开始时就进行验收测试。叙述是合理的复制品，前提是每个人都明白叙述是对话的补充而不是替代。

You'll need the acceptance tests eventually, so tests are the best format for corroborating detail. It seems to be impossible to get the acceptance tests at the beginning of the iteration. The narrative is a reasonable facsimile, providing that everyone understands that the narrative is a supplement to conversation not a substitute for it.

您需要找出最适合您环境的方法。在几次迭代过程中，您应该找到最适合您团队的方法。

You'll need to find out what works best in your environment. Over the course of a few iterations you should find what works best for your team.

列出迭代的任务

Listing the Tasks for an Iteration

每个故事都是几周理想的努力，因此对于计划的这个细节，我们需要将故事分解为几个更细粒度的任务。每项任务都应该是几天理想的努力。这些任务是开发任务，因此它们不需要对客户有意义。

Each story is a few ideal weeks of effort, so for this detail of planning we need to break the story down into a few finer-grained tasks. Each task should be a few ideal days of effort. The tasks are development tasks, so they don't need to make sense to the customer.

提出任务的最佳方式是让所有相关人员集思广益。通常这会涉及对如何构建故事的一些思考。您不需要在这里进行重大的设计工作，但您确实需要足够的时间来获得一份好的任务列表。简要介绍一下您需要添加和修改的类和交互。请记住，目标不是设计迭代所需的一切；而是设计迭代所需的一切。这是为了帮助确定最好的任务分解是什么。作为执行任务的一部分，您将进行其他设计会议。

The best way to come up with the tasks is for everyone involved to just brainstorm what they might be. Often this will involve a little thought about how you're going to build the story. You don't need a major design effort here, but you do need just enough to get a good list of tasks. Take a short pass at the classes and interactions you'll need to add and modify. Remember that the goal is not to design everything that is needed for the iteration; it is to help figure what the best task breakdown is. You'll do other design sessions as part of carrying out the tasks.

通常，您会发现故事之间存在重叠。这种重叠可能会让您有机会构建有助于同时满足多个故事的软件。可能存在来自过去迭代的现有设计，通过一些重构，可以显着帮助本次迭代。为此添加任务。拥有满足多个故事的任务真是太好了。

Often you'll find overlap between the stories. This overlap may give you the opportunity to build software that helps satisfy several stories at once. There may be existing designs from past iterations that, with a little refactoring, could significantly help this iteration. Add tasks for this. It's great to have tasks that satisfy more than one story.

例如，一些故事可能要求当您在字段中输入文本时，您会从给定列表中寻找该文本的可能补全。将这个设施开发三四次，每个故事一次，将是一种耻辱。所以把它变成一个任务。可能是过去迭代中的其他故事需要将此新功能改装到它们上面。您可以将改造作为一项单独的任务。

For example, several of the stories may require that as you enter text into a field you hunt for possible completions for that text from a given list. It would be a shame to develop this facility three or four times, once for each story. So make this into a task. It may be that other stories from past iterations need to have this new feature retrofitted onto them. You might make that retrofit a separate task.

您可能会发现任务之间的依赖关系。您不需要 PERT 图表或类似的东西。对于一个在几周内进行沟通的团队，您可以依靠团队来解决这些依赖关系。值得与他们讨论，以影响首先解决的任务。然而，正如您将看到的，您永远不会精确地计划每项任务何时完成，或者任务完成的顺序。

You'll likely find dependencies between tasks. You won't need PERT charts or similar beasts. With a team that is communicating over a few weeks you can rely on the team to sort these dependencies out. It's worth talking them over, to influence what tasks are addressed first. However, as you'll see, you never plan precisely when each task gets done, or in what order the task gets done.

最后，对于如何将某事分解为任务并没有硬性规定。使用对您有意义的任何方法。只要任务保持简短并且您可以为它们编写测试，就可以了。

In the end there's no hard and fast rules for how you break something down into tasks. Use whatever approach makes sense for you. As long as the tasks are kept short and you can write tests for them, you'll be fine.

技术任务

Technical Tasks

你的大部分时间将花在构建故事上。然而，有一些客户不关心但仍然需要完成的纯技术任务。这些包括安装供应商的数据库升级，重构系统的一些混乱部分，尝试一种设计思想以了解它是否有用，以及改进配置控制过程。像这样的任何东西都应该添加到列表中。同样，保持每个任务的规模较小很重要，因此将工作分解为几天的理想任务。

Most of your time will be spent in building stories. However, there are some purely technical tasks the customer doesn't care about but that still need to be done. These include installing the vendor's database upgrade, refactoring some messy bit of the system, trying out a design idea to learn if it will be useful, and improving the configuration control process. Anything like this should be added to the list. Again, it's important to keep each task small, so break the work into tasks of a few ideal days.

Ron Jeffries 声称他可以将任何技术任务转变为面向业务的故事，客户可以根据自己的选择安排或不安排此迭代。没有任何技术任务有话要说。一旦出于技术原因开始设置优先级的滑坡，就很难停下来。Dave Cleal 建议预留预算的固定部分，比如 10%，供程序员随意使用。我们还没有尝试过，但听起来很有趣。

Ron Jeffries claims he can turn any technical task into a business-oriented story the customer can either schedule this iteration or not as she chooses. There's something to be said for not having any technical tasks. Once you start down the slippery slope of setting the priority for technical reasons, it's hard to stop. Dave Cleal suggests that a fixed portion of the budget, say 10 percent, be set aside for the programmers to spend as they like. We haven't tried it, but it sounds interesting.

衡量程序员的速度

Measuring the Velocity of a Programmer

您如何确保个别程序员不会过度投入？在迭代计划期间，团队会面临压力，要求他们尽自己的一份力量。对责难的恐惧会淹没程序员的经验。

How do you make sure individual programmers don't overcommit? During iteration planning there's pressure to be seen by the team to be doing your part. Fear of censure can overwhelm a programmer's experience.

我们使用昨天的天气来减少这种情况经常发生的可能性。每个程序员通过跟踪他每次迭代的成就来衡量他的速度。程序员只能注册与他完成上一次迭代相同天数的任务。

We use Yesterday's Weather to reduce the chance of this happening regularly. Each programmer measures his velocity by tracking his accomplishments every iteration. A programmer can only sign up for the same number of days' worth of tasks as he completed last iteration.

有充分的理由修改这个数字。如果某人在这三周的迭代中有一周用于度假，他将只有三分之二的可用速度。

There are good reasons to modify this number. If someone is spending one week of this three-week iteration on vacation, he will only have two-thirds of his velocity available.

程序员的速度不是生产力、速度或守门员能力的衡量标准。它只是说他可以报名参加多少任务。一个人可能速度很慢，因为他在估计时天生乐观。另一个人的速度可能很慢，因为他花了很多时间帮助其他开发人员。对于程序员来说，做出准确的预测比达到任何任意的生产力指标更重要。速度的绝对值远不如其预测能力重要。

A programmer's velocity is not a measure of productivity, speed, or goalkeeping ability. It just says how many tasks he can sign up for. One person may have a low velocity because he is naturally optimistic when estimating. Another may have a low velocity because he spends a lot of time helping other developers. It's more important for a programmer to make accurate predictions than for him to reach any arbitrary productivity measure. The absolute value of velocity is far less important than its predictive capability.

注册和估计任务

Signing Up and Estimating Tasks

一旦你在白板上列出了任务列表，程序员就可以开始注册它们了。通过注册，程序员接受在迭代期间处理该任务的责任。她需要做的第一件事是估计她完成这项任务需要多长时间。

Once you have a list of the tasks on the whiteboard, programmers can then start signing up for them. By signing up, a programmer accepts the responsibility for working on that task during the iteration. The first thing she needs to do is to estimate how long it will take her to do the task.

由程序员决定如何进行估算。像往常一样，最好的方法是将任务与以前的工作进行比较。程序员可以说，“这应该与我上次迭代完成的交付 GUI 花费的时间大致相同。” 项目记录将显示该任务花费了多长时间，以便这次可以使用该数字。

It's up to the programmer to decide how to come up with an estimate. As usual, the best approach is to compare a task with previous work. The programmer can say, "This should take about the same time as the shipping GUI I did last iteration." The project records will show how long that task took, so that number can be used this time.

小心使用其他程序员的类似工作。我们是在与人打交道，而不是 Plug Compatible Programming Units。程序员工作的速度不一样，对于一个任务他们的速度也会不一样。让程序员查看记录以帮助做出估算是很有用的，但不要说，“Dinsdale 只花了三天时间完成这项任务，那你为什么认为它会花你五天时间？” 一旦你开始使用这些记录作为俱乐部，你将永远不会再得到一个诚实的估计。这里最重要的是尽可能准确地获得估计——如果你想比较程序员的能力，不要在计划时这样做。

Be wary of using comparable work from another programmer. We are dealing with people, not Plug Compatible Programming Units. Programmers do not work at the same speed, and their speed will be different for a task. It's useful to let a programmer look at the records to help come up with an estimate, but don't say, "It only took Dinsdale three days to do this task, so why do you think it'll take you five?" Once you start using the records as a club, you'll never get an honest estimate again. The most important thing here is to get estimates as accurately as you canif you want to compare programmers' abilities, don't do it during planning.

程序员在执行任务时应该始终假设他们有一个合作伙伴，因为在 XP 中，所有生产编码都是成对完成的。特定合作伙伴可能会影响估计。“如果 Spiny 愿意与我合作，我们可以在两天内完成。” 没关系。事实上，它强化了人们互相帮助的原则。

Programmers should always assume they have a partner when doing a task, since in XP all production coding is done in pairs. It may be that a particular partner can affect the estimate. "If Spiny will work with me on this, we can do it in two days." That's fine. Indeed it reinforces the principle that people help each other.

程序员还应该假设在编写并通过所有单元测试之前他们没有完成任务。“我完成了编码，但我还没有测试它，”在 XP 中是一个毫无意义的声明。没有测试的代码根本不存在用于计划目的。

Programmers should also assume that they aren't done with a task until they have all the unit tests written and passing. "I'm done with the coding, but I haven't tested it yet," is a meaningless statement in XP. Code without tests simply doesn't exist for planning purposes.

程序员可以注册他们想做的任何事情。人们可以做他们想做的事情，这会让他们保持动力。由于动力是生产力的关键，这是一件好事。一些程序员会选择一种他们喜欢的任务，并且大部分都是这样做的。其他人喜欢通过尝试新事物来扩大他们的兴趣。这是一件好事，因为它可以保持动力，让开发人员提高技能，并降低项目风险。

Programmers can sign up for whatever they want to do. People can work on things they have a desire to do, which keeps them motivated. Since motivation is the key to productivity, this is a Good Thing. Some programmers will pick one kind of task they prefer and mostly do this. Others like to broaden their interests by trying new things. This is a Good Thing because it keeps up motivation, it allows developers to grow their skills, and it reduces project risk.

在迭代计划中，就像在本书的所有内容中一样，我们关注的是程序员的工作。其他人需要完成的任务如何：编写文档、设计图标等？在迭代计划中，我们已经看到将工作分解为任务并将它们添加到列表中的一些成功。技术作家然后注册用户手册，艺术家注册图标设计，同时程序员注册编程。

In iteration planning, as indeed in all of this book, we've focused on what the programmers do. How about the tasks others need to do: writing documentation, designing icons, and so on? In iteration planning we've seen some success from breaking down the work into tasks and just adding them to the list. Technical writers then sign up for the user manuals and artists sign up for icon design at the same time programmers sign up for programming.

剪裁工作

Scut Work

一些项目经理在听说这种“签约”做法后担心会有一些肮脏的工作没有完成。实际上，我们认为这不是问题。开发人员千差万别，几乎总有人喜欢做任何事情。对于偶尔不受欢迎的任务，会进行一些非正式且通常不言而喻的分享。

Some project managers on hearing about this "signing up" practice fear there'll be some dirty work that doesn't get done. In practice we don't find this is an issue. Developers are so varied that there is almost always someone who likes doing anything. For occasional unpopular tasks, some informal and often unspoken sharing goes on.

如果有人总是以失败告终，请让团队想出一个解决方案。团队成员可能会选择进行更正式的轮换，轮流做冷门的工作。他们可能会尝试招募喜欢做这种工作的人加入团队。程序员喜欢解决问题，所以他们会找到解决方案。如果他们提出解决方案，他们将努力让它飞起来。

If someone always ends up with the short end of the stick, ask the team to come up with a solution. Team members may choose to do a more formal rotation to take turns doing unpopular work. They may try to recruit someone to the team who likes doing this kind of work. Programmers like solving problems, so they'll find a solution. If they come up with the solution, they will work to make it fly.

太多事情要做

Too Much to Do

一旦所有程序员都签署了任务并对其进行了评估，请查看您的任务列表。在一个完美的世界中，所有任务都将被注册。在这个特殊的星系中，我们经常发现一些任务无人认领。如果您有孤立任务，您会推迟哪些任务？

Once all the programmers have signed up for tasks and estimated them, take a look at your task list. In a perfect world all the tasks will be signed up for. In this particular galaxy, we often find that some tasks remain unclaimed. If you have orphan tasks, which tasks do you defer?

你能再等一次迭代来升级数据库吗？有时等待是最好的选择，但有时您认为没有任何技术任务可以推迟。

Can you wait another iteration to upgrade the database? Sometimes waiting is the best option, but other times there aren't any technical tasks you think you can defer.

如果没有可以推迟的技术任务，请询问客户。“我们缺少五个理想的日子。我们需要你删除五个理想的故事价值。”

If no technical tasks can be defered, ask the customer. "We are short five ideal days. We need you to remove five ideal days' worth of story."

客户可以推迟整个故事，或者他们可以选择拆分故事并推迟其中一个结果部分（请参阅第 49 页的“拆分用户故事”）。客户可以选择拆分多个故事以获得正确的组合。推迟的故事会出现在下一次迭代的列表中。客户可以在两周后再考虑。

Customers can defer a whole story, or they can choose to split a story and defer one of the resulting parts (see "Splitting User Stories" on page49). A customer may choose to split several stories to get the right mix. A deferred story goes on the list for the next iteration. The customer can consider it again in two weeks.

如果您推迟一个故事，您可能会想要调整整个发布计划。不要急于这样做。在重新制定发布计划之前进行一两次迭代。通常延期太小而不会立即成为问题。在值得尝试与他们打交道之前，他们需要建立起来。

You may be tempted to adjust the whole release plan if you defer a story. Don't rush to do that. Go for an iteration or two before you rework the release plan. Often the deferments are too small to be an issue right away. They need to build up before it's worth trying to deal with them.

做的太少

Too Little to Do

来吧，笑，但它确实不时发生。

Go ahead, laugh, but it does happen from time to time.

这个过程与太多事做相反。程序员要求客户添加一些故事。客户可以添加整个故事或拆分故事并移动其中的一部分。但是，像往常一样，决定移动什么的是客户，而不是程序员。

This process is the reverse of too much to do. The programmers ask the customer to add some stories. The customer can add a whole story or split a story and move a part in. However, as usual, the customer decides what gets moved, not the programmers.

例子

Example

迭代计划

Iteration Plan

我们将从时间囊中挖掘出更多内容来展示第二次迭代的迭代计划。笔记看起来像这样：

We'll dig some more stuff out of the time capsule to show the iteration plan for the second iteration. The notes look like this:

查找最低票价。

Find lowest fare.

备选票价查找器对象 - 知识库 2

Alternative fare finder objectKB 2

按日期范围查找候选票价 - MF 1

Find candidate fares by date rangeMF 1

更新行星端口以寻找替代品—知识库 1

Update planet ports to find alternativesKB 1

查找备选港口的候选票价 — 知识库 1

Find candidate fares for alternative portsKB 1

特别优惠——主要空间线——MF 2

Special offersmajor space linesMF 2

特别优惠—低价空间线—RJ 3

Special offerslow-price space linesRJ 3

低票价用户界面——RJ 1

UI for low faresRJ 1

查看行程。

Review itineraries.

简单的行程UI展示—WC 2

Simple UI display of itinerariesWC 2

显示一个行程的详细信息—RJ 2

Display detail for one itineraryRJ 2

预定一间旅馆。

Book a hotel.

酒店预订接口—MF 1

Hotel booking interfacerMF 1

IHAB 接口—MF 2

Interface to IHABMF 2

HiHat 接口—MF 1

Interface to HiHatMF 1

Mary's Rote 接口—MF 1

Interface to Mary's RoteMF 1

与 HillTown 的接口 — WC 1

Interface to HillTownWC 1

Best Southern 接口—RJ 1

Interface to Best SouthernRJ 1

Woodstar 接口—WC 1

Interface to WoodstarWC 1

（按城市显示酒店——IHAB。）

(Show hotelsIHAB by city.)

向 IHAB 查询指定城市的酒店 — WC 2

Query IHAB for hotels for named cityWC 2

命名城市显示的 UI—WC 1

UI for named city displayWC 1

其他

Other

UI清理—KA 2

UI cleanupKA 2

网络性能改进—知识库 2

Network performance improvementKB 2

使用 IPv84 进行调查 - 知识库 1

Investigate using IPv84KB 1

笔记：

Notes:

  • 故事中的任务不一定加到发布计划中的估计中。“预订酒店”被标记为一个理想的一周，但结果却是八个理想的日子。“寻找最低票价”是理想的三个星期，但结果却是理想的十一天。当您开始更详细地估计并获得有关迭代的更多信息时，这很常见。在这种情况下，他们抵消得很好，但他们可能不会。这就是为什么我们不在迭代计划中写下原始故事估算的原因。否则，我们会试图强制将任务估计值与故事估计值相加。那么我们将使用质量较低的信息进行规划。如果任务估计表明您过度承诺，​​请返回给客户。

  • The tasks in the stories don't necessarily add up to the estimates in the release plan. "Book a hotel" was marked as one ideal week but comes out as eight ideal days. "Find lowest fare" was three ideal weeks but came out as eleven ideal days. This is quite usual as you start estimating in more detail and have more information about the iteration. In this case they cancel out pretty well, but they may not. That's why we don't write down the original story estimate in the iteration plan. Otherwise, we will be tempted to force fit the task estimates to sum to the story estimate. Then we would be planning with lower-quality information. If the task estimates say you are overcommitted, go back to the customer.

  • 因为时间还剩，团队拿了“Show hotels”建了一小块。在这里，客户拆分“显示酒店”以获得有用且足以让团队用完可用的额外时间的部分。

  • Because there is time left over, the team took "Show hotels" and built a little piece of it. Here the customer split "Show hotels" to get a piece that was useful and enough for the team to use up the extra time it had available.

  • 大多数团队成员的速度为 7。KA 的速度为二。也许他是兼职或新加入团队，或者只是估计不同。

  • Most team members have a velocity of seven. KA has a velocity of two. Maybe he's part-time or new to the team or just estimates differently.

  • 任务中有很多依赖关系，但计划没有注意到它们中的任何一个。通过观看视频，我们可以看出，在您可以按日期范围查找候选票价或查找替代港口的候选票价之前，需要替代票价查找器对象。此外，您需要更新行星港口以显示替代港口，然后才能找到替代港口的候选者。这些都不在计划中。因为这是一个 XP 团队，所以我们可以放心地假设 MF 和 KB 是智能人，他们会就需要完成的事情的顺序进行沟通，并将在他们之间解决问题。

  • There are plenty of dependencies in the tasks, but the plan doesn't note any of them. From watching the videos we could tell that the alternative fare finder object was needed before you could find candidate fares by date range or find candidate fares for alternative ports. Also, you need to do the update of planet ports to show alternatives before you can find candidates for alternative ports. None of this is on the plan. Because this is an XP team we can safely assume that MF and KB are intelligent beings who will communicate about the order in which things need to be done and will sort things out between them.

第 19 章跟踪迭代

Chapter 19. Tracking an Iteration

每周几次，跟踪器检查迭代的进度以了解事情的进展情况。

A couple of times a week, the tracker checks progress on the iteration to see how things are going.

你有一个迭代计划，所以现在你所要做的就是坐下来看着计划展开——对吗？如果你说是，那就用这本书敲自己的脑袋三下（庆幸它很薄）。

You have an iteration plan, so now all you have to do is sit back and watch the plan unfoldright? If you said yes, hit yourself on the head three times with this book (and be glad it's a thin one).

关于计划，你唯一知道的就是事情不会按照计划进行。所以你必须定期监控迭代。您需要有人负责跟踪迭代中的进度。我们称这个人为追踪者。

The only thing you know about a plan is that things won't go according to it. So you have to monitor the iteration at regular intervals. You need to have someone whose job it is to track progress in an iteration. We call this person the tracker.

迭代进度检查

Iteration Progress Check

每周几次左右，跟踪器需要找出每个人在迭代中的位置。我们不建议为此召开会议或（但愿如此）撰写报告。相反，跟踪器应该一次访问每个程序员。

A couple of times a week or so the tracker needs to find out where everyone is with the iteration. We don't suggest calling a meeting for this or (heaven forbid) writing a report. Instead, the tracker should visit each programmer one at a time.

跟踪器向开发人员询问两个关于他们注册的每个任务的问题：

The tracker asks developers two questions about each task they signed up for:

  • 您为此工作了多少个理想的日子？

  • How many ideal days have you worked on this?

  • 在完成之前，您还需要多少天的理想时间？

  • How many more ideal days do you need before you're done?

请注意，我们不要求完成百分比。我们发现这样的问题会产生几乎毫无意义的答案。要监控剩余工作量，关键问题是剩余天数。（知道到目前为止已经做了多少对于建立历史记录更为重要。）

Notice we don't ask for the percentage complete. We've found that such a question generates a nearly meaningless answer. To monitor how much work there is left, the key question is how many days are left. (Knowing how much has been done so far is more important for building the historic record.)

此时，您可以将所有程序员任务的数字相加并评估情况。

At this point you can add up the figures for all the programmer's tasks and assess the situation.

最重要的是剩下要做的事情。理想的工作日数与开发人员的剩余日历时间相比如何？这种比较总是有些粗糙。使用剩余日历时间的比率没有意义，因为开发人员不会在迭代中均匀地工作理想的日子。但如果差异很大，那就是一个警告信号。如果有更多理想的事情要做的日子比剩下的日历天数，这也绝对是一个警告信号。

Most important is what is left to do. How does the amount of ideal days of effort compare with the developer's remaining calendar time? This comparison is always somewhat rough. There's no point using a ratio of the remaining calendar time because the developer won't get to work ideal days evenly through the iteration. But if there is a big difference, that's a warning sign. It's also definitely a warning sign if there are more ideal days of things to do than calendar days left to do them.

在很大程度上，分析取决于程序员。她认为她有太多事情要做吗？跟踪器的作用是提出简单的问题并指出可能存在的问题。最终是程序员自己判断她是否能够在迭代结束前获得足够多的理想天数。

To a large extent the analysis is up to the programmer. Does she think she has too much to do? The tracker's role is to ask simple questions and point out possible problems. In the end it is the programmer's judgement whether she will be able to get in enough ideal days before the end of the iteration.

在这个阶段，您不会对“到目前为止有多少天”问题做太多事情。这主要是为了帮助您获得完成任务的列表以及他们实际花费了多少理想天数。每次都询问比在迭代结束时询问要好，因为那时没人记得他们上周在某件事上花了多少时间。

At this stage you don't do much with the "How many days so far" question. Primarily that's to help you get a list of tasks done with how many ideal days they actually took. Asking each time is better than asking at the end of the iteration when nobody can remember how much time they spent on anything last week.

这个过程的一个非常重要的部分是跟踪器应该亲自与每个程序员讨论状态。你从身体线索和直觉中获得了如此多的信息。这些数字很有价值。同样重要的是程序员对进度的感受，它同时考虑了任务的状态和程序员的个性。个人风格对于追踪者监控进度的工作至关重要。

A very important part of this process is the fact that the tracker should personally talk to each programmer about status. You get so much information from physical cues and gut feel. The figures are valuable. Just as important is the sense of how the programmer feels about progress, which takes into account both the state of the task and the personality of the programmer. The personal touch is essential to the tracker's job of monitoring progress.

需要注意的一件事是，如果程序员报告说花在任务上的理想时间比平时少很多。这可能没有任何意义——她这周只是做了很多帮助——或者这可能意味着有其他事情占用了她的时间。也许程序员需要一些帮助来清理甲板。

One thing to watch is if a programmer reports a lot less ideal time spent on tasks than usual. This might mean nothingshe was just doing a lot of helping this weekor it may mean there's something else that's chewing up her time. Perhaps the programmer needs some help clearing the decks.

把旧数字拿给程序员。这样你就只要求自上次进度检查以来的变化。但不要采用最初的估计。您希望避免任何使新估计与旧估计相匹配的倾向。

Take the old figures to the programmer. That way you are asking only for the change since the last progress check. But don't take the original estimates. You want to avoid any tendency to make the new estimates match the old ones.

关闭

Getting Closure

罗布·米和爱德华·希亚特

Rob Mee and Edward Hiatt

在 Rob Mee 的指导下，在 Kent Beck 的频繁投入下，作为 XP 团队，我们从项目一开始就知道客户和开发人员之间持续协作的重要性。特别是，我们在每三周的迭代开始时留出一天或更长时间，让程序员和客户挤在一起敲定为该时间段安排的功能和任务。在这个启动日之后，任务被写在海报上并挂在墙上，等待完成后被打勾。在整个迭代过程中，程序员要求客户澄清需求；与此同时，客户在看到他们想象中的产品成型时，以这种方式推动新兴产品。当一对开发人员完成一项任务时，他们会走到墙上的海报前划掉它，

Coached by Rob Mee, and with frequent input from Kent Beck, we as an XP team knew from the start of our project the importance of constant collaboration between customers and developers. In particular, we set aside a day or more at the start of each three-week iteration when the programmers and the customers huddled together hammering out the features and tasks that had been scheduled for that time period. After this kick-off day the tasks were written on posters and hung up on the wall, waiting to be ticked off as they were completed. Throughout the iteration programmers asked the customers for clarification of requirements; at the same time, customers nudged the emerging product this way and that as they saw what they had imagined taking shape. When a pair of developers completed a task, they went to the wall poster and crossed it off, and moved on to the next one.

听起来很理想，但有一个问题。请注意开发人员在完成任务后是如何不交叉的。当他们认为已经完成时，他们正在划掉它们。合作还不够深入。尽管在开发过程中进行了密切合作，但最后一步，即业务决策，是由程序员自己完成的。这产生了不愉快的后果。任务被划掉后，客户会看着这个功能说，“这不太对劲，需要稍微调整一下。” 由于流程不清楚在这种情况下如何返回，客户只会将差异记录为错误。

Ideal as that might sound, there was a problem. Notice how the developers weren't crossing off tasks when they were done. They were crossing them off when they thought they were done. The collaboration hadn't been taken far enough. In spite of the close cooperation during development, the programmers were taking that final step, that business decision, by themselves. This had unpleasant consequences. After the task had been crossed off, the customers would look at the feature and say, "That doesn't work quite right. It needs a minor adjustment." With the process unclear about how to go back in a situation like this, the customers would simply log the discrepancy as a bug.

随着时间的推移，错误列表不断增加：不完整、小缺陷和简单的误解被添加到错误列表中。管理层开始向开发人员施压，要求他们降低错误数量。开发人员对压力感到不满，因为许多项目显然不是“错误”；它们只是澄清，甚至是改变主意。客户对额外跟踪的开销感到不满。每个人都知道问题的根源是沟通问题，而不是缺乏能力。但是如何解决呢？我们已经在不断地沟通。

As time went by, the bug list grew: incompletions, small deficiencies, and simple misunderstandings were being added to the bug list. Management started pressuring the developers to lower the bug count. Developers resented the pressure because many of the items clearly weren't "bugs"; they were just clarifications or even changes of mind. Customers resented having the overhead of the extra tracking. Everybody knew the root of the problem was a communication issue, not a lack of competency. But how to fix it? We were already in constant communication.

最后，项目经理 Vraj Mohan 看到了简单的解决方案：应该由客户而不是开发人员在完成时划掉任务。这将强制执行流程中缺失的最终协作步骤。一旦采取了这一步骤，大部分已经形成的摩擦都消失了。程序员对完成更有信心——如果客户看到最终的作品并感到满意，开发人员就可以确定他们已经完成了任务。客户仍然希望在完成后更改功能，但现在这些更改被视为增强功能或他们自己生成的附加功能，而不是程序员的错误。

Finally the project manager, Vraj Mohan, saw the simple solution: It should be the customer, not the developer, who would cross off tasks at completion. This would force the final collaborative step that had been missing from the process. Once this step was instituted, most of the friction that had been developing melted away. Programmers had a much more confident sense of completionif the customer saw the final piece of work and was satisfied, the developers could be sure that they were finished with the task. Customers still wanted changes in features after completion, but now the changes were viewed as enhancements or additional features that they themselves had generated, rather than as bugs that were the fault of the programmers.

共享荣耀

Sharing the Glory

在每次迭代结束时，整个团队都会聚集在一起，观看开发人员演示每个人在前三周内参与的工作。这部分是为了让每个人都能及时了解最新的发展，部分是为了鼓舞士气——开发者-客户团队向团队其他成员展示他们共同完成的工作是令人欣慰的。我们会沿着任务列表走下去，对于每个划掉的任务，曾经处理过该任务的一对开发人员中的一个会上前演示该功能。

At the end of each iteration, the whole team would gather round and watch the developers demo the work in which each had been involved in the preceding three weeks. This was partly so that everyone could be kept abreast of the latest developments, and partly as a morale boostit's gratifying for the developer-customer team to show off the work they have done together to the rest of the team. We would walk down the task list, and for each crossed-off task, one of the developers from the pair that had worked on the task would step forward and demo the feature.

当每个任务都被演示时，通常会犹豫，因为在任务上结对的两个开发人员决定谁将演示该功能。在这样的一个时刻，在第三次或第四次迭代结束时，碰巧出现了很长的延迟。为了结束等待，客户走上前来，善意地宣布她将亲自演示它，而不是等待开发人员决定。这是一时冲动完成的，让在场的团队都笑了起来；但是当罗伯和肯特想到刚刚发生的事情时，他们意识到这是一个绝妙的主意。为什么不总是让客户演示他们的功能？毫无疑问，这将确保客户能够跟上迭代期间正在完成的工作。在观众面前，

As each task came up to be demoed, there was often a hesitation as the two developers who had paired on the task decided on who would be the one to demo the feature. At one such point, at the end of the third or fourth iteration, there happened to be a long delay. To end the wait, the customer whose feature it was stepped forward and good-naturedly announced that she herself would demo it instead of waiting for the developers to decide. It was done on the spur of the moment and brought a laugh from the team watching on; but as Rob and Kent thought about what had just happened, they realized that this was an excellent idea. Why not always have customers demo their features? It would ensure without a doubt that customers would keep up with the work being done during the iteration. In front of an audience, everyone wants to be prepared for their "performance," so no customers would want to lose track of what progress had been made on their features.

这个过程已经流行起来。它鼓励客户与开发者对保持更紧密的联系：我们发现客户更渴望与开发者签到以尽快看到新作品，这往往会导致客户的愿景与最终的结果更加匹配产品。

This process has become popular. It encourages the customer to keep in closer contact with the developer pair: We have found that customers are more eager to check in with developers to see new work as soon as possible, which tends to lead to closer matching of the customer's vision with the final product.

落后

Falling Behind

跟踪是被动的，直到您发现出现问题为止。在这种情况下，向上意味着程序员意识到她无法完成她注册的所有任务。发生这种情况的原因有很多，但最重要的一点是对此采取一些措施。

Tracking is passive, until you find that something is up. Up in this case means the programmer realizes she can't complete all the tasks she signed up for. There are plenty of reasons this can happen, but the most important point is to do something about it.

第一反应是找有时间愿意接任务的人。然后，他应该给出自己对完成任务所需时间的估计。如果他的估计最终大于可用时间，则问题尚未解决。

The first reaction is to look for someone else with time available who is willing to accept the task. He should then give his own estimate of how much time is needed to finish the task. If his estimate ends up greater than the time available, the problem hasn't been solved yet.

如果没有人有足够的时间来承担这项任务，那么团队就需要想办法解决这个问题。让每个人都知道这个问题很重要，因为有人可能手头有好的解决方案。这就是站立会议派上用场的地方。通常，一对夫妇花点时间进行一些非正式的杂耍就可以解决这个问题。

If nobody has enough time to take on the task, then the team needs to figure out what to do about it. It's important to let everyone know about the problem, as someone may have a good solution at hand. This is where the stand-up meeting comes in handy. Often a bit of informal juggling of a couple people's time can overcome the problem.

如果没有任何好的解决方案可用，您必须去找客户并告诉她分数。客户需要知道哪些故事已经完成了哪些工作。然后她经历了与她在迭代开始时几乎相同的过程：选择一个故事来推迟或拆分一个故事并推迟一部分。您越早将情况引起客户的注意，她就有更多的选择来从迭代中挽救最大可能的业务价值。

If there aren't any great solutions available, you have to go to the customer and tell her the score. The customer will need to know what work has been completed on what stories. She then goes through much the same process as she did at the beginning of the iteration: choose a story to defer or split a story and defer a part. The sooner you bring the situation to the customer's attention, the more options she has for salvaging the greatest possible business value out of the iteration.

客户在迭代中期这样做很烦人，所以团队应该努力避免这种情况。解决这个问题的关键是更好地进行估算，而这只能通过实践和良好的任务记录来实现。随着时间的推移，迭代中期修正的发生频率应该会降低。如果它们的发生频率没有降低，则团队需要找出问题出在哪里。虽然故事估计相当模糊，但一旦您着手处理迭代计划中的任务，您就不应该有如此大的波动。

It's annoying for the customer to do this in the middle of the iteration, so the team should work to avoid this. The key cure to this problem is to get better at estimating, and this can only come with practice and good task records. Over time mid-iteration corrections should happen less often. If they aren't occurring less often, the team needs to figure out what is going wrong. While the story estimates are pretty vague, once you get down to tasks in the iteration plan, you shouldn't get such big swings.

我们从项目经理那里听到过这样的话：“XP 是我的程序员告诉我我得不到我想要的东西的借口。” 客户永远不会因为不得不削减已经承诺的范围而感到高兴。有时客户得不到他们想要的东西。谁来决定他们得不到什么——客户、程序员、项目经理，还是机会？

We've heard this line from project managers: "XP is an excuse for my programmers to tell me I can't have what I want." Customers aren't ever happy about having to cut already-committed scope. Sometimes customers can't have what they want. Who is going to decide what they don't getthe customers, the programmers, the project managers, or chance?

加班呢？简单的规则是任何人都不能连续两周加班。如果有人想花一两天时间赶上进度，那很好。但是不要指望那个人在一两天内得到全部结果。

What about overtime? The simple rule is that no one can work overtime two weeks in a row. If someone wants to crank for a day or two to get caught up, fine. But then don't expect full results from that person for a day or two.

当程序员有额外的时间

When a Programmer Has Extra Time

不可避免地，这是最不常见但也更令人愉快的问题。第一个选择是看别人的任务负荷，看程序员能不能帮到别人。通常你会在团队中混合平衡。

Inevitably this is the least frequent but also the more pleasant problem. The first choice is to look at other people's task load and see if the programmer can help others. Often you'll have a mix on the team that balances out.

如果没有，则再次由客户决定可以提出什么，无论是完整的故事还是故事的一部分。

If not, then it's off to the customer again to see what can be brought forward, either a full story or part of a story.

但如果程序员在最近的迭代中负担过重，可以考虑让他休息一下。如果他最近不得不加班，这可能意味着休息一天。这可能意味着需要花一些时间进行试验——花一天时间研究一些可能有用的技术。这样的休息有助于保持人们的积极性，并可能产生有助于项目的有用想法。

But if the programmer has had a heavy load in recent iterations, consider letting him take a break. This may mean a day off if he has had to use overtime recently. It may mean some time experimentingspending a day looking at some bit of technology that might be useful. Such breaks help keep people motivated and may lead to useful ideas that'll help the project.

迭代何时完成？

When Is the Iteration Done?

迭代在开始时设置的日期完成。两周的迭代在两周内结束，没有但是。已经完成的故事，已经完成。未完成的故事将推迟到下一次迭代计划会议中考虑实施。

The iteration is done on the date that was set at the beginning. A two-week iteration ends in two weeks, no buts. Stories that are done, are done. Stories that are not done are deferred to be considered for implementation in the next iteration planning meeting.

故事什么时候完成？

When Is a Story Done?

当故事的功能向客户展示并且客户同意该功能基本上满足预期时，故事就完成了。

A story is done when the function of that story is demonstated to the customer and the customer agrees that the functionality substantially fulfills what is expected.

狡猾的词“基本上满足”是什么意思？客户正在支付标签，因此客户决定她是否满意。

What do we mean by the weasel words "substantially fulfills"? The customer is paying the tab, so the customer decides if she is satisfied.

客户应对该故事运行验收测试。可能会出现故障。然后客户决定失败是否足以保证说故事没有完成。如果电话账单上的费用打印错了，那么客户可能会说，“不，这个故事是不可接受的。” 如果格式有一点差，她可能会说，“好吧，有错误，但我们会采用软件。” 很多人发布的软件都有已知的错误。一些发布的软件带有大量已知错误。只要客户知道分数，她会接受什么取决于她。

The customer should run the acceptance tests for that story. There may be failures. The customer then decides whether the failures are enough to warrant saying that the story isn't done. If the charges on the phone bill print out wrong, then the customer will probably say, "No, the story isn't acceptable." If the formatting is one pica off, she may say, "Okay, there are bugs, but we'll take the software." Plenty of people ship software with known bugs. Some ship software with plenty of known bugs. As long as the customer knows the score, it's up to her what she will accept.

示例迭代跟踪

Example Iteration Tracking

回到时间胶囊，查看在第二次迭代进行到三分之二时完成的一些迭代跟踪。您可以使用一个简单的表格来显示迭代的状态。

Back into the time capsule to look at some iteration tracking done two-thirds of the way through the second iteration. You can show the state of the iteration with a simple table.

表 19.1给出了迭代的状态。底线警告我们潜在的问题。KA 直到迭代结束才消失，所以我们有四个人。我们计划每个人可以在三周的迭代中完成 7 天的理想工作。四个人在整个迭代中可以做28个理想的日子。在上周，他们大约可以完成其中的三分之一：9 天。但是我们还有 14 天的工作要做。

Table 19.1 gives us the state of the iteration. The bottom line warns us of potential problems. KA is gone until the end of the iteration, so we have four people. We plan that each can do 7 ideal days in a three-week iteration. The four people can do 28 ideal days in the whole iteration. In the last week, they can do roughly a third of that: 9 days. But we have 14 days of work to go.

查看任务和各个状态，我们可以看到更多细节。RJ 几乎步入正轨，还有三天的理想时间。与他交谈表明他对按时完成工作感到很自在。

Looking at the tasks and individual states we can see some more details. RJ is pretty much on track, with three ideal days to go. Talking to him brings out that he is comfortable that he will complete his work on time.

厕所很舒服。他的任务比他想象的要容易。他上周有空。

WC is very comfortable. His tasks worked out easier than he thought. He is free for the last week.

但是，KB 和 MF 都遇到了相当多的未完成时间。我们可以通过引入 WC 来进行一些调整，但这还不够。因此，我们需要与客户交谈以决定需要做什么。客户可以查看任务，但主要是查看故事的状态。

However, both KB and MF are in trouble with a quite a bit of outstanding time. We can do a bit of shuffling here by bringing in WC, but it won't be enough. So we need to talk to the customer to decide what needs to be done. The customer can look at the tasks, but primarily he looks at the state of the stories.

客户知道我们有大约 9 天的理想时间。应该剪什么？“找到最低票价”是这里的关键故事。它需要不惜一切代价完成。“订酒店”不太重要，绩效工作对客户来说也不是那么重要；否则这将是一个故事。因此，这允许团队重新审视任务并再次注册需要工作的任务。表 19.3显示了未完成的任务。

The customer knows we have around nine ideal days available. What should be cut? "Find lowest fare" is the key story here. It needs to be done at all costs. "Book a hotel" is less important and the performance work is not that critical to the customer; otherwise it would be a story. So this allows the team to look at the tasks afresh and sign up again for the ones that need work. Table 19.3 shows the outstanding tasks.
