厕所总计   2个

新计划推迟了进一步的性能改进。为了专注于最低价故事，WC 从 MF 那里接了特价任务。客户说他宁愿使用 Mary's Rote 接口也不愿使用有问题的 IHAB 接口，因此 MF 完全放弃了后者。

The new plan defers further performance improvement. To focus on the lowest price story, WC picks up the special offers task from MF. The customer says that he would rather get the Mary's Rote interface than the problematic IHAB interface, so MF drops the latter completely.

（任务表的格式只是跟踪任务的一种方式。我们每个团队都有自己的格式。）

(The format of the task tables is just one way to track tasks. Every team of ours has come up with its own format.)

第 20 章站立会议

Chapter 20. Stand-up Meetings

当会议变得无聊时，请离开。

——罗伯特·塞西尔“鲍勃叔叔”马丁

When a meeting gets boring, leave.

Robert Cecil "Uncle Bob" Martin

每天召开一次简短的会议，这样每个人都知道发生了什么，什么没有发生。

Have a short meeting once a day so everybody knows what's going on, and what's not.

你会注意到我们没有参加很多会议。会议是大多数程序员最无聊的浪费时间的清单。但会议也是人们交流的一种方式。挑战在于弄清楚什么样的会议效果最好。

You'll notice we aren't into lots of meetings. Meetings are at the top of most programmers' lists of boring time wasters. But meetings are also a way for people to communicate. The challenge is to figure out what kind of meetings work well.

我们发现，每天的简短会议对于让每个人都了解其他人在做什么来说是非常宝贵的。然而，重点是短。如果日常会议开始拖延，你就会遇到麻烦。

We've found that short daily meetings are invaluable for giving everyone an idea of what other people are doing. However the emphasis is on short. If the daily meetings ever start dragging, you'll run into trouble.

站立会议的名字来源于我们用来保持简短的技巧之一：每个人都必须在整个会议期间站起来。这提醒大家要简短。如果他们不记得了，再次提醒他们（必要时用棍子）。

The stand-up meeting gets its name from one of the tricks we use to keep it short: Everyone has to stand up for the whole meeting. That reminds everyone to be brief. If they don't remember, remind them again (with a stick if necessary).

格式很简单。每个人站成一圈，你一个人一个人围着转（你是顺时针还是逆时针，由你决定）。每个人都简要说明他或她昨天做了什么以及他或她今天正在做什么。传递对团队重要的问题或公告。

The format is simple. Everyone stands in a circle and you go round person by person (whether you go with or against the clock is up to you). Each person briefly says what he or she did yesterday and what he or she is doing today. Problems or announcements that are important to the team are passed on.

站会的目的是交流问题，而不是解决问题。保持会议简短。通常的绊脚石是当有人说，“我实现了一些代码来让 foobar 飞起来，”其他人说，“我上个月做了类似的事情，”“哦，我需要一个三轴，”“你可以做到通过修改配置文件。” 突然间，它正在成为一场漫长的谈话。这时你建议，“也许你们今天早上应该聚在一起谈谈这个。” 除了简短的公告之外，任何需要做的事情都应该转移到只有感兴趣的人才能参加的另一场会议上。

The purpose of the stand-up is to communicate problems, not to solve them. Keep the meeting brief. The usual stumbling block is when somebody says, "I implemented some code to the floop the foobar," someone else says, "I did something like that last month," "Oh, I needed a triple axel," "You can do that by modifying the config file." Suddenly it's on the way to being a long conversation. At this point you suggest, "Maybe you should get together this morning and talk about this." Anything that requires anything more than a brief announcement should be shunted off to another session where only those who are interested need to attend.

每天召开站立会议，这样每个人都大致了解每个人在做什么。每天选择相同的时间，并瞄准每个人都在的时间。当天早些时候更好，因为这样可以让人们有时间在需要时快速聚在一起。

Have the stand-up meeting daily, so everyone knows roughly what everyone's doing. Pick the same time every day, and aim at a time when everyone is there. Earlier in the day is better, as that allows time for people to get together quickly if they need to.

第 21 章可见图

Chapter 21. Visible Graphs

任何人都应该能够通过查看团队工作区中的一些图表来了解项目的状态。

Anyone should be able to sense the state of the project by looking at a handful of graphs in the team's working area.

我们是科学方法的忠实拥护者。像“我认为你做得太慢了”或“这个软件漏洞百出”这样的情绪爆发对你试图引导一个软件项目没有帮助。我们多快？该软件与哪种瑞士奶酪最相似？

We are big fans of the scientific method. Emotional outbursts like, "I think you are going too slow," or, "This software is riddled with bugs," don't help when you're trying to steer a software project. How fast are we going? What variety of Swiss cheese does the software most closely resemble?

戴明说，“你无法管理你无法衡量的东西。” 我们确信这不是真的，因为很多软件在交付时都没有收集任何指标。但是，如果您选择在没有指标的情况下进行管理，那么您就会陷入难以维持的情绪超然状态，尤其是在压力下。这些数字可以帮助您直面恐惧。一旦你承认了你的恐惧，你就可以使用明智的直觉来做出决定。

Deming says, "You can't manage what you can't measure." We're sure this isn't true, because lots of software gets shipped without any metrics being gathered. However, if you choose to manage without metrics, you are committing yourself to a degree of emotional detachment that is difficult to maintain, especially under pressure. The numbers help you look your fears in the face. Once you've acknowledged your fear you can use informed intuition to make your decision.

“科学”规划方法的危险在于，测量可能成为目的而不是手段。数据收集的开销会淹没实际工作。这个过程可能会变得不人道，因为人们——脏兮兮的、有异味的、容易分心的、有灵感的、不可预测的人——很容易被抽象成一组数字。

The danger with a "scientific" approach to planning is that the measurements can become the end instead of the means. The overhead of data collection can swamp real work. The process can become inhumane, with peoplemessy, smelly, distractable, inspired, unpredictable peopleconveniently abstracted away to a set of numbers.

那不是我们正在谈论的。不要那样做。

That's not what we are talking about. Don't do that.

相反，这是一个结合了直觉和测量的过程：

Instead, here is a process that combines intuition and measurement:

  1. 闻起来有问题。

  2. Smell a problem.

  3. 设计一个测量。

  4. Devise a measurement.

  5. 显示测量值。

  6. Display the measurement.

  7. 如果问题没有消失，返回到 2。

  8. If the problem doesn't go away, return to 2.

例子

Examples

下面是一个已经运行了十次迭代的真实 XP 项目的一些示例。该团队设计了一种巧妙的低成本数据收集技术。首先，团队足够小（五个程序员），团队成员不需要区分故事和任务。他们的故事很小，在四到二十小时之间。每张故事卡的背面都有一张小桌子：

Here are some examples from a real XP project that has been operating for ten iterations. The team devised an ingenious low-cost data-gathering technique. First, the team is small enough (five programmers) that team members don't need to distinguish between stories and tasks. Their stories are small, between four and twenty hours. On the back of each story card is a little table:

一对 日期 小时
____ ____ ________ ______
____ ____ ________ ______
____ ____ ________ ______
____ ____ ________ ______
____ ____ ________ ______

在每次迭代结束时，有人将卡片背面的所有值输入到电子表格中。原始数据可以以多种不同的形式呈现。

At the end of every iteration, someone types in all the values on the backs of the cards onto a spreadsheet. The raw data can then be presented in many different forms.

生产率

Productivity

团队成员开始觉得他们的进度比他们应该的慢。与其做一些明显无效的事情，比如延长工作时间，他们决定进行衡量。他们选择的衡量标准是花在编程上的办公时间百分比。

Team members began to get the feeling that they were going slower than they should. Rather than do something obviously ineffective like work longer hours, they decided to measure. The measure they chose was the percentage of office hours spent on programming.

从图 21.1中可以明显看出，该团队并没有花很多时间进行编程。难怪它进展缓慢。一点点的反思表明，时间减少了大约团队的时间

It's obvious from Figure 21.1 that the team just wasn't spending many hours programming. No wonder it was going slowly. A little reflection showed that the hours dropped about the time the team

图 21.1。测量开销

  • 拆分以启动第二个项目，并且

  • Split to start a second project, and

  • 获得外部客户

  • Acquired external customers

难怪团队没有那么多时间进行编程。在尽力增加编程时间后，团队成员修改了他们的发布计划以反映他们新测量的速度。

No wonder the team didn't have as much time for programming. After doing what they could to increase programming time, team members modified their release plan to reflect their new measured velocity.

集成地狱（好吧，无论如何“见鬼”）

Integration Hell (Well, "Heck" Anyway)

开始闻到的另一个问题是集成花费的时间太长，并且是太多错误的根源。该团队开始跟踪他们在集成之前一起编程的时间（见图21.2）。

Another problem that began to smell was that integrations were taking too long and were the source of too many errors. The team started tracking how long they were programming together before integrating (see Figure 21.2).

图 21.2。较长的会话会降低集成速度

编程时间越来越长的趋势很明显。结果是人们在最终整合时精疲力尽，增加了出错的可能性。此外，整合之前的延迟增加了与其他对的变化发生冲突的可能性。一旦测量到位（6 月 14 日），配对会话的平均持续时间下降到两个小时，集成变得更容易。

The trend toward longer and longer programming sessions was obvious. The consequence was that people were exhausted when they finally integrated, increasing the probability of errors. Also, the delay before integrating increased the probability of conflicts with the changes from other pairs. Once the measurement was in place (on June 14), the average duration of a pairing session dropped to two hours and integration got easier.

这个例子说明了衡量管理的一个重要原则：间接。该团队本可以单独开始跟踪每个集成花费的时间并尝试优化集成。通过找到难以集成的根本原因，团队成员能够治本，而不仅仅是治标。

This example illustrates an important principle of management by measurement: indirection. The team could have separately started tracking how long each integration took and tried to optimize integration. By finding the root cause of difficult integrations, team members were able to treat the cause, not just the symptoms.

选择要显示的图表

Choosing Which Graphs to Show

以下是您可能想要使用的一些图表。仔细选择图表。考虑一下您、您的管理层、您的程序员和客户关心的事情。对于每一个担忧，试着想出一个简单的图表来展示在场的每个人正在发生的事情。

Here are some graphs you may want to use. Choose your graphs carefully. Consider what things you, your management, your programmers, and the customers are concerned about. For each worry try to think of a simple graph that'll demonstrate what's happening to everyone present.

当图表完成其工作后，将其删除。图表是一种强大的工具，但过多会削弱其用途。每个人都应该知道图表很重要，绘制图表的繁琐工作应该由对您获得的有用信息的温暖感觉来补偿。

When a graph has done its job, drop it. Graphs are a powerful tool, but too many of them blunts their purpose. Everyone should know that the graphs count, and the chore of plotting them should be compensated by the warm feelings about the useful information you are gaining.

许多人建议将这些图表放在网站上。如果远程站点上的人需要查看正在发生的事情，这很好。但是不要让它代替将它们放在开发人员区域的墙上。网站如果不被点击就不会被浏览。你无法避免浴室墙上的东西。当您正在做其他事情的一半时，当您无所事事地盯着图表看时，许多见解就会出现。

Many people suggest putting these graphs on a Web site. This is good if people on remote sites need to see what's happening. But don't let that be a substitute for putting them on the wall in the developers' area. Web sites don't get looked at if they aren't clicked on. You can't avoid what's on the bathroom wall. Many an insight comes when idly staring at a graph when you're half doing something else.

以下是我们很高兴使用的一些图表：

Here are a handful of graphs we've been glad we used:

  • 定义并通过验收测试

  • Acceptance Tests Defined and Passing

  • 生产代码批量与测试代码批量

  • Production Code Bulkv versus Test Code Bulk

  • 集成

  • Integrations

  • 错误密度

  • Bug Density

  • 故事进展

  • Story Progress

  • 系统性能

  • System Performance

最重要的是要记住选择您需要的图表并停止生成您不需要的图表。虽然如果您选择我们建议的图表我们会感到受宠若惊，但更重要的是您要考虑您的担忧并选择能够说明您的担忧的图表。只是想弄清楚图表应该是什么可能会帮助您思考问题。毕竟，我们已经受够了奉承。

The most important thing to remember is to select the graphs you need and stop producing graphs you don't. Although we'll be flattered if you pick the graphs we suggest, it's far more important that you think about your worries and choose graphs that illustrate your worries. Just trying to figure out what the graphs should be will probably do a lot to help you think through your issues. After all, we already get enough flattery.

第 22 章处理错误

Chapter 22. Dealing with Bugs

这是针对物种，男孩和女孩的。

——星河战队

This is for the species, boys and girls.

Starship Troopers

安排带有故事的错误修复，以便客户可以在修复错误和添加更多功能之间进行选择。

Schedule bug fixes with stories so the customer can choose between fixing bugs and adding further functionality.

我们从未尝试过耕种，尽管肯特现在住在农场、皮卡车和真正戴牛仔帽的人中间。我们认为我们与农民的共同点是对虫子的厌恶。编程错误可能不会吞噬我们的源代码，但它们确实会吞噬我们的客户关系和生产力。而且我们不能在最近的供应商店买到软件杀虫剂。

We've never tried farming, even though Kent now lives in the middle of farms, pick-up trucks, and people who wear cowboy hats for real. One thing we imagine we have in common with farmers is a distaste for bugs. Programming bugs may not eat our source code, but they do eat at our customer relationships and productivity. And we can't get software insecticide at the nearest supply shop.

为什么我们还要谈论错误？XP 的测试实践不会导致无缺陷的系统吗？不会。缺陷应该少得多，但还是会有一些。甚至可能有足够的需要管理。

Why are we even talking about bugs? Don't XP's testing practices lead to defect-free systems? No. There should be far fewer defects, but there will still be some. There may even be enough to need managing.

软件错误最糟糕的事情之一是它们伴随着强烈的责备（来自客户）和内疚（来自程序员）。如果我们测试得更多，如果你是称职的程序员，就不会有这些错误。我们看到人们在新闻组中大喊大叫，经理们敲桌子说没有错误是可以接受的。所有这些情绪确实搞砸了处理错误的过程，并伤害了关键的人际关系，而这对于软件开发的良好运行至关重要。

One of the worst things about software bugs is that they come with a strong element of blame (from the customer) and guilt (from the programmer). If only we'd tested more, if only you were competent programmers, there wouldn't be these bugs. We've seen people screaming on news groups and managers banging on tables saying that no bugs are acceptable. All this emotion really screws up the process of dealing with bugs and hurts the key human relationships that are essential if software development is to work well.

因此，让我们制定一些基本规则。

So let's get a few ground rules on the table.

我们假设程序员正在努力做他们能做的最专业的工作。作为其中的一部分，他们将竭尽全力消除错误。但没有人可以消除所有这些。客户必须相信程序员正在努力减少错误，并且可以监控测试过程以查看他们是否做了他们应该做的事情。

We assume that the programmers are trying to do the most professional job they can. As part of this they will go to great lengths to eliminate bugs. But nobody can eliminate all of them. The customer has to trust that the programmers are working hard to reduce bugs, and can monitor the testing process to see that they are doing as much as they should.

但是，对于大多数软件，我们实际上并不希望出现零错误。（现在有一个声明，我们保证会被断章取义地用来对付我们。）任何缺陷，一旦存在，就需要花费时间和精力来消除。那些时间和精力将减少花在功能上的精力。所以你必须决定要做什么。即使您知道一个错误，也必须有人来决定您是要消除错误还是添加其他功能。谁来决定？在我们看来，它必须是客户。客户必须根据拥有错误的成本与拥有另一个功能的价值——或者现在部署的价值而不是等待减少错误数量来做出业务决策。

For most software, however, we don't actually want zero bugs. (Now there's a statement that we guarantee will be used against us out of context.) Any defect, once it's in there, takes time and effort to remove. That time and effort will take away from effort spent putting in features. So you have to decide which to do. Even when you know about a bug, someone has to decide whether you want to eliminate the bug or add another feature. Who decides? In our view it must be the customer. The customer has to make a business decision based on the cost of having the bug versus the value of having another featureor the value of deploying now instead of waiting to reduce the bug count.

（我们认为这不适用于可能危及生命的错误。在那种情况下，我们认为程序员对公共安全的责任远大于他们对客户的责任。）

(We would argue that this does not hold true for bugs that could be life-threatening. In that case we think the programmers have a duty to public safety that is far greater than their duty to the customer.)

在很多情况下，业务决策是改用该功能。也许有些读者会想到他们经常使用的软件产品，他们认为它的错误多于应有的错误。该公司做出了添加功能而不是修复错误的业务决策。查看他们过去几年的股价，以确定这是否是一个不错的选择。

There are plenty of cases where the business decision is to have the feature instead. Perhaps some readers can think of a software product they use regularly that they think has more bugs than it should. The company made a business decision to add features rather than fix bugs. Look at their share price over the last few years to determine if that was a good choice.

我们曾经遇到过一个尖锐的例子。我们参与了一个替换现有系统的项目。客户决定延迟部署，因为尽管团队尽了最大努力，错误仍然存​​在。后来发现，在一个月的时间里，现有系统由于存在缺陷，给公司造成了数百万美元的损失。新的 bug 并没有那么贵。客户是否有权延迟部署？事后看来，我们认为不是，尽管我们当时同意这个决定。

We once ran into a sharp example of this. We were involved in a project to replace an existing system. The customer decided to delay deployment because of bugs that, despite the team's best efforts, were still there. It then transpired that during one month the existing system, due to its bugs, lost the company several million dollars. The new bugs weren't anywhere near that expensive. Was the customer right to delay deployment? In hindsight we think not, although we agreed with the decision at the time.

处理生产缺陷

Dealing with Production Defects

最重要的是去除情绪。错误报告是对已部署系统的更改请求。其中许多更改可被视为增强功能而不是缺陷修复程序。我们不鼓励您尝试以一种或另一种方式对它们进行分类，因为这样做通常会导致无益的相互指责。

The most important thing is to remove the emotion. A bug report is a request for a change to the deployed system. Many of these changes could be considered to be enhancements rather than defect fixes. We don't encourage you to try to classify them one way or the other, because doing so usually leads to unhelpful finger pointing.

首先确定错误是否严重。要做到这一点并处理它，请参阅下面的处理严重错误。

First determine if the bug is critical. To do this and to deal with it see Dealing with Critical Bugs below.

如果不重要，则将其记录在卡上。让开发人员查看它并估计消除它所涉及的工作量。很多时候你不知道这个阶段涉及什么，所以将其标记为未知。如果它小于理想的一天，则将其标记为小。

If it's not critical, then log it on a card. Get development to look at it and estimate the effort involved to eliminate it. A lot of the time you don't know what's involved at this stage so mark it as unknown. If it's less than an ideal day mark it as small.

如果估计值超过一天的工作量，则将缺陷视为一个故事。然后客户可以说出哪个迭代应该解决缺陷，就像任何其他故事一样。通常，将几个错误集中在一起以获得一周的价值是值得的。

If the estimate is more than a day's worth of effort, treat the defect as a story. The customer can then say which iteration should address the defect, just as with any other story. Usually it's worth lumping several bugs together to get a week's worth.

就在下一次迭代计划会议之前，客户应该解决小的和未知的错误并确定它们的优先级。客户应该指出开发人员应该花多少时间来处理他们。“Squash little bugs”成为迭代计划练习中的一个故事。

Just before the next iteration planning meeting the customer should take the small and unknown bugs and prioritize them. The customer should indicate how much ideal time the developers should spend dealing with them. "Squash little bugs" becomes a story that goes into the iteration planning exercise.

我们希望鼓励每个人以理性的方式处理错误，在修复缺陷和添加功能之间做出明智的权衡。这里没有两个项目具有相同的优先级。如果修复错误是绝对必要的，那么你首先使用这个过程来完成它们。

We want to encourage everyone to deal with bugs in a rational way, to make sensible tradeoffs between fixing defects and adding features. No two projects have the same priorities here. If fixing bugs in an absolute must, then you do them first using this process.

此时我们必须宣布健康警告。我们还没有设法在行动中尝试这个纯粹的过程。相反，我们看到人们使用生产支持团队。

At this point we have to declare a health warning. We haven't managed to try this pure a process in action. Instead we've seen people use a production support team.

生产支持团队

Production Support Team

两到四个程序员自愿专注于修复错误。每个程序员都在生产支持上花费了几次迭代，然后轮流回到开发。在每次迭代中，至少有一个开发人员在进行他的第一次迭代支持，并且至少有一个开发人员在进行第二次迭代。总有人负责生产支持，这项（有时令人不愉快的）工作在团队中轮换。

Two or four programmers volunteer to focus on fixing bugs. Each programmer spends a couple of iterations in production support, then rotates back to development. In every iteration there is at least one developer doing his first iteration of support and at least one doing her second. Someone always has the responsibility for production support, and this (occasionally unpleasant) work is rotated around the team.

这工作得相当好。但是客户并不完全理解他为了获得生产支持而做出的牺牲。生产支持成为开销，独立于其他开发安排的单独工作。因此，客户不必被迫进行他必须在其他地方进行的明确权衡。

This has worked fairly well. But the customer didn't fully appreciate what he was trading off to get production support. Production support became overhead, a separate lump of effort that was scheduled independently of the rest of development. As such the customer wasn't forced to go through the explicit tradeoffs that he had to undergo elsewhere.

处理严重错误

Dealing with Critical Bugs

有一些bug不能等到下一次迭代。他们现在确实必须修复，或者至少在本周。困难在于确定哪些东西确实是关键错误。只有客户可以拨打此电话。如果可以，请消除情绪并遵循与标准过程类似的过程：程序员估计修复需要多长时间，客户设置优先级。程序员可能不知道修复需要多长时间，在这种情况下他们最好进行调查。然后客户选择当前计划中的哪个故事受到打击。这样，客户明确地在功能（或什至其他错误修复）与修复此错误之间进行权衡。（人们总是含蓄地做出这种权衡。我们更喜欢明确的事情。）

There are some bugs that can't wait until the next iteration. They really do have to be fixed now, or at least this week. The difficulty is identifying which things really are critical bugs. Only the customer can make this call. Remove the emotion if you can and follow a similar process to the standard one: Programmers estimate how long it will take to fix, customer sets priorities. Programmers may well have no idea how long the fix will take, in which case they'd better investigate. Then the customer picks which story on the current plan takes the hit. That way the customer is explicitly making a tradeoff of function (or even other bug fixes) versus fixing this bug. (People make this tradeoff implicitly all the time. We prefer things to be explicit.)

第 23 章 团队的变化

Chapter 23. Changes to the Team

当团队发生变化时，这对您的计划有何影响？

When the team changes, how does that affect your planning?

未来

Coming

给新的团队成员一两次迭代来适应环境。他们能

Give new team members an iteration or two to get acclimated. They can

  • 与更有经验的人结对

  • Pair with more experienced folks

  • 阅读代码和测试用例

  • Read code and test cases

  • 与客户交谈

  • Talk to customers

在这次培训期间，我们没有发现需要预测团队速度的降低。花在回答新手问题上的时间可以用他们对旧问题带来的新视角来弥补。

During this orientation, we haven't found the need to predict a reduction in the team's velocity. Time spent answering newbie questions is made up for in the new perspective they bring to old problems.

昨天的天气会告诉您何时根据新人的存在来增加您的估计。Kent 的一个项目在一个八人团队中增加了两个新人，并且出现了灾难性的迭代，这主要是因为延迟重构赶上了他们。团队宣布“迭代失败”并计划下一次迭代，就好像迭代失败没有发生过一样。下一次迭代他们致力于 22 天的故事并完成了 37 个。是重构还是新人？很难说，但该团队正处于一个新的、更高的轨道上，此后一直保持下去。

Yesterday's Weather will tell you when to increase your estimates based on the presence of new people. A project of Kent's added two new people to a team of eight and had a disastrous iteration, mostly because of deferred refactorings that caught up with them. The team declared that the "Lost Iteration" and planned for the next iteration as if the Lost Iteration hadn't happened. The next iteration they committed to 22 days of stories and completed 37. Was it the refactorings or the new folks? Impossible to tell, but the team was on a new, higher trajectory that has since been sustained.

去

Going

如果你有五个程序员，一个离开了，那么将你的下一次迭代减少 20%。昨天的天气将足够快地确定新的速度。

If you have five programmers and one leaves, reduce your next iteration by 20 percent. Yesterday's Weather will fix the new velocity quickly enough.

拆分团队

Splitting the Team

Ward Cunningham 推测将 XP 扩展到 30 到 40 名程序员的方法是用十人团队完成第一个版本，然后分成两个团队。每个团队都从自己的客户那里获得自己的故事流。五人小组随后增加到十人。这样做两次，你就 40 岁了。

Ward Cunningham speculates that the way to scale XP up to 30 to 40 programmers is to complete the first release with a team of ten, then split into two teams. Each team gets its own stream of stories from its own customer. The teams of five then grow to ten. Do this twice and you're at 40.

出于计划目的，如果我们要这样做，我们将开始让每个子团队完成整个团队在拆分前完成的一半的工作。Yesterday's Weather 会很快告诉您需要计划多少跨团队开销。

For planning purposes, if we were to do this, we would begin committing each subteam to half of what the whole team accomplished before the split. Yesterday's Weather will quickly tell you how much cross-team overhead to plan for.

人们成长

People Growing

人们每天都不一样。测试人员变成程序员，程序员变成管理者，管理者摆脱压迫的枷锁，重新成为程序员（哎呀，我们的偏见暴露了）。

People are different day to day. Testers become programmers, programmers become managers, managers throw off the shackles of oppression and become programmers again (oops, our bias is showing).

XP 不是由插件兼容编程单元执行的。它由人执行，改变人。如果有人厌倦了一直编程怎么办？团队如何优雅地适应生活方式的变化？

XP isn't executed by Plug Compatible Programming Units. It is executed by people, changing people. What if someone got bored with programming all the time? How could the team gracefully adapt to changes in lifestyle?

这只是一个想法，但如果您在迭代计划期间将管理任务与技术任务一起放在白板上会怎么样？项目经理通常会注册跟踪、状态报告和披萨选择。不过，如果其他人想尝尝项目管理的滋味，他可以时不时地报名参加。如果项目经理需要离开，有人可以轻松介入，即使只是暂时的。项目经理还可以时不时地执行一项编程任务，从底层查看事情的情况。

This is just an idea, but what if you put the management tasks on the board alongside the technical tasks during iteration planning? The project manager would typically sign up for tracking, the status report, and pizza selection. However, if someone else wanted to get a taste of project management, he could sign up for one from time to time. If the project manager needed to move on, someone could easily step in, even if only temporarily. The project manager could also take a programming task from time to time to see how things looked from ground level.

第 24 章工具

Chapter 24. Tools

（法国元帅）计划他们的战役，就像你制作一套漂亮的挽具一样。它看起来很好，回答也很好，直到它坏了；然后你就完成了。现在，我进行了绳索运动。如果出了什么问题，我就打个结；然后继续。

——威灵顿公爵

(The French Marshals) planned their campaigns just as you might make a splendid set of harness. It looks very well, and answers very well, until it gets broken; and then you are done for. Now, I made my campaigns of ropes. If anything went wrong, I tied a knot; and went on.

The Duke of Wellington

  • 坚持使用简单的工具，例如铅笔、纸和白板。沟通对于成功比神出鬼没更重要。

  • Stick with simple tools, like pencil, paper, and whiteboard. Communication is more important to success than whizbang.

项目管理中有两个问题需要解决：

There are two problems to solve in project management:

  • 跟踪所有数据

  • Keeping track of all data

  • 维持人与人之间的沟通和关系

  • Maintaining communication and relationships between people

我们的项目管理工具策略严重偏向于维护人际沟通和人与人之间的关系。对于中小型项目，让每个人都坦诚相待是一个比计算意外的进度影响更难解决的问题，因此需要更强大的工具。获胜者是：小纸片。

Our tool strategy for project management is biased heavily towards maintaining human communication and the relationships between people. For small to medium-sized projects, keeping everybody talking honestly is a much more difficult problem to solve than calculating the schedule impact of surprises, so it deserves stronger tools. And the winner is: little pieces of paper.

XP 项目进度信息的主要物理单位是索引卡。索引卡是

The primary physical unit of schedule information on XP projects is the index card. Index cards are

  • 便携的

  • Portable

  • 独立于机器

  • Machine independent

  • 平易近人

  • Approachable

  • 便宜（很抱歉这个 - 如果你愿意，你可以寄给我们一大笔钱，我们会让 Bob Martin 寄给你非常好的索引卡）

  • Cheap (sorry about this oneyou can send us a bunch of money if you'd like, and we'll get Bob Martin to send you really nice index cards)

记住我们在规划中的目的：

Remember our purposes in planning:

  • 决定是否继续

  • Decide whether to go ahead

  • 协调团队内部和外部世界

  • Coordinate within the team and with the outside world

  • 衡量意外的影响

  • Gauge the impact of surprises

  • 设定优先级

  • Set priorities

这些都不是计算上令人印象深刻的任务。我们可以在脑子里算算，然后把答案写在卡片上。电子表格可以轻松处理更复杂的计算。从这个电子表格中，您还可以生成各种很酷、令人印象深刻的报告和图表，其中一些甚至很有用。

None of these are computationally impressive tasks. We can do the arithmetic in our heads and write the answers down on the cards. More complicated calculations can easily be handled by a spreadsheet. From this spreadsheet you can also generate all kinds of cool and impressive reports and graphs, some of which are even useful.

如果你必须使用电子表格，永远不要忘记电子表格不如沟通和关系重要。“我为这次迭代发现了更多任务，但我不想编辑所有这些报告。” 暂停！尾巴摇着狗。确保每个人都了解本次迭代所需的所有任务远比立即正确生成报告重要得多。如有必要，放弃电子表格。如果每个人都明白，但电子表格已经无可救药地过时了，那比拥有错误信息的完美记录要好得多。

If you must use a spreadsheet, never forget that the spreadsheet is not as important as communication and relationships. "I discovered a couple more tasks for this iteration, but I don't want to edit all those reports." Time out! The tail is wagging the dog. Making sure everyone understands all the tasks required for this iteration is far more important than getting the reports exactly right this instant. If necessary, abandon the spreadsheet. If everyone understands but the spreadsheet is hopelessly out of date, that is much better than having a perfect record of incorrect information.

第 25 章商业合同

Chapter 25. Business Contracts

如果您打算使用 XP 计划和执行项目，传统的业务关系需要稍微调整一下。

Traditional business relationships require a little tweaking if you're going to plan and execute a project with XP.

我们知道我们承诺只谈项目规划，但世界上最好的软件开发流程在错误的合同面前束手无策。下面我们简单谈谈三种典型的软件业务，以及XP规划如何改变它们：

We know we promised to only talk about project planning, but the very best software development process in the world is helpless in the face of the wrong contract. Here we will talk briefly about three typical software businesses and how XP planning changes them:

  • 外包

  • Outsourcing

  • 内部开发

  • In-house development

  • 收缩包装

  • Shrink-wrap

任何使供应商利益与客户利益相抵触的合同都是麻烦。如果随着压力的增加，反对的声音越来越大，那麻烦就几乎无法克服了。

Any contract that pits the interests of the supplier against the interests of the customer is trouble. If the opposition becomes worse as pressure increases, the trouble is well nigh insurmountable.

外包

Outsourcing

典型的外包合同固定了四个变量中的三个：[1]

The typical outsourcing contract fixes three of the four variables:[1]

[1] 感谢 Dave Cleal 对可协商范围合同的许多改进。

[1] Thanks to Dave Cleal for many of the refinements on negotiable scope contracts.

  • 范围

  • Scope

  • 时间

  • Time

  • 成本

  • Cost

不幸的是，不可能修复所有四个变量。如果出乎意料，其中一个变量会发生变化（因此得名“变量”）。由于质量是最难衡量的变量，惊喜往往会被降低质量所吸收——少一点测试，少一点设计，少一点沟通。任何通过增加风险来挽救计划的尝试都注定要失败。一旦潜伏着未知数量的工作，范围、时间和成本都会爆炸式增长。

Unfortunately, it is impossible to fix all four variables. If there is a surprise, one of the variables will change (hence the name "variable"). Since quality is the hardest variable to measure, surprises tend to get absorbed by reducing qualitya little less testing, a little less design, a little less communication. Any attempt to rescue a plan by adding risk is doomed. Once you have an unknown amount of work lurking, scope, time, and cost will all explode.

固定范围合同的根本问题在于它们使供应商和客户的利益直接相互对抗。客户希望尽可能多地花钱，但供应商希望为钱做尽可能少的工作。只要一切都按计划进行，这种对立并不一定是致命的。当意外开始累积时，合同就失效了。

The fundamental problem with fixed-scope contracts is that they pit the interests of supplier and customer directly against each other. Customers want as much scope as possible for their money, but suppliers want to do as little work as possible for the money. As long as everything is going according to plan, this opposition isn't necessarily fatal. When the surprises start adding up, the contract goes sour.

相反，合同可以这样写：“供应商将以 320,000 美元的价格让八名程序员为客户工作两个月。范围将根据经典书籍规划极限编程每两周协商一次。 ” 就是这样。写起来简单，读起来也简单（而且它促进了我们的图书销量）。

Instead, the contract could read, "Supplier will have eight programmers work for Customer for two months for $320,000. Scope will be negotiated every two weeks according to the classic book Planning Extreme Programming." That's it. Simple to write, simple to read (and it boosts our book sales).

可是等等。顾客想知道她的 300 盛大会得到什么。当然，她想知道，但她不能知道。规划不是预测未来。我们可以给她大计划。她每两周就能看到我们的进步。毕竟才两个月，项目很可能要持续六到八个月。你不太可能会把四分之三的钱都留在桌子上。

But wait. The customer wants to know what she is going to get for her three hundred grand. Sure, she wants to know, but she can't know. Planning is not about predicting the future. We can give her the Big Plan. She can see our progress every two weeks. After all, it's only two months, and the project is likely to last for six to eight months. It's not likely you will send in scrubs and leave three-fourths of the money on the table.

可是等等。供应商想知道他未来六个月的就业要求是什么。那么，尽可能让客户满意。

But wait. The supplier wants to know what his employment requirements are for the next six months. Well, then, keep the customer as happy as you can.

内部开发

In-House Development

内部开发对于 XP 有其自身的优点和缺点。优点是

In-house development has its own sets of advantages and disadvantages for XP. The advantages are

  • 你没有明确的合同，所以你不必担心如果失败会被起诉——你可能会被解雇，但不会被起诉。好吧，所以这不是一个很大的优势。

  • You don't have an explicit contract, so you don't have to worry about being sued if you failyou may be fired, perhaps, but not sued. Okay, so this isn't such a big advantage.

  • 你们在同一种文化中工作。商业和发展可能会共享一些价值观和神话（即使在某些故事中好人和坏人的角色颠倒了）。

  • You are working inside the same culture. Business and development are likely to share some values and myths (even if the roles of Good Guys and Bad Guys are reversed in some of the stories).

  • 你在“大老板”中有一个内置的仲裁员。当然，您宁愿在分歧升级到这种程度之前解决你们的分歧，但至少有一个明确的地方可以让责任停止。

  • You have a built-in arbitrator in "the big boss." Of course, you'd rather resolve your disagreements before they escalate that far, but at least there is a clear place where the buck stops.

缺点是

The disadvantages are

  • 业务和开发已经有历史了，而且很可能有点紧张（如果业务和开发顺畅地相处，你不需要 XP，XP 需要你）。

  • Business and development already have a history, and it is likely to be, well, a bit strained (if business and development get along swimmingly, you don't need XP, XP needs you).

  • 您可能有多个客户要服务，而不仅仅是一个。解决相互冲突的优先事项会占用你所有的精力。

  • You likely have several customers to serve, not just one. Resolving conflicting priorities can take up all your energy.

内部项目的最大问题是寻找客户。肯特见过的最好的客户是在一个客户服务系统项目上。客户在使用旧系统的同时打开信封和接听电话已经花费了七年时间。然后她花了三年时间监督其他代表。这使她对现有系统有了完整的了解，并了解系统的薄弱环节、可能出错的地方以及需要重复信息的地方。她在做决定时也无所畏惧，但在做出决定后会认真核实。

The biggest problem with in-house projects is finding the customer. The best customer Kent ever saw was on a customer service system project. The customer had spent seven years opening envelopes and answering phones while using the legacy system. Then she spent three years supervising other representatives. This left her with complete knowledge of the existing system and an understanding of where the system was weak, where mistakes were likely to be made, where duplicate information was required. She was also fearless in making decisions but conscientious about verifying them after she made them.

如果您能找到一个可以自信地为业务代言的人，那是最好的。这个人需要

It's best if you can find a single person who can confidently speak for business. This person needs

  • 经验

  • Experience

  • 联系人

  • Contacts

  • 想象

  • Vision

  • 勇气

  • Courage

如果你找不到一个人充当客户，你就必须有一个客户委员会。让这个委员会明确。坚持让他们聚在一起讨论您的优先事项。我们看到一个团队在一年内从企业英雄变成了山羊，因为两个客户的优先事项大相径庭。他们从来没有明确表示过他们的分歧，也没有采取任何措施来解决这些分歧。

If you can't find a single person to act as customer, you will have to have a committee of customers. Make this committee explicit. Insist that they get together to discuss your priorities. We watched a team go from corporate heroes to goats in one year because two customers had widely differing priorities. They were never explicit about their differences, and they did nothing to resolve them.

如果客户无法协作决定发布和迭代的故事，请尝试 Dave Cleal 的想法：给每个客户一个预算。假设您已经测量出您的团队每次迭代都可以制作八个理想周的故事。给交易大厅三个星期的时间，给后台办公室三个星期的时间。两位客户都必须出席每次发布计划会议和每次迭代计划会议，并且都必须在整个开发过程中回答问题。

If the customers can't collaborate to decide on stories for releases and iterations, try an idea from Dave Cleal: Give each customer a budget. Let's say you've measured that your team can produce eight ideal weeks' worth of stories every iteration. Give the trading floor three weeks to spend and give the back office three weeks. Both customers will have to be present at every release planning meeting and each iteration planning meeting, and both will have to be available for answering questions throughout development.

收缩包装

Shrink-Wrap

当你没有一个客户，你有数百、数千、数百万、数十亿和数万亿客户时，你如何计划？XP 要求客户用一种声音说话。

How do you plan when you don't have one customer, you have hundreds, thousands, millions and billions and trillions of customers? XP requires the customer to speak with one voice.

这个角色在大多数地方被称为“产品经理”。产品经理听取了许多来源：

This role is called "product manager" in most places. The product manager listens to many sources:

  • 销售量

  • Sales

  • 营销

  • Marketing

  • 客户支持

  • Customer support

  • 顾客

  • Customers

产品经理合并故事，从开发中获得估计，设置相对的任务优先级，并通过迭代和发布计划与开发对话。关键是解决冲突的责任从发展中转移了。如果你只能立即满足三个客户中的两个，产品经理决定现在抚摸哪两个，暂时不高兴哪一个。

The product manager merges the stories, gets estimates from development, sets relative task priorities, and speaks to development through iteration and release planning. The key point is that responsibility for resolving conflicts is shifted away from development. If you can only satisfy two of three customers immediately, the product manager decides which two get stroked now and which one will be upset for a while.

Kent 有一个项目，其中有六名产品经理。一个作为整体产品经理，另外五个人各负责一部分产品。通过一些对开发完全不可见的神奇过程，他们逐次迭代计算出它们的相对优先级。当他们参加计划会议时，他们用同一种声音讲述了他们的故事。

Kent has a project where there are six product managers. One acts as the overall product manager, while the other five each have responsibility for a part of the product. Through some magic process completely invisible to development, they work out their relative priority iteration by iteration. By the time they get to the planning meeting, they present their stories with one voice.

第 26 章红旗

Chapter 26. Red Flags

以下是我们不止一次看到的一些危险情况，以及我们希望我们对它们采取的措施。

Here are some dicey situations we've seen more than once and what we wished we'd done about them.

肯特有一个滚动的手提箱，它的轮子靠得太近了。当他在飞机之间奔跑时，手提箱开始摇晃。试图更紧地握住手柄只会让它摇晃得更多。最终，愚蠢的事情就倒下了。

Kent has a rolling suitcase whose wheels are too close together. When he is running between planes, the suitcase starts wobbling. Trying to hold on tighter to the handle just makes it wobble more. Eventually the stupid thing just falls over.

解决办法当然是买一个轮子间隔适当的新手提箱。不过，这不会成为一个教学故事。肯特的解决办法是放慢速度，直到手提箱不再摇晃。不管你的飞机迟到多久，如果手提箱翻倒了，你就会迟到。

The solution, of course, is to buy a new suitcase with suitably spaced wheels. That wouldn't make much of a teaching story, though. Kent's solution is to slow down until the suitcase stops wobbling. It doesn't matter how late you are for your plane, if the suitcase falls over you'll be later.

这里有一些常见的“摇摆不定”，计划出现问题的迹象，以及如果我们看到它们应该怎么做。解决方案都是某种形式的“放慢速度，直到你受到控制，然后再加速”。

Here are some common "wobbles," signs of trouble with planning, and what we do if we see them. The solutions are all some form of "slow down until you are under control, then speed up again."

  • 缺少估计

  • Missing estimates

  • 客户不会做决定

  • Customers won't make decisions

  • 缺陷报告

  • Defect reports

  • 不会首尾相接

  • Not going end to end

  • 每日构建失败

  • Failing daily builds

  • 客户不会完成

  • Customer won't finish

遗漏估计

Missing Estimates

如果每次迭代结束时都必须丢弃一半的故事，那么肯定是有问题的。迭代可能会有一段紧张的时刻，但大多数迭代应该可以轻松完成。您可能在第二个星期二不知道是否能成功，但是当星期五午餐比萨饼送来并且您按下按钮运行验收测试时，每个人都应该对结果充满信心。

If every time you come to the end of an iteration you have to throw away half of the stories, then something is definitely wrong. Iterations can have a moment of dramatic tension, but most iterations should finish comfortably. You might not know on the second Tuesday if you're going to make it, but when the lunch pizza comes on Friday and you push the button to run the acceptance tests, everyone should be confident of the outcome.

你承诺太多了吗？Kent 有一个项目，在这个项目中，程序员的罪恶感很高，以至于他们总是被围捕。“我们在上一次迭代中用 4 个人完成了 38 天，所以称每人 10 天，我们有一个新人，所以是 50 天。” 他们在每次迭代中都错过了一点，但更重要的是，他们在测试和重构方面落后了，直到最后一次迭代完全失败。他们向客户交付了 1（一）天。这是关注昨天的天气的警钟。

Are you committing to too much? Kent had a project where the programmers' guilt level was high enough that they always rounded up. "We got 38 days done last iteration with 4 people, so call that 10 days per person and we have a new person, so that's 50." They missed a little every iteration, but, more important, they got behind on testing and refactoring until finally one iteration completely pancaked. They delivered 1 (one) day to the customer. That was the wake-up call to just follow Yesterday's Weather.

您在测试和重构方面落后了吗？如果是这样，您将看到调试花费的时间百分比越来越高，但百分比不可预测。我们找到的唯一解决方案是暂时放慢速度，编写额外的测试并进行更多重构。几次迭代后，您的速度应该会加快。

Have you gotten behind on testing and refactoring? If so, you'll see debugging take an increasing percentage of time but an unpredictable percentage. The only solution we've found is to slow down, temporarily, and write the extra tests and do a little more refactoring. After a couple of iterations your speed should pick up.

你是否屈服于削减你的估计的诱惑？当客户失望时，程序员很容易感到内疚，并且这种内疚会变成更短的估算，这不是出于任何技术原因，而是因为他们希望客户开心（或者至少停止骚扰他们）。这是行不通的。不要那样做。当程序员进行估算时，让他们找到可比较的工作并进行可比较的估算。“我们有两份新报告。它们都与我们上次迭代所做的 framdoozle 报告大致相同，那花了一周时间。给他们打电话一周。”

Have you succumbed to the temptation to slice your estimates? It is so easy for programmers to feel guilty when the customer is disappointed and for that guilt to turn into shorter estimates, not for any technical reason, but because they want the customer to be happy (or at least stop bugging them). This doesn't work. Don't do that. When programmers make estimates, have them find comparable work and make the estimates comparably. "We have two new reports. They are both about the same as the framdoozle report we did last iteration, and that took a week. Call them a week each."

客户不会做出决定

Customers Won't Make Decisions

有时客户只是拒绝做出决定。他们不会选择故事进行迭代。他们不会指定验收测试。他们不会回答有关范围的小问题。

Sometimes customers simply refuse to make decisions. They won't pick the stories for an iteration. They won't specify acceptance tests. They won't answer little questions about scope.

没有客户做出决定，极限编程就无法工作。客户不必坚持这些决定。改变主意是他们的权利之一。但决策必须由具有商业视角的人做出。

Extreme Programming cannot work without a customer making decisions. Customers don't have to stick with those decisions. Changing their mind is one of their rights. But the decisions must be made, and by someone with a business perspective.

Sam Gentile 报告了一个项目，在该项目中，客户的老板签署了一份极限开发合同。当团队到达那里并开始探索时，客户被激怒了。“我雇你做分析，不是让我做分析的。快点开始吧。而且我很忙，所以不要问我任何问题。” 幸运的是，团队当时有智慧终止合同。

Sam Gentile reports on a project where the customer's boss signed a contract for extreme development. When the team got there and started exploration the customer was incensed. "I hired you to do the analysis, not for me to do the analysis. Get to it. And I'm busy, so don't ask me any questions." Fortunately the team had the wisdom to terminate the contract at that point.

找出客户不做决定的原因。如果他的优先事项在别处，也许整个项目就没有意义。如果他不想公开犯错，你能做的最好的事情就是让他放心，他将有机会在下一次迭代中修正任何错误。

Find out why the customer won't make the decisions. If his priorities are elsewhere, perhaps the whole project doesn't make sense. If he doesn't want to be publicly wrong, the best you can do is reassure him that he will get a chance to fix any errors in the next iteration.

缺陷报告

Defect Reports

在单元测试和验收测试之间，极端团队生产的软件应该没有明显的缺陷。应该有很多增强请求，但软件应该按规定工作。

Between the unit tests and the acceptance tests, the software produced by an extreme team should be remarkably defect free. There should be enhancement requests aplenty, but the software should work as specified.

如果您看到的缺陷报告足以破坏开发，请放慢速度，直到您看不到它们为止。让一对检查每个缺陷并找到它发生的位置以及应该编写什么单元测试来捕获它，然后向团队报告。

If you are seeing enough defect reports to disrupt development, slow down until you aren't seeing them. Have a pair go through every defect and find where it occurred and what unit test should have been written to catch it, then report back to the team.

有时一类缺陷会变成设计变更。“当我们使用 Netscape 运行时，我们有六个错误。我们必须创建一个浏览器对象来隔离特定于浏览器的行为。”

Sometimes a class of defects will turn into a design change. "We have six bugs when we run with Netscape. We have to create a browser object to isolate the browser-specific behavior."

不会结束到结束

Not Going End to End

当您感到不舒服时，很容易停止开发。我们正在构建一个 Web 服务器，我们已经进行了所有这些测试，但它们始终在我们的网络中运行。出门去西雅图咖啡，在网上租个站，试试上不去服务器。如果我们不能，因为我们的代理服务器没有配置 yadda yadda yadda，然后停止，直到它被配置。你没有用手电筒探索过的每个黑暗角落都充满了虫子。

It is so tempting to stop developing when you get uncomfortable. We're building a Web server and we've got all these tests, but they always run inside our network. Go out to Seattle Coffee, rent a station on the Internet, and try to get to the server. If we can't, because our proxy server isn't configured yadda yadda yadda, then stop until it is. Every dark corner you haven't explored with your flashlight is full of bugs.

失败的构建

Failing Builds

如果你每天做的八到十个集成都很顺利，但是你在把软件推到生产的时候出现了问题，那就让集成环境和生产环境更加匹配。如果您不知道自己实际取得了多少进展，那么来自小集成的反馈将无助于您的计划。

If the eight to ten integrations you do every day are going smoothly but you have problems when you push the software to production, make the integration environment match the production environment more closely. The feedback from the little integrations won't help your planning if you don't know how much progress you've actually made.

客户不会完成

Customer Won't Finish

我们在 XP 中看到的失败之一是客户从一朵花飞到另一朵花——这里有一些故事，那里有一些故事。程序员们一路狂奔，达到了他们的估计，在重构的同时找到了极好的抽象，疯狂地测试。然后有一天，该项目被取消，因为它没有完成任何事情。

One of the failures we've seen in XP is where the customer flits from flower to flowera few stories from here, a few from there. The programmers blaze along, hitting their estimates, finding fabulous abstractions while refactoring, testing like mad. Then one day the project is cancelled because it didn't get anything done.

制定客户向高层管理人员提交的三到四个月的发布计划。这些计划的结果是否在日期临近时得到审查？大奶酪是有目的的——使用它们。大老板们善于发现季度规模的不适应，“我可以看到所有这些网络内容都令人兴奋，但如果我们不为这份美联储报告做好准备，我们就会倒闭。”

Make three- to four-month release plans that the customer presents to upper management. Are the results of those plans reviewed when the date rolls around? The big cheeses are there for a purposeuse them. Big bosses can be good at spotting misfits at a quarterly scale, "I can see that all this Web stuff is exciting, but if we don't prepare for this Federal Reserve report we're out of business."

第 27 章你自己的过程

Chapter 27. Your Own Process

没有两个 XP 项目会完全一样。一旦您对基本流程感到满意，您就会发展它以更精确地适应您的情况。

No two XP projects will ever act exactly alike. Once you get comfortable with the basic process, you will grow it to fit your situation more precisely.

我们在这里是规定性的，告诉您如何规划您的软件项目。然而，归根结底，您必须拥有自己的计划和计划。

We have been prescriptive here, telling you what to do to plan your software project. At the end of the day, however, you have to own your own plan and your own planning.

使 XP 计划适应您自己的情况的一种方法是将其中有意义的零碎部分与您现在正在做的事情结合起来。混合搭配的问题在于 XP 计划的各个部分旨在相互补充。如果项目经理估算任务然后将其分配给程序员，那么程序员将不会像他们自己分解任务并进行估算那样拥有主人翁意识。

One way to adapt XP planning to your own situation is to take the bits and pieces of it that make sense and mix them with what you are doing now. The problem with mix-and-match is that the parts of XP planning are intended to complement each other. If the project manager estimates tasks then assigns them to programmers, the programmers won't have the same sense of ownership as if they did the task breakdown and estimates themselves.

这是另一种策略。“按部就班”地采用 XP 计划。运行几次迭代。然后查看您遇到的问题并尝试每次迭代。

Here's an alternative strategy. Adopt XP planning "by the book." Run for a couple of iterations. Then look at the problems you are having and experiment with each iteration.

  • 我们没有按时完成。让我们尝试一个月的一周迭代。

  • We aren't getting done on time. Let's try one-week iterations for a month.

  • 让客户勾选任务框。

  • Let's have the customer check off the task boxes.

  • 让我们将重构目标放在板上。

  • Let's put targets for refactoring on a board.

  • 让我们开始让我们的性能图形可见。

  • Let's start making our performance graphics visible.

每次迭代花一两个小时回顾过去的实验和结果，并集思广益新的。如果您在迭代的最后一个星期五的午餐时间举行了验收测试按钮的仪式性按下，您可以在当天剩下的时间里讨论您的流程。

Spend an hour or two each iteration reviewing past experiments and results and brainstorming new ones. If you have the ceremonial pushing of the acceptance test button at lunch on the last Friday of the iteration, you can spend the rest of the day talking about your process.

我们看到 XP 被愉快地采用的商店是那些从简单开始并不断发展壮大的商店。有些变体起初看起来非常激进。但是一旦团队解释了新做法的基本原理，它们就有意义了。

The shops where we've seen XP happily adopted are those where they have started simple and grown. Some of the variations seem pretty radical at first. But once the team explains the rationale for the new practices, they make sense.

具有短迭代和大量数据的迭代过程的美妙之处在于，您可以执行更多的实验，并对结果进行更精确的测量，这比其他方式是不可能的。充分利用您的数据。玩转你的过程。

The beauty of an iterative process with short iterations and lots of data is that you can perform many more experiments, and with much more precise measurements of the results, than would otherwise be possible. Take advantage of your data. Play with your process.
